Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Iqalah Before Delivery for Movables and Immovables
Ruling on iqalah before delivery for movables and immovables.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings on iqalah before delivery for movables (manqul) and immovables (aqar) according to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and explain why Abu Yusuf treats iqalah of immovables as a sale.

Core Idea
Iqalah before delivery for movables is always rescission; for immovables, Abu Yusuf treats it as a sale because sale before delivery is valid.

The permissibility of selling property before the buyer takes physical possession differs between movables and immovables in the Hanafi school. This affects the legal nature of iqalah when the parties cancel the sale before delivery. This lesson examines the interplay between the rules of pre-delivery sales and the classification of iqalah.

Guided Path
1
Recall the rule on pre-delivery sales
Recognize that sale of movables before delivery is impermissible by consensus. Sale of immovables before delivery is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but impermissible according to Muhammad.
2
Apply to iqalah for movables
For movables, all three Imams agree that iqalah before delivery is rescission (faskh) because a sale is impossible; thus rescission is the only option.
3
Apply to iqalah for immovables
For immovables, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad still treat iqalah as rescission. However, Abu Yusuf treats it as a sale because for him, a sale of immovables before delivery is valid, so the iqalah can be a sale.
4
Understand Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Since Abu Yusuf considers iqalah as a sale in principle, and since a sale of immovables before delivery is permissible, he can treat the iqalah as a sale. For movables, he is forced to treat it as rescission because a sale would be invalid.
5
Identify the practical difference
Under Abu Yusuf's view for immovables, the iqalah is a new sale, which may trigger pre-emption rights and other sale-related provisions. Under the other Imams, it is rescission, restoring the parties to their pre-contract positions.

نہیں ہے۔ اور اشیاء غیر منقولہ جیسے زمین اور مکان کی بيع قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے شیخین کے نزدیک جائز ہے لیکن امام محمد کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے۔ اب حاصل عبارت یہ ہے کہ مبیع شی منقول ہو یا شی غیر منقول ہو اگر مشتری نے قبضہ کئے بغیر اقالہ کیا تو طرفین کے نزدیک یہ اقالہ فسخ بيع ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں کے نزدیک اصل یہی ہے کہ اقالہ، فسخ بيع ہو اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک بھی اگر بيع شی منقول ہو تو اقالہ فسخ ہی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اگرچہ اقالہ کا بيع ہونا اصل ہے مگر چونکہ مشتری نے مبیع منقول پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے ہی اقالہ کر دیا ہے اور شی منقول کی بيع ناجائز ہے اس لیے اس اقالہ کو بيع قرار دینا تو متعذر ہو گیا اور جب بيع قرار دینا متعذر ہو جائے تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس کو فسخ قرار دیا جاتا ہے اس لئے امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقالہ فسخ ہوگا اور اسی طرح اگر مبیع غیر منقول ہو اور مشتری نے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اقالہ کیا تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس اقالہ کو بيع قرار دیا جائے گا کیونکہ غیر منقول کے اقالہ کو بيع قرار دینا ممکن ہے اور غیر منقول کے اقالہ کو بيع قرار دینا اس لئے ممکن ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے غیر منقول کی بيع جائز ہے۔ (منی شرح ہدایہ)
Ruling of iqalah with a different type than the original price. 'And if he cancels (iqalah) with other than the type of the first price, then it is a rescission based on the first price according to Abu Hanifa, and the naming (of the other type) is considered void. And according to them (Sahibayn), it is a sale, as we have established. And if the sold female slave gives birth to a child, then they make iqalah, the iqalah is void according to him (Abu Hanifa) because the child prevents rescission. And according to them, it would be a sale. And iqalah before delivery, for movable property and other than it, is rescission according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and similarly according to Abu Yusuf for movables, due to the impossibility of sale. And for immovables, according to him, iqalah is a sale because sale is possible, for sale of immovables before delivery is permissible according to him.' Translation: And if iqalah is made with a different type than the first price, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is a rescission based on the first price, and the mention of the other type is considered void. And according to the Sahibayn, this iqalah is a sale due to the proof we mentioned. And if a slave-girl gives birth to a child, then both make iqalah, the iqalah is void according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) because the child prevents rescission. And according to the Sahibayn, it would be a sale. And iqalah before delivery for movables and other things is rescission according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and similarly according to Abu Yusuf for movables because sale is impossible. And for immovables, according to him, iqalah is a sale because sale is possible, for according to Abu Yusuf sale of immovables before delivery is permissible. (Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Sharh of Hidayah, Volume 8) Explanation: The case is that if iqalah is made with a different type than the first price, e.g., the first price was dirhams and iqalah is made with dinars, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this iqalah is a rescission of the sale based on the first price (dirhams), and the mention of dinars is void. That is, the seller must return the first price (dirhams), not the dinars. According to the Sahibayn, this iqalah is a sale with the other type, i.e., it will be said that the buyer sold the item, which he had bought for dirhams, back to the seller for dinars. Their proof has passed earlier: for Abu Yusuf, iqalah being sale is the principle; for Muhammad, the principle is rescission, but since rescission is impossible due to mentioning a different type, it is considered a sale because that is possible. The author of al-Hidayah said: If the slave-girl gives birth after the buyer took possession, then the parties make iqalah, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this iqalah is void. The proof is that according to him, iqalah is only rescission. After possession, an increase that is separate from the sale prevents rescission, and the child is a separate increase, so it prevents rescission. When rescission is prevented, iqalah becomes void, and the first sale remains as it was. But if the slave-girl gives birth before the buyer took possession, then according to Imam the iqalah is valid because a separate increase before possession does not prevent rescission. And if the sold item becomes fat (increases), this increase does not prevent rescission either before or after possession. The Sahibayn said that if iqalah is made after the slave-girl gives birth, this iqalah is a sale: for Abu Yusuf because iqalah being a sale is the principle; for Muhammad because when rescission is impossible due to the separate increase, iqalah is made a sale because that is possible. Before explaining the passage of the author of al-Hidayah, 'And iqalah before delivery for movables...' etc., note that sale of movables before delivery is unanimously impermissible. And sale of immovables like land and house before delivery is permissible according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) but impermissible according to Imam Muhammad. Now the meaning of the passage is: If the sold item is movable or immovable, and the buyer makes iqalah without taking possession, then according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) this iqalah is a rescission of the sale, because for them the principle is that iqalah is rescission. And according to Abu Yusuf also, if the sale is of a movable, iqalah is rescission because sale is impossible, so he treats it as rescission. And if the sold item is immovable and the buyer makes iqalah before possession, according to Abu Yusuf this iqalah is a sale because sale is possible, since according to him sale of immovables before delivery is permissible. (From Minyah al-Hidayah)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings on iqalah. First, it addresses iqalah with a different type of price (e.g., dirhams to dinars). Abu Hanifa maintains it as rescission with the original price, ignoring the new specification. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it a new sale because rescission is impossible. Second, it discusses iqalah when the sold slave-girl gives birth. Abu Hanifa voids the iqalah because the child is a separate increase that prevents rescission; the Sahibayn treat it as a sale. Third, it examines iqalah before delivery. For movables, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is rescission; Abu Yusuf agrees because sale of movables before delivery is invalid. For immovables, Abu Yusuf treats iqalah as a sale because sale of immovables before delivery is allowed in his view. The detailed Urdu commentary clarifies these points, emphasizing that the ruling depends on whether rescission is possible or not, and the different positions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
منقول (manqul): Movable property; items that can be transferred without damage.
عقار (aqar): Immovable property; land and buildings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Abu Yusuf rule iqalah before delivery of immovables as a sale, while for movables he rules rescission?
A) Because immovables are more valuable.
B) Because sale of immovables before delivery is permissible, so iqalah can be a sale; for movables, sale is impossible.
C) Because he follows the buyer's intent.
D) Because immovables require a written contract.

Key Takeaway
Iqalah before delivery of movables is always rescission; for immovables, Abu Yusuf treats it as a sale due to the permissibility of pre-delivery sale of immovables.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Iqalah with a Different Type of Price: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the ruling when iqalah is made with a different type of price.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on iqalah with a different price type and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Iqalah with a different price type: faskh for Abu Hanifa, new sale for Sahibayn.

When a buyer and seller mutually agree to cancel a sale, they may return the exact same item and price. But what if they agree on a different type of price—say, dirhams originally but dinars upon cancellation? Is this a simple rescission (faskh) or does it create a new sale? The Hanafi masters differ, and this lesson unpacks their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The original sale was for a specific price type (e.g., dirhams). The iqalah is made with a different price type (e.g., dinars).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa regards iqalah as rescission (faskh) regardless of the price type mentioned. The seller must return the original price, not the new type.
His view: the iqalah does not become a sale; it is pure faskh.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf holds that iqalah is inherently a sale, so this is a new sale. Muhammad holds that iqalah is faskh in principle, but if faskh is impossible due to change in price type, it becomes a sale.
Both conclude it is a sale, but for different reasons.
4
Compare the practical outcome
Under Abu Hanifa, the seller gets back the item and returns the original price (dirhams). Under Sahibayn, the seller returns the item but the buyer pays the new price (dinars) as a new sale.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Identify the underlying principle
The dispute hinges on the nature of iqalah: Is it always faskh (Abu Hanifa) or can it be a sale when the price type changes? Muhammad's position shows flexibility: faskh when possible, sale when not.
Imam Muhammad's principle: when faskh is impossible, consider it a sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر من اول کے علاوہ دوسری جنس پر اقالہ کیا مثلا من اول در اہم تھے اور ا قالہ کیا گیا دنا نیر پرتو حضرت امام حنیفہ کے نزدیک یا قاله من اول یعنی در اہم پر نخ بیج ہو گا اور نا نیر کاذکر نہ ہوگا یعنی بائع پر شمن اول یعنی در اہم کا واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا اور دنا نیر کا واپس کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا اور ا قالہ نخ بیچ ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ اقالہ ثمن اول کے سواء دوسری جنس پر بیع ہوگا یعنی یہ کہا جائے گا کہ مشتری نے وہ بیع جو بائع سے دراہم کے عوض خریدی تھی دنا تیر کے عوض اس کو فروخت کر دی ہے دونوں کی دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی ہے یعنی امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تو اقالہ کا بیج ہوتا ہی اصل ہے اس لیے ان کے نزدیک یہ اقالہ بیج ہوگا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اصل تو یہی ہے کہ اقالہ، فسخ ہو لیکن جب ثمن اول کے سوا، دوسری جنس ذکر کر دینے کی وجہ سے نسخ متعذر ہو گیا تو اس کو بیچ قرار دیا جائے گا کیونکہ اس کو بیع قرار دینا ممکن ہے اور امام محمد کا اصول بھی یہی ہے کہ جب اقالہ کو فسخ قرار دینا ممکن نہ ہو تو اس کو بیچ قرار دیا جائے گا۔
Explanation of the scenario: If iqalah is made with a different type of price than the original, e.g., the original price was dirhams and iqalah was made with dinars, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not a sale of the original price—i.e., there is no mention of dinars—so the seller must return the original price (dirhams) and not dinars, and the iqalah is not a sale. According to the Sahibayn, this iqalah is a sale with a different type of price not being the original—i.e., it will be said that the buyer has sold the item he bought from the seller for dirhams back to him for dinars. Their proofs have passed earlier: according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the principle is that iqalah is a sale, so this iqalah is a sale. According to Imam Muhammad, the principle is that iqalah is faskh, but when faskh becomes impossible because a different type of price is mentioned, it is considered a sale because it is possible to consider it a sale. Imam Muhammad's principle is that when iqalah cannot be considered faskh, it is considered a sale.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding iqalah when the agreed cancellation involves a different type of price than the original. The scenario: the original sale was for dirhams, but the parties agree to cancel with dinars. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that this is not a valid iqalah as faskh; rather, it is simply a faskh (rescission) of the original sale, meaning the seller must return the original price (dirhams), not the dinars. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider this a new sale of the item for dinars. Their reasoning: Abu Yusuf holds that iqalah is fundamentally a sale, so any iqalah is a sale. Muhammad holds that iqalah is fundamentally faskh, but if faskh is impossible due to the change in price type, it becomes a sale. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that iqalah can be either faskh or sale depending on circumstances.

Key Terms
إقالة (iqalah): A transaction between buyer and seller to mutually dissolve the sale contract, often by returning the goods and price.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract, reverting ownership to the original state.
ثمن (thaman): The price in a sale contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an iqalah where the original price was dirhams but the parties agree to cancel with dinars, what is Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling?
A) It is a new sale for dinars.
B) It is a faskh; the seller returns the original dirhams.
C) It is invalid because the price type changed.
D) It is a gift of the item.

Key Takeaway
In iqalah, changing the price type triggers an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds it as faskh (return original price), while the Sahibayn consider it a new sale for the new price.

Iqalah After Birth of a Sold Slave-Girl: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iqalah validity with separate increase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi disagreement regarding iqalah after the sold slave-girl gives birth and apply the distinction between separate (munfasila) and non-separate increases.

Core Idea
A separate increase after possession prevents faskh in iqalah, leading to a dispute on whether it becomes a sale.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about iqalah (mutual cancellation of a sale) when the sold item has undergone a change after the buyer's possession. Specifically, if a slave-girl gives birth, the child is a separate increase. Imam Abu Hanifa strictly treats iqalah as faskh (rescission), which requires returning the item unchanged. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow iqalah to function as a new sale when faskh is impossible. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi principle that the nature of iqalah depends on the possibility of returning the property exactly as it was.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario and timing
Read the passage to identify two scenarios: birth before vs. after the buyer's possession. Note that the child is a separate increase (ziyada munfasila).
Separate increase means a distinct entity that can be separated from the sold item, like a newborn.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling and rationale
State that for Abu Hanifa, iqalah after possession is invalid because the separate increase prevents faskh; before possession it is valid because no increase after possession blocks faskh.
Abu Hanifa holds iqalah is only faskh, never a sale.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's ruling and rationale
State that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that iqalah after possession is valid as a sale. Abu Yusuf says iqalah is essentially a sale; Muhammad says when faskh is impossible, iqalah becomes a sale.
Thus, even with a separate increase, the parties can cancel via a new sale.
4
Distinguish separate vs. non-separate increases
Note that non-separate increases like fat do not affect iqalah at all—faskh remains possible. This shows the key is the separability of the increase.
Fat is part of the slave-girl's body, not separate, so faskh returns the item as it is.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, if birth occurs after possession, iqalah is invalid and the original sale stands. Under the Sahibayn, iqalah is treated as a new sale, so the buyer returns the slave-girl (without the child? Actually the child remains with the buyer) for a price, often the same price.
The dispute affects whether cancellation requires a new contract or is simply void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر مبیعہ باندی نے مشتری کے قبضہ کرنے کے بعد بچہ جنا پھر عاقدین نے اقالہ کیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ ا قالہ باطل ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اقالہ فقط مسخ ہوتا ہے۔ قبضہ کرنے کے بعد ایسی زیادتی کا پیدا ہو جانا جو بیع سے جدا ہو۔ مانع فسخ ہوتی ہے اور بچہ بھی زیادتی منفصلہ ہے لہذا یہ بھی فتح کے لئے مانع ہوگا۔ اور جب زیادتی منفصلہ کی وجہ سے فسخ ممنوع ہے تو اقالہ باطل ہو جائے گا اور بیج اول اپنے حال پر باقی رہے گی۔ لیکن اگر مبیعہ باندی نے مشتری کے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بچہ جنا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک اقالہ درست ہو جائے گا کیونکہ زیادتی منفصلہ قبضہ کرنے سے مانع منع نہیں ہوتی ہے اور اگر اس پر چربی چڑھ گئی تو یہ زیادتی نہ قبضہ سے پہلے مانع فتح ہے اور نہ قبض کے بعد مانع نسخ ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ مبیعہ باندی کے بچہ جننے کے بعد اگرا قالہ کیا تو یہا قالہ بیچ ہوگا ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تو اس لیے کہ اقالہ کا بیع ہونا ہی اصل ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس لیے کہ جب زیادتی منفصلہ کی وجہ سے مسخ ممکن نہیں رہا تو اقالہ کو بیچ قرار دیا جائے گا کیونکہ بیچ قرار دینا ممکن ہے اور یہی امام محمد کا اصول ہے کہ اگر فسخ ممکن نہ ہو تو اقالہ کو بیع قرار دیا جائے گا۔
The author of Hidayah said: If the sold slave-girl gave birth after the buyer took possession, then the parties made iqalah, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this iqalah is invalid. The proof is that according to Imam, iqalah is only faskh. After possession, the occurrence of such an increase that is separate from the sale prevents faskh. The child is a separate increase, so it becomes a preventer of faskh. When faskh is prevented due to separate increase, the iqalah becomes invalid and the original sale remains as is. But if the slave-girl gave birth before the buyer took possession, then according to Imam the iqalah is valid because a separate increase before possession does not prevent faskh. And if she gained fat (increase that is not separate), this increase does not prevent faskh either before or after possession. The Sahibayn said: If iqalah is made after the slave-girl gave birth, this iqalah is a sale. For Abu Yusuf, because iqalah is essentially a sale. For Muhammad, because when faskh is not possible due to separate increase, iqalah is considered a sale as it is possible to consider it a sale. This is Muhammad's principle: when faskh is not possible, iqalah is considered a sale.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of an increase (child) in the sold slave-girl on iqalah. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes based on whether the birth occurred before or after the buyer's possession. If after possession, the child is a separate increase (ziyada munfasila) that prevents faskh, so iqalah is invalid; if before possession, it does not prevent faskh, so iqalah is valid. In contrast, the Sahibayn treat the situation as a sale: Abu Yusuf because iqalah is sale by nature, Muhammad because when faskh is impossible due to increase, it becomes a sale. Note that non-separate increases (like fat) do not affect iqalah at all. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that the nature of iqalah (faskh vs. sale) depends on the possibility of returning the property exactly as it was.

Key Terms
زیادہ منفصلہ (ziyada munfasila): A separate increase in the sold item, such as a child born to a slave-girl, that is distinct from the original item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why does iqalah become a sale when the sold slave-girl gives birth after possession?
A) Because iqalah is always a sale by definition.
B) Because faskh is impossible due to the separate increase, so it is treated as a sale.
C) Because the child belongs to the seller, requiring a new contract.
D) Because the buyer wants to keep the child.

Key Takeaway
The validity of iqalah after a separate increase depends on whether it is treated as faskh (Abu Hanifa) or as a sale (Sahibayn), with the timing and separability of the increase being decisive.

Iqalah Before Possession: Movable vs. Immovable Property
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iqalah before possession for movable vs. immovable property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on iqalah before possession for movable and immovable property, and apply the talil (legal reasoning) that determines whether it is a sale or faskh.

Core Idea
Iqalah before possession: for movables always faskh; for immovables, sale (Abu Yusuf) or faskh (Muhammad) depending on validity of pre-possession sale.

This passage from Hidayah addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: what is the nature of iqalah (rescission/revocation) when conducted before the buyer has taken possession? The ruling hinges on whether the underlying sale of the item before possession is valid. For movable goods, there is consensus that such a sale is invalid, so iqalah must be faskh. For immovable goods, the Sahibayn differ: Abu Yusuf permits the sale before possession, so iqalah can be a new sale; Muhammad prohibits such a sale, so iqalah remains faskh. Understanding this reasoning (talil) is key to mastering the Hanafi approach to conditional transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
What is iqalah? When does it occur? (before possession). What are the two categories of property? (manqul/movable, ghayr manqul/immovable).
2
Recall the baseline ruling on sale before possession
For movables: invalid by consensus (ijma). For immovables: dispute between Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf permits, Muhammad prohibits).
3
Apply the talil (legal reasoning)
How does the baseline ruling affect the nature of iqalah? If the sale before possession is invalid, then iqalah cannot be a sale; it must be faskh. If the sale is valid (as per Abu Yusuf for immovables), then iqalah can be a sale.
4
Compare the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Abu Yusuf: iqalah before possession for immovables = sale (because sale is permissible). For movables = faskh (because sale is invalid). Muhammad: iqalah before possession for both = faskh (because he prohibits sale of immovables before possession as well).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Yusuf, the iqalah is a new sale, so the buyer resells to the original seller; under Muhammad, it is simply a rescission, returning the contract to its original state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ کی عبارت والا قبالة قبل القبض فى المنقول وغيره .... الخ کوحل کرنے سے پہلے یہ ذہن نشین فرما لیجئے کہ اشیاء منقولہ کی بیع قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بالا جماع جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور اشیاء غیر منقولہ جیسے زمین اور مکان کی بیع قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے سیخین کے نزدیک جائز ہے لیکن امام محمد کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے۔ اب حاصل عبارت یہ ہے کہ مبیع شی منقول ہو یاشی غیر منقول ہوا گر مشتری نے قبضہ کئے بغیر ا قالہ کیا تو طرفین کے نزدیک یہ اقالہ صبح بیع ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں کے نزدیک اصل یہی ہے کہ اقالہ، فسخ بیع ہو اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک بھی اگر بیع شی منقول ہو تو قالہ مسخ ہی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اگر چدا قالہ کا بیع ہونا اصل ہے مگر چونکہ مشتری نے مبیع منقول پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے ہی اقالہ کر دیا ہے اور شی منقول کی بیع نا جائز ہے اس لیے اس اقالہ کو بیع قرار دینا تو مستعد ر ہو گیا اور جب بیج قرار دینا منعد ر ہو جائے تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس کو فسخ قرار دیا جاتا ہے اس لئے امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقالہ بیچ ہوگا کیونکہ غیر منقول کے اقالہ کو بیع قرار دینا ممکن ہے اور غیر منقول کے اقالہ کو بیچ قرار دینا اس لئے ممکن ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے غیر منقول کی بیع جائز ہے۔
Before explaining the text of Hidayah regarding iqalah before possession for movable and other items, keep in mind: The sale of movable items before possession is unanimously not permissible. And the sale of immovable items like land and house before possession is permissible according to the Sahibayn but not permissible according to Imam Muhammad. Now the summary of the text: If the sold item is movable or immovable and the buyer makes iqalah without taking possession, then according to both (Sahibayn) this iqalah is faskh (rescission) because according to both, iqalah is faskh. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, if the sale is of a movable item, then iqalah is faskh because although according to Abu Yusuf iqalah is originally a sale, but since the buyer made iqalah before taking possession of the movable item, and the sale of a movable item without possession is impermissible, so considering this iqalah as a sale becomes impossible. When considering it as a sale becomes impossible, then according to Abu Yusuf it is considered faskh. Therefore, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, iqalah is a sale (for immovable) because for immovable, considering iqalah as a sale is possible because according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the sale of immovable before possession is permissible.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on iqalah before the buyer takes possession. For movable goods, the sale before possession is invalid by consensus, so iqalah cannot be a sale and must be faskh. For immovable goods, there is a dispute between the Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf permits selling immovable before possession, so he considers iqalah before possession as a sale; Muhammad prohibits selling immovable before possession, so he considers iqalah as faskh. This shows how the nature of iqalah depends on the permissibility of the underlying sale.

Key Terms
منقول (manqul): Movable property that can be transported without damage.
غیر منقول (ghayr manqul): Immovable property like land and buildings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the consensus (ijma) mentioned in the passage, what is the ruling on selling movable property before possession?
A) Valid
B) Invalid
C) Permissible
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The nature of iqalah before possession depends on the validity of the underlying sale before possession: for movables (invalid), it is faskh; for immovables, it is sale (Abu Yusuf) or faskh (Muhammad).

Effect of Destruction of Price vs. Sold Item on Iqalah
Ruling with proof using qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on iqalah when the price is destroyed versus when the sold item is destroyed, and explain the Hanafi reasoning based on the sale's existence.

Core Idea
Iqalah requires an existing sale; only the sold item's existence matters, not the price.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: after a sale, one party may wish to rescind (iqalah). What if the price has been destroyed? Or the sold item? The Hanafi ruling provides a clear distinction based on the nature of the sale contract, where the sold item is the principal element.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the two cases: destruction of price vs. destruction of sold item, and the corresponding validity of iqalah.
The ruling is: iqalah valid if price destroyed, invalid if sold item destroyed.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence in the text: 'Because the revocation of the sale requires its existence, and it exists with the sold item, not with the price.'
This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the dalil proves the ruling: the sale contract's existence depends on the sold item (mabi'), not the price (thaman).
The word 'qaim' indicates that the sale is established by the sold item.
4
Note the underlying principle
In Hanafi fiqh, the sold item is the principal (asl) and the price is subsidiary (tabi). Thus, the sale exists as long as the sold item exists.
This principle is applied consistently in sales.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وهلاك الثمن لا يمنع صحة الاقالة وهلاك المبيع يمنع عنها لان رفع البيع يستدعى قيامه وهو قائم بالمبيع دون الثمن ترجمہ اور شمن کا ہلاک ہو جانا اقالہ صحیح ہونے کو نہیں روکتا ہے اور مبیع کا ہلاک ہو جانا اس سے روکتا ہے کیونکہ بیع کا دور کرنا اس کے موجود ہونے کا تقاضہ کرتا ہے اور بیج کا قیام بیع کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے نہ کہ شمن کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عقد بیع کے بعد اگر بائع کے پاس سے ثمن بلاک ہو گیا اور عاقدین نے اقالہ کرنا چاہا تو اقالہ درست ہو جائے گا لیکن اگر مبیع ہلاک ہوگئی تو اقالہ درست نہ ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ شمن کا ہلاک ہو جانا صحت اقالہ کے لیے مانع نہیں ہے لیکن مبیع کا ہلاک ہو جانا صحت اقالہ کے لیے مانع ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقالہ نام ہے بیچ دور کرنے کا اور بیع بیع کے ساتھ قائم ہوتی ہے ثمن کے ساتھ قائم نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ عقد بیع میں مبیع اصل ہوتی ہے ثمن اصل نہیں ہوتا۔ یمن تو بمنزلہ وصف کے ہوتا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر شمن موجود نہ ہو تو عقد بیع تب بھی جائز ہو جاتا ہے لیکن اگر بیع موجود نہ ہو تو عقد بیع جائز نہیں ہوتا پس اگر مبیع موجود نہ ہو تو بیع موجود نہ ہوگی اور جب بیع موجود نہیں ہو گی تو اس کا رفع یعنی اقالہ بھی درست نہ ہو گا لیکن اگر شمن موجود نہ ہو اور مبیع موجود ہو تو بیچ موجود ہوگی ۔ اور جب بیع موجود ہے تو اس کا رفع یعنی اقالہ بھی درست ہو گا۔
He said: Destruction of the price does not prevent the validity of iqalah, and destruction of the sold item prevents it. Because the revocation of the sale requires its existence, and it exists with the sold item, not with the price. Translation: And the destruction of the price does not prevent the iqalah being valid, and the destruction of the sold item prevents it, because revoking the sale requires its existence, and the existence of the sale is with the sold item, not with the price. Explanation: The scenario is that after the contract of sale, if the price is destroyed from the seller's side and the parties intend to make iqalah, the iqalah is valid. But if the sold item is destroyed, iqalah is not valid. The conclusion is that destruction of the price is not a preventer for the validity of iqalah, but destruction of the sold item is a preventer. The evidence is that iqalah is the name of revoking the sale, and the sale is established with the sold item, not with the price, because in the contract of sale, the sold item is the principal, the price is not the principal; the price is like a description. This is why if the price does not exist, the sale contract is still valid, but if the sold item does not exist, the sale contract is not valid. So if the sold item does not exist, the sale does not exist, and when the sale does not exist, its revocation (iqalah) is not valid. But if the price does not exist and the sold item exists, then the sale exists, and since the sale exists, its revocation (iqalah) is valid.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage establishes a key ruling: iqalah is valid if the price has been destroyed, but invalid if the sold item is destroyed. The reasoning is that iqalah revokes the sale contract, and the sale contract's existence depends on the existence of the sold item (mabi'), not on the price (thaman). The sold item is the principal subject matter; the price is subsidiary. Thus, as long as the sold item exists, the sale exists and can be revoked. If the price is gone, the sale still exists. This principle is based on the Hanafi view that the sale contract is centered on the sold item.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price in a sale contract.
مبيع (mabi'): The object of sale, the sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the price (thaman) is destroyed after the sale contract but before iqalah, what is the ruling on iqalah?
A) Iqalah is invalid because the price is gone.
B) Iqalah is valid because the sale still exists.
C) Iqalah is valid only if the buyer agrees.
D) Iqalah becomes a new sale.

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is valid if the sold item exists; destruction of the price does not invalidate it because the sale contract is established by the sold item.

Iqalah After Partial Destruction and in Exchange Sales
Ruling that iqalah is valid for remaining part if part destroyed, and valid in muqayadah if one countervalue destroyed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that iqalah is valid on the remaining part of a sale after partial destruction and in muqayadah (exchange) sales after destruction of one countervalue.

Core Idea
Iqalah requires the sale to exist; partial destruction or treating destroyed item as price preserves the sale.

This ruling addresses two edge cases: when part of the sold goods is destroyed before iqalah, and when an exchange sale (muqayadah) loses one item. The Hanafi view allows iqalah on the remainder by treating the sale as still extant for that part, or by designating the destroyed item as the price. Understanding this preserves the flexibility of iqalah and prevents unnecessary contractual breakdowns.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios and their rulings
Read the passage to identify the two distinct cases: (1) partial destruction in a normal sale, and (2) destruction of one countervalue in a muqayadah sale. Note the ruling for each: iqalah is valid on the remaining part and valid after destruction of one item in muqayadah.
2
Extract the underlying principle
The common principle is that iqalah requires the sale contract to exist. Both rulings show that the sale is considered to continue in the relevant subject matter after partial destruction or after designating the destroyed item as price.
3
Analyze the reasoning for partial destruction
The passage states 'liqiyam al-mabi' fihi' (because the sale exists in it). So the sale remains for the undestroyed part, hence iqalah is valid on that part.
Example: 10 maunds wheat, 4 lost, iqalah on remaining 6 is valid.
4
Analyze the reasoning for muqayadah
The reasoning is 'li-anna kulla wahidin minhuma mabi'' (each one is sold). In muqayadah, both items are both price and sold. We treat the destroyed item as price, so the surviving item remains as sold, preserving the sale for iqalah.
Example: slave for slave-girl, if slave-girl destroyed, iqalah on slave valid.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
This ruling is the standard Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) and there is no intra-madhhab disagreement. It is the operative ruling for fatwa.

فان هلک بعض المبيع جازت الاقالة فى الباقى لقيام المبيع فيه وان تقايضا تجوز الاقاله بعد هلاک احدهما ولا تبطل بهلاك احدهما لان كل واحد منهما مبيع فكان البيع باقيا والله اعلم باصواب ترجمہ پس اگر مبیع کا ایک حصہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو باقی کے اندرا قالہ جائز ہے کیونکہ باقی مبیع میں بیع قائم ہے اور اگر بیع مقائضہ کی ہو تو احد العوضین کے ہلاک ہو جانے کے بعد ا قالہ جائز ہے اور احد العوضین کے تلف ہونے کے بعد اقالہ باطل نہ ہو گا۔ اس لیے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک مبیع ہے پس بیج باقی ہوگی ۔ واللہ تعالیٰ اعلم بالصواب تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مبیع کا ایک حصہ ہلاک ہوگیا تو باقی مبیع میں اقالہ جائز ہے مثلاً دس من گندم دور و پسید فی من کے حساب سے ہیں روپے میں خریدے پھر چار من خرچ ہو گئے اور باقی چھے من میں دونوں نے اقالہ کیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ باقی مبیع یعنی چھ من گندم میں بیچ موجود ہے تو اس کا اقالہ بھی جائز ہے اور اگر بیع مقائضہ کی ہو یعنی سامان کی بیع سامان کے عوض کی ہو۔ مثلاً ایک غلام ایک باندی کے عوض خریدا ہو اور پھر احد العوضین ہلاک ہو گیا ہو تو بھی اقالہ جائز ہے۔ احد العوضین کے ہلاک ہونے سے اقالہ باطل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ بیع مقایضہ میں ہر عوض مبیع ہوتا ہے۔ اور ہر عوض شمن ہوتا ہے پس جو عوض ہلاک ہو گیا اس کو شمن قرار دیں گے اور جو موجود ہے وہ بیع ہوگا۔ اور مبیع موجود ہونے کی صورت میں چونکہ بیچ موجود ہوتی ہے۔ اور بیج موجود ہونے کی صورت میں اقالہ درست ہوتا ہے۔اس لئے اس صورت میں ا قالہ درست اور جائز ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
If part of the sold item is destroyed, iqalah is permissible in the remaining part because the sale exists in it. And if it is a muqayadah (exchange sale), iqalah is permissible after the destruction of one of the two countervalues, and it does not become invalid by the destruction of one of them, because each of them is a sold item, so the sale remains. (Allah knows best). Translation: So if part of the sold item is destroyed, iqalah is allowed in the remainder because the sale exists in the remainder. And if it is a muqayadah sale, iqalah is allowed after the destruction of one of the two countervalues, and it is not invalidated by the destruction of one of them, because each of them is a sold item, so the sale remains. Allah knows best. Explanation: The scenario is that if part of the sold item is destroyed, iqalah is allowed in the remaining part. For example, ten maunds of wheat were bought for twenty rupees (two rupees per maund), then four maunds were lost, and the parties make iqalah on the remaining six maunds – it is valid because the sale exists in the remaining wheat. And if the sale is a muqayadah, i.e., exchange of goods for goods, for example, a slave was bought for a slave-girl, and then one of the two countervalues is destroyed, then iqalah is still valid. The destruction of one countervalue does not invalidate iqalah because in a muqayadah sale, each countervalue is a sold item and each is a price. So the one that is destroyed is considered the price, and the one that exists is the sold item. When the sold item exists, the sale exists, and when the sale exists, iqalah is valid. Therefore, in this case, iqalah is valid and allowed. Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage addresses two situations. First, if part of the sold item is destroyed (e.g., part of a batch of wheat), iqalah is valid for the remaining part because the sale contract continues for that part. Second, in a muqayadah (exchange) sale where goods are exchanged for goods directly, if one of the items is destroyed, iqalah is still valid because we treat the destroyed item as the price and the surviving item as the sold item. Since the sold item exists, the sale exists and can be revoked. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that iqalah requires the existence of the sale, which can persist even after partial or one-sided destruction.

Key Terms
مقایضہ (muqayadah): An exchange sale where goods are exchanged directly for other goods, without money as price.
اقالة (iqalah): Mutual rescission of a sale contract by the parties, cancelling the sale and returning the subject matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a muqayadah (exchange) sale where a slave is bought for a slave-girl, if the slave-girl is destroyed, is iqalah valid?
A) No, because one countervalue is gone.
B) Yes, we consider the destroyed entity as the price, so the slave exists as sold item.
C) Yes, but only if both parties agree.
D) No, because the sale contract is void.

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is valid as long as the sale contract exists in the subject matter; partial destruction or treating destroyed items as price preserves that existence.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
8 min
Definition and Ruling of Murabahah and Tawliyah
Defines murabahah and tawliyah and establishes their permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define murabahah and tawliyah, state their permissibility (mubah) in the Hanafi school, and identify the key evidence (dalil) from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Murabahah and tawliyah are permissible sales based on trust, allowing reliance on an expert's purchase.

In this lesson, we explore two special types of sale: murabahah (sale at cost plus disclosed profit) and tawliyah (sale at exact cost). These sales are built on honesty and serve the needs of inexperienced buyers. The Hanafi school rules them permissible, provided the general conditions of sale are met.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definitions
Read the Arabic definitions carefully. Murabahah involves a known profit over the original cost; tawliyah involves no profit. Both require transfer of ownership from the first contract.
Focus on the key terms: 'ziyadat al-ribh' and 'min ghayr ziyadat ribh'.
2
Identify the ruling
The text clearly states 'al-bay'ani ja'izan' (both sales are permissible). Note the reasoning: need and necessity (hajah) for such transactions.
The ruling is mubah (permissible), not wajib.
3
Examine the evidence
The author cites the hadith of Abu Bakr and the Prophet during hijrah. Identify how the Prophet's request for a camel as tawliyah proves permissibility and the principle of paying a fair price.
The hadith is also used to show that tawliyah is a recognized transaction.
4
Note the conditions
While not enumerated, the text implies that general conditions of sale (offer, acceptance, capacity, etc.) must be met. Additionally, honesty and full disclosure are emphasized.
The murabahah specifically requires disclosure of the original cost and profit amount.

Book of Sales. Chapter on Murabahah and Tawliyah. Translation: This chapter is about the sale of murabahah and the sale of tawliyah. Explanation: Until now, the discussion was about sales that relate to the sale itself; now from here, the discussion is about sales that relate to the price, i.e., the sale of murabahah and tawliyah. According to the explanation of Sahib Kifayah, sales are of four types with respect to price, provided that there is goods in exchange for the price: 1. Sale of wadi'a, 2. Sale of murabahah, 3. Sale of musawamah, 4. Sale of tawliyah. Musawamah is bargaining for goods; in this sale, no attention is paid to the previous price. Wadi'a is selling for less than the first price. Murabahah is selling for more than the first price. Tawliyah is selling for the exact equivalent of the first price. Definition of murabahah and tawliyah, and the legal status of both sales. He said: Murabahah is transferring what one owns by the first contract for the first price with an increase of profit, and tawliyah is transferring what one owns by the first contract for the first price without an increase of profit. Both sales are permissible if the conditions of permissibility are met. And the need leads to this type of sale because the ignorant person who is not guided in trade needs to rely on the action of the intelligent, guided person, and his soul is pleased with the like of what was purchased and with an increase of profit. So it is necessary to rule on their permissibility. For this reason, their foundation is on honesty and avoiding treachery and what resembles it. And it is established that when the Prophet intended to migrate, Abu Bakr bought two camels. The Prophet said: 'Give me one of them as a tawliyah.' He said: 'It is for you without anything.' He said: 'But not without a price.' Translation: Murabahah is to transfer what one has become owner of by the first contract for the first price with an increase of profit, and tawliyah is to transfer what one has become owner of by the first contract for the first price without an increase of profit. And both sales are permissible because the conditions of permissibility are met, and there is a need for this type of sale because the ignorant person who does not know how to buy and sell needs to rely on the action of the intelligent, experienced person, and his heart is pleased that he purchased for the same amount with an increase of profit. So it is obligatory to say that both types of sale are permissible. And for this reason, both are based on honesty and avoiding treachery and the suspicion of treachery. And it is correct that when the Messenger of Allah intended to migrate, Abu Bakr bought two camels. Then Abu Bakr said: 'This is for you without money.' Then the Prophet said: 'But not without a price.' Explanation: Sahib Quduri defines murabahah and tawliyah. He says: Murabahah is that the buyer sells the goods he purchased for a known price with an increase to someone else. For example, goods purchased for one thousand rupees, another person relying on him buys them for one thousand one hundred rupees. This is called murabahah. Tawliyah is to sell for the same price without profit. For example, a horse purchased for one thousand rupees is sold for one thousand rupees. This is called tawliyah. Sahib Hidayah says: Both sales are permissible because, firstly, all conditions of permissibility exist; secondly, people engage in this type of transaction; thirdly, there is a need for this type of sale. The need for this type of sale is that sometimes a person is ignorant and unaware of trade matters, so he needs to rely on the action of an experienced person and please his heart by saying: 'I have purchased this goods for the same price as such-and-such knowledgeable person purchased it' or 'I have purchased it with this profit.' In these sales, the ignorant person will not be cheated, but rather will gain some satisfaction. In any case, conditions of permissibility exist, people's practice exists, and need demands, so what doubt is there in their permissibility? Certainly both sales are permissible. This is why murabahah and tawliyah are based on the seller being trustworthy and avoiding anything that involves treachery or the suspicion of treachery. The permissibility of tawliyah is also established from hadith. It is narrated that when the Prophet intended to migrate, Abu Bakr bought two camels. Then the Prophet said: 'Give me one of them as a tawliyah,' i.e., sell it to me for what you bought it. Abu Bakr said: 'It is for you without price.' The Prophet said: 'I will not take it without a price.' Also in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, there is a hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib: 'The Prophet said: Tawliyah, iqalah, and shirkah are permissible, there is no harm in them.' And in Sahih Bukhari, in the hadith of Aisha about the hijrah: 'Abu Bakr said to the Prophet: 'Take one of these two mounts.' The Prophet said: 'For a price.' The she-camel that the Prophet took from Abu Bakr was named Qaswa. And in Ibn Majah, a hadith: 'The Messenger of Allah said: 'I have not benefited from anyone's wealth as I have benefited from Abu Bakr's wealth.'' And scholars have written that the Prophet accepted much financial service from Abu Bakr, even in the sermon of his final illness he said: 'Whoever had a financial right over me, I have compensated him except Abu Bakr; his favor remains upon me; Allah will complete it on the Day of Judgment.' But despite this, he did not accept the she-camel without a price because hijrah was an act of obedience and worship, and participation in worship is not appropriate, just as seeking help in wudu is disliked. So he did not accept it without a price.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage deals with the definitions and rulings of two specific types of sale: murabahah and tawliyah. The author begins by situating these sales within the broader classification of sales based on price. He notes that previously the discussion focused on sales related to the sold object; now it turns to sales related to the price. According to the author, there are four types of sales concerning price: musawamah (bargaining without reference to original price), wadi'a (selling at a loss), murabahah (selling at a profit), and tawliyah (selling at cost). The core of the lesson is the definition of murabahah and tawliyah. Murabahah is defined as transferring ownership of an item acquired through a first contract for the original price plus a stated profit. Tawliyah is similar but without any profit; the item is sold exactly at the original cost. The author then states that both sales are permissible, provided all general conditions of sale are met. The reasoning given is based on necessity: an inexperienced buyer can rely on an experienced buyer's purchase and is willing to pay a profit for that reliability. This need justifies the permissibility. The author emphasizes that these sales are built on trust (amanah) and avoidance of fraud. He then provides a hadith proof: during the Prophet's hijrah, Abu Bakr purchased two camels. The Prophet requested one as a tawliyah (i.e., at cost), and when Abu Bakr offered it for free, the Prophet insisted on paying the price. This shows the permissibility of tawliyah and the importance of not taking something without compensation in transactions. The commentary elaborates with examples: murabahah is like buying goods for 1000 rupees and selling them for 1100 with a declared profit; tawliyah is selling for exactly 1000. The author further supports the ruling with additional hadiths from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Bukhari, and notes that the Prophet's refusal to accept the camel for free was because hijrah was an act of worship, and participation in worship through financial gifts is disliked. Thus, the permissibility of murabahah and tawliyah is firmly established by evidence and necessity.

Key Terms
المرابحة (al-murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the original cost and adds a known profit, selling at cost plus profit.
التولية (al-tawliyah): A sale where the seller transfers ownership at exactly the original cost, without any profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on murabahah and tawliyah?
A) Both are prohibited because they involve uncertainty.
B) Both are permissible provided conditions are met.
C) Murabahah is permissible but tawliyah is not.
D) Both are disliked (makruh).

Key Takeaway
Murabahah and tawliyah are permissible sales built on trust and disclosure, and their validity is supported by the Prophet's own practice.

Definition and Permissibility of Murabahah and Tawliyah
Defining Murabahah and Tawliyah and proving their validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Murabahah and Tawliyah, state the three reasons for their permissibility, and identify the hadith evidence used.

Core Idea
Murabahah and Tawliyah are permissible trust sales based on disclosure, custom, and need, and confirmed by the Prophet's practice.

In this lesson, we examine two special types of sales: Murabahah (cost-plus) and Tawliyah (sale at cost). These are trust-based transactions where the seller must be honest about the original price. The author of Hidayah establishes their permissibility using three arguments: fulfilment of general sale conditions, established custom, and practical necessity. We also explore the hadith evidence from the Hijrah incident and explicit prophetic statements.

Guided Path
1
Define the two sales
Explain the difference between Murabahah and Tawliyah in your own words. Note that both require disclosure of the original cost.
Murabahah includes a known profit; Tawliyah has no profit.
2
Identify the three reasons for permissibility
List the three reasons given in the text: (1) all conditions of a valid sale are met, (2) people customarily engage in them, (3) there is a genuine need, especially for inexperienced buyers.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Review the hadith of the Prophet's purchase of a camel from Abu Bakr at cost during the Hijrah, and the explicit hadith from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib: 'There is no harm in Tawliyah, iqalah, and partnership.'
4
Understand the condition of trustworthiness
The seller must be amin (trustworthy) and avoid any real or suspected deceit. The Prophet's refusal to take the camel for free shows the importance of clear transaction terms.

Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume eight. Explanation: Author of Quduri defines Murabahah and Tawliyah. He said: Murabahah sale is that the buyer sells the goods to another at the known cost plus a stated profit. For example, goods bought for one thousand rupees, then another person relying on him buys it for one thousand one hundred rupees, this is called Murabahah. And Tawliyah sale is that he sells it at the same price without profit, e.g., bought a horse for one thousand rupees and sells it for one thousand rupees, this is called Tawliyah. The author of Hidayah says both these sales are permissible because firstly all conditions of permissibility exist, secondly people customarily engage in such transactions, and thirdly there is a need for this type of sale. The need is that sometimes a person is unfamiliar with trade practices, so he needs to rely on an expert and console himself that he bought it at the same price as the expert. In these sales, there is no suspicion of deceit; rather, there is satisfaction. Since conditions are met, custom exists, and need necessitates, there is no doubt about their permissibility. Thus Murabahah and Tawliyah are based on the seller being trustworthy and avoiding everything involving deceit or suspicion. The permissibility of Tawliyah is also proven by hadith. It is narrated that when the Prophet intended migration, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq bought two mounts. The Prophet said, 'Give me one of these as Tawliyah,' i.e., sell it to me at the cost. Abu Bakr said, 'It is for you without price.' The Prophet said, 'I will not take it without price.' Also in Musannaf Ibn Abd al-Razzaq, the hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib: The Prophet said, 'Tawliyah, iqalah, and partnership – there is no problem in them.' In Sahih al-Bukhari, the hadith of Aisha about migration: Abu Bakr said to the Prophet, 'Take one of these two mounts.' The Prophet said, 'For a price.' The camel the Prophet took from Abu Bakr was named Qaswa. In Ibn Majah's hadith, the Prophet said, 'No one has benefited me with his wealth as Abu Bakr has.' Scholars have written that the Prophet accepted much financial help from Abu Bakr, even in his final illness he said, 'Whoever had a financial right upon me, I have compensated, except Abu Bakr, whose favor remains; Allah will complete it on the Day of Judgment.' Despite this, the Prophet did not accept the camel without price because migration was an act of worship, and associating others in worship is not appropriate, just as seeking help in wudu is disliked. Therefore he did not accept it without price.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage opens by defining two types of sales: Murabahah (cost-plus sale) and Tawliyah (sale at cost). The author of Quduri defines them, and the author of Hidayah states that both are permissible. Three reasons are given: (1) all conditions for a valid sale exist, (2) there is established custom (ta'amul) of people engaging in such transactions, and (3) there is a genuine need — an inexperienced buyer can rely on the seller's expertise without fear of deception. The underlying principle is that the seller must be trustworthy (amin) and avoid any real or suspected dishonesty. The permissibility of Tawliyah is further supported by multiple hadith: the Prophet's own purchase of a camel from Abu Bakr at cost during the Hijrah, and explicit reports from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and the incident with Aisha. The passage also explains why the Prophet refused to take the camel for free: because Hijrah was an act of worship, and accepting a gift in the context of worship is disliked (makruh), similar to seeking material help during wudu. Thus, the permissibility is firmly established by textual evidence and rational reasoning.

Key Terms
بیع مرابحہ (bay' al-murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost and sells with an agreed profit margin. The buyer knows the original price.
بیع تولیہ (bay' al-tawliyah): A sale at the original cost without any profit; the seller transfers ownership at the same price he paid.
تعامل (ta'amul): Common practice or custom among people in transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Conditions of validity are met, custom supports them, and people need them.
C) The Prophet specifically commanded them.
D) They are more profitable for the seller.

Key Takeaway
Murabahah and Tawliyah are permissible trust sales based on disclosure, custom, need, and prophetic proof.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Condition for Murabahah and Tawliyah: Price Must Be Mithli
Establishing a condition for trust-based sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid Murabahah and Tawliyah according to the Hanafi school, and distinguish between mithli and qimiy prices with examples.

Core Idea
Murabahah and Tawliyah require the price to be mithli; qimiy prices create uncertainty invalidating the trust-based sale.

This passage explains a crucial condition for trust-based sales (Murabahah and Tawliyah) in Hanafi fiqh. The price must be a standardized (mithli) item, not a unique (qimiy) one, because uncertainty in valuation leads to suspicion of deceit. Through clear examples, the text shows how this preserves the transparency these contracts require.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage rules on Murabahah (sale with profit) and Tawliyah (sale at cost). The ruling: they are invalid unless the price is mithli.
The hukm is fasid if the condition is not met.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a rational inference (qiyas jaliy) based on the need to avoid shubhat al-khiyanah (suspicion of deceit) in trust sales.
No direct text from Quran or hadith is cited; the reasoning is derived from the nature of these contracts.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The 'illa (effective cause) is the uncertainty (jahalah) that arises from a qimiy price: since no standard equivalent exists, valuation is estimation, which inevitably creates the appearance of possible deception.
This parallels the prohibition of gharar in other sales.
4
Apply to examples
The passage gives examples: mithli items (dirhams, measurable wheat) are valid; qimiy items (horses, slaves) are not. An exception exists if the second buyer already owns the exact substitute item.
The exception removes the uncertainty because the specific item can be delivered.
5
Note the practical implication
In practice, for a Murabahah contract to be valid, the price must be from among makilat (measured), mawzunat (weighed), or adadiyat mutaqaribah (similar countable) items.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

قال ولا تصح المرابحة والتولية حتى يكون العوض مماله مثل لانه اذا لم يكن له مثل لو ملكه ملكه بالقيمة وهى مجهولة ولو كان المشتری باعه مرابحة ممن یملک ذالک البدل وقد باعه بربح درهم او بشئی من المكيل موصوف جاز لانه يقدر على الوفا بما التزم وان باعه بربح ده یازده لا يجوز لا نه باعه براس المال و ببعض قيمته لانه ليس من ذوات الامثال
ترجمہ اور بیچ مرابحہ اور تولیہ جائز نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ ثمن ایسی چیز ہو جس کا مثل ہوتا ہے کیونکہ اگر اس کا مثل نہ ہو تو اگر مالک ہوا تو با قیمت اس کا مالک ہوگا ۔ حالانکہ قیمت مجبول ہے اور اگر مشترکی نے اس چیز کو بطور مرابحہ ایسے آدمی کے ہاتھ فروخت کیا جو اس عوض کا مالک ہے حالانکہ اس نے ایک درہم مطلع پر پاکسی ملیلی متعین چیز کے نفع پر فروخت کیا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ اس چیز کوادا کرنے پر قادر ہے جس کا اس نے التزام کیا ہے اور اگر اس نے وہ یازدہ کے نفع پر بچا تو جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس نے رأس المال اور اس کی بعض قیمت کے عوض فروخت کیا ہے کیونکہ وہ ذوات الا مثال میں ہے نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ بیچ مرا بجھہ اور بیع تولیہ اس وقت جائز ہے جبکہ شمن ذوات الامثال میں سے ہو یعنی مکیلات میں سے ہو یا موزونات میں سے ہو یا عددیات متقاربہ میں سے ہو اور اگر شمن ذوات القیم میں سے ہو مثلا کپڑایا جانور یا غلام کوشن بنایا ہوتو پھر بیچ مرابحہ اور تولیہ جائز نہ ہوئی۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ بیج مرابحہ اور بیع تولیہ میں خیانت اور شبہ خیانت دونوں سے احتراز ممکن ہے مثلاً ایک غلام ایک ہزار دینار کے عوض خریدا پھر دوسرے کو گیارہ سو دینار کے عوض فروخت کر دیا یا ایک ہزار دینار کے عوض ہی فروخت کر دیا یا ایک ہزار دینار کے عوض ہی فروخت کیا تو پہلی صورت میں بیج مرابحہ ہوگی اور دوسری صورت میں بیج تولیہ ہوگی ۔ ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں نہ خیانت ہے اور نہ خیانت کا شبہ ہے یا مثلاً ایک غلام ایک سوصاع گندم کے عوض خریدا پھر اس کو ایک سو دس صاع گندم کے عوض یا ایک سوصاع گندم کے عوض فروخت کر دیا تو پہلی صورت میں بیع مرابحہ ہوگی اور دوسری صورت میں بیع تولیہ ہوگی ۔ اور اس میں نہ خیانت ہے اور نہ خیانت کا شبہ ہے اور ذوات القیم کی صورت میں اگر چہ خیانت سے احتراز ممکن ہے لیکن شہبتہ الخیانت سے احتراز ممکن نہیں ہے مثلاً کسی نے ایک غلام ایک گھوڑے کے عوض خریدا پھر اس نام کو مرابحہ یا تولیہ فروخت کیا تھے مشتری ثانی گھوڑے کی قیمت کا اندازہ لگا کرشن ادا کرے گا کیونکہ مشتری ثانی بعینہ وہ گھوڑا تو دے نہیں سکتا اور نہ اس کا مثل دے سکتا بعینہ وہ گھوڑا تو اس لئے نہیں دے سکتا کہ مشتری ثانی اس کا مالک نہیں سے بلکہ اس کا مالک بائع اول سے اور اس کا مثل اس لئے نہیں دے سکتا کہ گھوڑ ا ذات الامثال میں سے نہیں بلکہ ذوات القیم میں سے ہے۔ لامحالہ گھوڑے کی قیمت ادا کرے گا اور گھوڑے کی قیمت مجبول ہے کیونکہ قیمت کا فیصلہ بالکل حتمی اور قطعی نہیں کیا جاسکتا بلکہ اس کا تخمینہ اور اندازہ ہی کیا جا سکتا ہے اور تخمینہ اور اندازہ میں آدمی سے غلطی بھی ہو سکتی ہے اس لئے قیمت کا اندازہ کرنے کی صورت میں چہ خیانت متحقق نہیں ہے لیکن یہ خیانت ضرور متحقق ہے اور مرابحہ اور تولیہ میں خیانت کی طرح عبۂ خیانت سے بچنا بھی ضروری ہے اس
لئے ہم نے کہا کتی من اگر ذوات القیم میں سے ہو تو مشتری کو مرابحہ اور تولیہ کے طور پر فروخت کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ ولو كان المشتری باعه ات کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ سابق میں بیان ہوا کہ اگر کسی نے کوئی چیز ایسی شئی کے عوض خریدی ہو جو ذوات القیم میں سے ہے تو مشتری کو وہ پیچ مرابحہ یا تولیہ فروخت کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ یعنی حامد اس چیز کو ادا کرنے پر قادر ہے جس کا اس نے التزام کیا ہے۔ یعنی بیچ اول میں جو شمن تھا یعنی گھوڑ ا حامد اس کو ادا کرنے پر قادر ہے اور اس صورت میں چونکہ نہ خیانت ہے اور نہ شب خیانت ہے اس لیے جائز ہے وان باعه بربح ده یازده ... الخ کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر خالد نے یہ غلام حامد کے ہاتھ اس گھوڑے کے عوض اور دوم یازدہ نفع یعنی دس فیصد نفع پر بچا ہو تو یہ مرابحہ نا جائز ہے وہ یاز دو یا دس فیصد کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ثمن اول اگر دس درہم ہوں تو نفع ایک درہم ہوگا۔ اور اگر میں درہم ہوں تو نفع دو درہم ہوگا اور اگر میں درہم ہوں تو نفع تین درہم ہوں گے اور اگر من اول ایک سو درہم ہوں تواضع دیس درہم ہوں گے وغیرہ ذالک اور یہ نا جائز اس لیے ہے کہ وہ یازدہ یا دس فیصد نفع اس بات کا تقاضہ کرتا ہے کہ نفع راس المال یعنی تمن کی جنس سے
He said: Murabahah and Tawliyah are not valid until the price is of a type that has a similar (mithli) counterpart, because if it has no similar, when the owner takes ownership, he owns it by value (qimah), and value is unknown. If the buyer sold it as Murabahah to someone who owns that substitute, and he sold it with a profit of one dirham or something described from the measurable (makil), it is valid because he can fulfill what he undertook. But if he sold it with a profit of 'dah yazdah' (ten percent), it is not valid because he sold it for the original capital and part of its value, since it is not of the mithli type. Translation: Murabahah and Tawliyah sales are not valid unless the price is a thing that has a mithl (standardized equivalent), because if it has no mithl, then when the owner takes ownership, he owns it by value, and value is unknown. And if the buyer sold it as Murabahah to a person who owns that substitute, and he sold it with a profit of one dirham or some specific described thing from the measurable, then it is valid, because he is able to deliver what he committed. But if he sold it with a profit of 'dah yazdah' (ten percent), it is not valid because he sold it for the original capital and part of its value, since it is not of the mithli type. Explanation: Author of Quduri says that Murabahah and Tawliyah are valid only when the price is from the mithliyat, i.e., from measurable (makilat), weighable (mawzunat), or countable similar items (adadiyat mutaqaribah). But if the price is from the qimiyyat, e.g., cloth, animal, or slave, then Murabahah and Tawliyah are not valid. The proof is that earlier it passed that in Murabahah and Tawliyah, both real deception and suspicion of deception can be avoided. For example, a slave bought for one thousand dinars, then sold to another for eleven hundred dinars, or for one thousand dinars exactly – in the first case it is Murabahah, the second Tawliyah. Clearly there is no deception or suspicion. Similarly, a slave bought for one hundred sa' of wheat, then sold for one hundred ten sa' or one hundred sa' – again no deception. But in case of qimiy items, although actual deception can be avoided, suspicion cannot. For example, someone bought a slave for a horse, then sells it as Murabahah or Tawliyah – the second buyer will pay the estimated value of the horse because he cannot deliver the exact horse nor its mithl (since horse is not mithli). Therefore he pays its value, which is unknown because value cannot be precisely determined; only estimation is possible, and estimation involves error. Thus, although actual deception may not occur, there is suspicion. Therefore it is not allowed. Summary of the text: earlier it was stated that if someone bought something with a qimiy price, he is not allowed to sell it as Murabahah or Tawliyah. However, if the second buyer owns that specific substitute (e.g., the horse), then it is valid because he can deliver it, removing deception and suspicion. But if the profit is specified as 'dah yazdah' (ten percent), it is invalid because it implies the profit is of the same type as the capital, which is not defined.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents a crucial condition for the validity of Murabahah and Tawliyah: the price (thaman) must be a mithli item – something standardized like measurable (makil: e.g., wheat, dates), weighable (mawzun: e.g., gold, silver), or countable similar items (adadiyya mutaqariba: e.g., eggs, nuts). The reason is that when the price is unique (qimiy), the second buyer cannot pay the exact same item nor its standardized equivalent; he must pay the estimated value, which introduces uncertainty (gharar) and suspicion of deceit. The text explains through examples: if the price is a mithli like dinars or wheat, the transaction is valid because the buyer can deliver the exact same type. But if the price is a horse (qimiy), the buyer cannot deliver that horse (he doesn't own it) nor its mithl (horses have no standard equivalence), so he must pay the value, which is unknown. The ruling is a direct application of the principle that Murabahah and Tawliyah are trust-based sales requiring full transparency and absence of suspicion. The exception is when the second buyer owns the exact same substitute (e.g., he is the owner of that specific horse) – then the transaction is valid because he can deliver it. A fatwa of 'dah yazdah' (ten percent profit) is invalid if the capital is not a mithli, because the profit then becomes part of the unknown value. This demonstrates the Hanafi emphasis on certainty and avoidance of gharar in trust sales.

Key Terms
مثلی (mithli): A commodity that has standard equivalents (amthal) such that one unit can substitute another without significant difference (e.g., wheat, silver, eggs).
قیمی (qimiy): A commodity that has no standard equivalent; its value is determined by estimation (taqdeer) (e.g., slaves, animals, land).
شبهة الخيانة (shubhat al-khiyanah): Suspicion of dishonesty; even if actual deception is absent, the mere appearance of possible deceit invalidates the transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Murabahah invalid when the price is a qimiy item (e.g., a horse)?
A) Because the profit cannot be calculated.
B) Because the buyer cannot deliver the exact same item or its standard equivalent, leading to valuation uncertainty.
C) Because qimiy items are more expensive.
D) Because the seller may not own the item.

Key Takeaway
For Murabahah and Tawliyah to be valid, the price must be a standardized mithli item to avoid uncertainty and suspicion of deceit.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Condition for Murabahah and Tawliyah: Thaman Must Be Mithli
Stating condition of mithli thaman for Murabahah and Tawliyah with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition for a valid Murabahah or Tawliyah sale, explain the rationale based on avoiding suspicion of dishonesty, and distinguish mithli from qimi thaman in practical scenarios.

Core Idea
Murabahah and Tawliyah require a mithli thaman to eliminate uncertainty and suspicion of dishonesty.

Murabahah (cost-plus sale) and Tawliyah (sale at cost) are trust-based contracts where transparency is paramount. The Hanafi school stipulates a critical condition: the price paid by the first buyer (thaman) must be from items that have exact equivalents (mithliyat). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this rule through examples and exceptions, emphasising the principle of avoiding both actual dishonesty and its mere suspicion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
State the Hanafi ruling: Murabahah and Tawliyah are not valid unless the thaman is mithli (has a known like). Note that the thaman here refers to the price the first buyer paid for the item being resold.
2
Understand the proof (dalil)
The text argues via qiyas/istihsan: if the thaman is qimi (unique), the second buyer cannot return an identical item, forcing him to pay an estimated value. Estimation introduces uncertainty (gharar) and raises suspicion of dishonesty, which invalidates these trust-based contracts.
The key principle is avoiding 'shubhat al-khiana' (suspicion of dishonesty), not just actual dishonesty.
3
Distinguish mithli from qimi
Mithli items have measurable units that can be exactly replaced (e.g., gold, wheat). Qimi items are unique (e.g., a specific horse, a slave). Only mithli thaman allows precise performance of the obligation.
Examples of mithli: currencies, grains, standardized goods. Qimi: animals, real estate, art.
4
Apply the exceptions
The text allows Murabahah/Tawliyah with a qimi thaman if the second buyer actually owns the exact item (e.g., the same horse). Then he can return it, eliminating the need for estimation. Also, selling with a profit of 'dah yazdah' (10%) is invalid if thaman is qimi, because the profit would be a fraction of an unknown value.
Exception limits: the second buyer must be the owner of the exact substitute, not just some similar item.
5
Note the practical implication
The mufta bihi position is as stated. This rule ensures that Murabahah and Tawliyah remain transparent and free from uncertainty, which is the basis of their validity.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement on this condition.

مشتری کو وہ بيچ مرابحہ يا توليہ فروخت کرنے کی اجازت نہيں ہے۔ یعنی حامد اس چيز کو ادا کرنے پر قادر ہے جس کا اس نے التزام کيا ہے۔ یعنی بيچ اول میں جو ثمن تھا یعنی گھوڑا حامد اس کو ادا کرنے پر قادر ہے اور اس صورت میں چونکہ نہ خيانت ہے اور نہ شبہ خيانت ہے اس لیے جائز ہے وان باعه بربح ده يازده ... الخ کا حاصل يہ ہے کہ اگر خالد نے يہ غلام حامد کے ہاتھ اس گھوڑے کے عوض اور دوم يازده نفع يعني دس فيصد نفع پر بچا ہو تو يہ مرابحہ نا جائز ہے وہ يازده يا دس فيصد کا مطلب يہ ہے کہ ثمن اول اگر دس درہم ہوں تو نفع ایک درہم ہوگا۔ اور اگر بیس درہم ہوں تو نفع دو درہم ہوگا اور اگر تيس درہم ہوں تو نفع تين درہم ہوں گے اور اگر ثمن اول ایک سو درہم ہوں تو نفع دس درہم ہوں گے وغيرہ ذالک اور يہ نا جائز اس لیے ہے کہ وہ يازده يا دس فيصد نفع اس بات کا تقاضہ کرتا ہے کہ نفع رأس المال یعنی ثمن کی جنس سے ہو کیونکہ نفع ثمن کا دسواں حصہ ہے اور شئی کا دسواں حصہ اس کی جنس سے ہوتا ہے اور اس جگہ ثمن یعنی گھوڑا ذوات الأمثال میں سے نہيں ہے بلکہ ذوات القيم میں سے ہے پس گويا خالد نے يہ غلام حامد کے ہاتھ اس گھوڑے کے عوض ( جو بيچ اول میں ثمن تھا) اور اس کے دسويں حصہ کے عوض فروخت کيا اور گھوڑے کے دسويں حصہ کا تعين قیمت کے ذريعہ ہوگا اور قیمت مجہول ہے پس جب گھوڑے کی قیمت مجہول ہے تو قیمت کا اندازہ کرنے میں خيانت اگر متحقق نہ ہو تو شبہ خيانت ضرور متحقق ہوگا اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ بيچ مرابحہ اور توليہ میں خيانت اور شبہ خيانت دونوں سے احتراز ضروری ہے اس لیے اس صورت میں شبہ خيانت کی وجہ سے بيع مرابحہ نا جائز ہے۔
He said: Murabahah and Tawliyah are not valid until the substitute (thaman) is something that has a like (mithl). Because if it does not have a like, when he owns it, he owns it by value, and it is unknown. And if the buyer sells it as Murabahah to someone who owns that substitute, and he sold it with a profit of a dirham or something of a specified measurable thing, it is permissible, because he is able to fulfill what he undertook. But if he sold it with a profit of ten-eleven (10%), it is not permissible, because he sold it for the capital and part of its value, since it is not from things with likes. Explanation: Al-Quduri says: Murabahah and Tawliyah are permissible only when the thaman is from things with likes (dhawat al-amthal), i.e., measurable things, weighable things, or countable things that are similar. If the thaman is from things of value (dhawat al-qiam), e.g., cloth, animal, or a slave made as thaman, then Murabahah and Tawliyah are not permissible. The proof is that it has passed previously that in Murabahah and Tawliyah, avoidance of both dishonesty (khiana) and suspicion of dishonesty (shubhat al-khiana) is possible. For example, a slave bought for one thousand dinars, then sold to another for eleven hundred dinars, or sold for exactly one thousand dinars; the first is Murabahah, the second Tawliyah, and there is no dishonesty or suspicion. Another example: a slave bought for one hundred sa' of wheat, then sold for one hundred ten sa' or exactly one hundred sa'; that is permissible. In the case of qimiyat, even if dishonesty is avoidable, suspicion of dishonesty is not. For example, someone bought a slave in exchange for a horse, then sold that slave as Murabahah or Tawliyah; the second buyer will estimate the horse's price and pay, because he cannot give the exact horse (he does not own it) nor its like (horses are not mithli). Therefore he pays the value, which is unknown. Thus in such a case, while actual dishonesty may not occur, suspicion of dishonesty is inevitable. Hence we say that if the thaman is from qimiyat, it is not permissible to sell as Murabahah or Tawliyah. 'And if the buyer sold it...' The gist is that if someone buys something for a qimi substitute, then the buyer cannot sell it as Murabahah or Tawliyah. But if the second buyer is the owner of the substitute (i.e., the horse), he can fulfill what he undertook, so it is permissible. And if he sold it with a profit of dah yazdah (10%), it is not permissible because this profit requires that the profit be from the same genus as the capital, but the horse is not mithli; so the tenth of the horse is determined by value, which is unknown, leading to suspicion of dishonesty.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Hidayah regarding the validity of Murabahah and Tawliyah sales. The key condition is that the thaman (price paid by the first buyer) must be from among mithliyat—i.e., items that have standard measures or weights such that a precise like can be determined. The rationale is to avoid both actual dishonesty and the suspicion of dishonesty, which are forbidden in these types of sales because they are built on trust. The text provides two illustrations: one with dinars (mithli) and one with wheat (also mithli) to show permissible cases. Then it contrasts with a scenario where the thaman is a horse (qimi). If the second buyer does not own the exact horse, he must pay its value, which is uncertain, creating suspicion—hence impermissible. However, an exception is made if the second buyer owns the exact horse; then he can return it, eliminating suspicion. The text also discusses the prohibition of selling with a profit of 'dah yazdah' (10%) when the thaman is qimi, because the profit would be a tenth of the value, which is unknown. This lesson underlines the importance of transparency and trust in Murabahah and Tawliyah transactions.

Key Terms
مرابحة (murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the original cost and adds a specified profit; the buyer pays the cost plus profit.
تولية (tawliyah): A sale where the seller transfers the item to the buyer at the same cost without profit.
ذوات الأمثال (dhawat al-amthal): Items that have standard measures or weights such that one unit can be exactly replaced by another of the same kind (e.g., gold, silver, wheat).
ثمن (thaman): The price paid by the first buyer for the item being resold in Murabahah or Tawliyah.
ذوات القيم (dhawat al-qiam): Items that have no standard equivalent; their value is subjective and differs from one unit to another (e.g., animals, real estate).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Murabahah invalid when the thaman is a unique horse?
A) Because the first buyer does not own the horse.
B) Because the second buyer cannot return the exact horse or its like, leading to valuation and suspicion of dishonesty.
C) Because selling at a profit is not allowed in Hanafi fiqh.
D) Because horses are impure animals.

Key Takeaway
Murabahah and Tawliyah require a mithli thaman to avoid uncertainty and suspicion of dishonesty; otherwise, the contract is invalid.
