Adding Expenses to Capital in Murabahah and Tawliyah
Ruling on permissible additions to capital in trust sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which expenses may be added to the capital in Murabahah and Tawliyah and apply the Hanafi principle that custom and value increase justify such additions.

Core Idea
Only expenses that increase the item itself or its value can count as part of the capital in trust sales.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a key practical issue in Murabahah and Tawliyah: what costs can the seller legitimately include in the disclosed capital? Using examples from laundry, dyeing, and transport, the author establishes two tests – custom and value enhancement – to determine permissible additions. Understanding this prevents hidden profits and ensures transparency in these trust-based contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sale type and the issue
Recognise that Murabahah and Tawliyah are trust-based sales where the seller must disclose the capital (ra's al-mal). The question is which expenses can be added to that capital.
In Murabahah, profit is a percentage of capital; in Tawliyah, it's sold at cost.
2
List the permissible expenses from the text
The text explicitly names five expenses: launderer's wage, embroiderer's wage, dyer's wage, rope-twister's wage, and grain transport wage.
3
Extract the two legal justifications
First, custom (urf) among merchants treats these as part of capital. Second, the general principle that any expenditure increasing the sold item (substance) or its value (due to location or enhancement) is attached to capital.
The principle is stated as 'كل ما يزيد فى المبيع اوفى قيمته يلحق به'.
4
Distinguish between substance and value
Dyeing and embroidery physically become part of the item (increase in 'ayn). Transport increases market value because prices vary by location (increase in qima).
This distinction explains why both types of expense are allowed.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Test your understanding: a gemstone is polished (value increase) and placed in a new setting (substance increase). Both can be added. But simply storing it does not count.
Use the criteria: does it enhance the item itself or its market value? Is it customary?

Source Text

ويجوز ان يضيف الى راس المال اجر القصار والطراز و الصبغ والفتل واجرة حمل الطعام لان العرف جار بالحاق هذه الاشياء براس المال فى دعاة التجار ولان كل ما يزيد فى المبيع اوفى قيمته يلحق به هذا هو الاصل وما عددناه بهذه الصفة لان الصبغ واخواته يزيد فى العين والحمل يزيد فى القيمة اذا لقيمة تختلف باختلاف المكان. ترجمہ: اور راس المال میں دھوبی کی اجرت اور نقش و نگار بنانے والے کی اجرت اور رنگ کی اجرت اور رسی باٹنے کی اجرت اور اناج ڈھونے کی اجرت کا ملانا جائز ہے کیونکہ تاجروں کی عادت میں ان چیزوں کو راس المال کے ساتھ ملانے کا عرف جاری ہے اور اس لیے کہ جو چیز بیع میں يا اس کی قیمت میں زيادتی کرے اس کو راس المال کے ساتھ لاحق کيا جائے گا يہی اصل ہے اور جن چیزوں کو ہم نے شمار کيا ہے وہ اسی صفت کی ہيں کیونکہ رنگ اور اس کے مانند چیزیں عين شئی میں اضافہ کرتی ہيں اور بار برداری قیمت میں اضافہ کرتی ہے کیونکہ جگہ بدلنے سے قیمت بدل جاتی ہے۔ تشريح: صاحب قدوري فرماتے ہيں کہ بيع مرابحہ اور بيع توليہ کرتے وقت رأس المال یعنی ثمن کے ساتھ دھوبی کی اجرت ملانا جائز ہے مثلاً ایک تھان ایک سو روپيه میں خریدا پھر دھوبی کو پانچ روپيه اجرت دے کر اس کو دھلايا گيا تو اب مشتری اس تھان کو ایک سو پانچ روپيه پر نفع لے کر مرابحہ يا بغیر نفع لئے ایک سو پانچ روپيه کے عوض توليہ فروخت کر سکتا ہے اسی طرح اگر کپڑے میں پھول بوٹے بنوائے تو اس نقش و نگار کرنے والے کی اجرت کو راس المال کے ساتھ ملانے کی اجازت ہے اسی طرح رنگ کی اجرت ملانا جائز ہے اور اسی طرح پچھلولے باٹنے کی اجرت ملانا جائز ہے مثلاً ایک آدمی نے ایک سو روپيه میں کمبل يا چادر خریدی پھر کسی کو دس روپيه اجرت دے کر اس کے دونوں جانب پھلويے بوايے تو اب اگر يہ شخص مرابحہ يا توليہ کے طور پر بيچنا چاہے تو مرابحہ کی صورت میں ایک سو دس روپيه پر نفع لے گا اور توليہ کی صورت میں ایک سو دس روپيه کے عوض فروخت کرے گا اور اسی طرح ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ اناج ڈھونے کی اجرت کا راس المال کے ساتھ ملانا جائز ہے، مثلاً ایک آدمی نے ديو بند میں دس من گندم دو سو روپيه کے عوض خریدا پھر دس روپيه بار برداری کی اجرت دي کر اس کو سہارنپور میں منتقل کرايا تو اب اگر مشتری سہارنپور میں اس گندم کو مرابحہ يا توليہ فروخت کرنا چاہے تو بار برداری کی اجرت یعنی دس روپيه راس المال کے ساتھ ملا سکتا ہے چنانچہ مرابحہ کی صورت میں دو سو دس روپيه پر نفع لے گا اور توليہ کی صورت میں دو سو دس روپيه کے عوض فروخت کرے گا.
And it is permissible to add to the capital (ra's al-mal) the wage of the launderer, the embroiderer, the dyer, the rope-twister, and the wage for transporting grain, because custom is in operation to attach these things to the capital among merchants. And because everything that increases the sold item or its value is attached to it; this is the principle. And what we have enumerated are of this description, because dye and its like increase the substance, and transport increases the value, as value varies with location. Explanation: Al-Quduri says: When doing Murabahah or Tawliyah, it is permissible to add the launderer's wage to the capital. For example, a cloth bought for one hundred rupees, then laundered for five rupees; the buyer can now sell it as Murabahah at one hundred five plus profit, or as Tawliyah at one hundred five. Similarly for embroidery, dyeing, and rope-twisting. And likewise transport of grain from one place to another; e.g., ten maunds of wheat bought in Deoband for two hundred rupees, then transported to Saharanpur for ten rupees; the buyer can add the transport cost, so Murabahah at two hundred ten plus profit, or Tawliyah at two hundred ten.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Hidayah regarding which expenses may be legitimately added to the capital (ra's al-mal) when selling by Murabahah or Tawliyah. The author enumerates specific expenses: laundering, embroidery, dyeing, rope-twisting, and grain transport. The justification is two-fold: first, the prevalent custom among merchants treats such expenses as part of the capital; second, the underlying principle is that any expenditure that increases the item itself (like dye that becomes part of the cloth) or its value (like transport that changes the location price) can be added. The text distinguishes between 'ayn (substance) and qima (value). Dye physically alters the cloth, while transport changes its market value due to location. The commentary by Al-Quduri provides practical examples with specific numbers (e.g., cloth purchased for 100 rupees, laundering adds 5 rupees, so new capital 105 rupees). This lesson is important for students to understand transparency in disclosing costs in trust-based sales.

Key Terms
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The initial cost of the item plus any permissible expenses that increase its substance or value.
عرف (urf): Customary practice among merchants that is given legal consideration to determine what costs are attached to capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Salary of the seller's employee.

Key Takeaway
In Murabahah and Tawliyah, only costs that increase the item or its value, supported by custom, may be included in the capital.

Suspicion of Deception Invalidates Murabahah
Explaining why a murabahah sale is impermissible due to uncertainty in valuation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why suspicion of deception (shubh khiyanah) invalidates a murabahah sale in the Hanafi school and apply the rule to cases involving non-fungible goods (dhawat al-qiam).

Core Idea
Suspicion of deception in the cost price invalidates murabahah as surely as actual deception.

This passage from Al-Hidayah demonstrates a key Hanafi principle in muamalat: even the mere suspicion of deception in a murabahah contract renders it impermissible. The author uses a detailed scenario involving a horse and a slave to show how uncertainty in valuation leads to shubh khiyanah. We will unpack the reasoning step by step to understand the strict requirement of clarity in the cost price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of sale and its core requirement
Recognize that this is a murabahah sale (cost-plus-profit). The core requirement is that the seller must disclose the exact cost price (ras al-mal) to the buyer.
2
Analyze the nature of the price (thaman) in the scenario
The price originally paid for the slave was a horse (a unique valuable) plus a tenth of something. The horse is not a fungible (dhawat al-amthal) but a non-fungible (dhawat al-qiam). Understand the distinction: fungibles can be exactly replaced, non-fungibles cannot.
Dhawat al-qiam items require market valuation.
3
Understand why dhawat al-qiam creates valuation uncertainty
One-tenth of a horse cannot be paid in kind because the horse is unique. So its value must be estimated by market price. This estimation introduces uncertainty (jahalah) in the cost price.
Uncertainty (jahalah) in the price is a major defect in sales.
4
Link uncertainty to shubh khiyanah and the established rule
Because the cost price is uncertain, there is a suspicion that the seller might misstate the cost, even if no actual deception occurs. The Hanafi school has established that both khiyanah (actual deception) and shubh khiyanah (suspicion of deception) must be avoided in murabahah and tawliyah sales.
The principle was established earlier in the text (pahle guzar chuka).
5
State the final ruling
Therefore, this murabahah sale is impermissible (na ja'iz). The transaction cannot proceed as a murabahah because the necessary clarity of the cost price is absent, leading to shubh khiyanah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہو کیونکہ نفع شمن کا دسواں حصہ ہے اورشی کا دسواں حصہ اس کی جنس سے ہوتا ہے اور اس جگہ شمن یعنی گھوڑ اذوات الا مثال میں سے نہیں ہے بلکہ ذوات القیم میں سے ہے پس گویا خالد نے یہ غلام حامد کے ہاتھ اس گھوڑے کے عوض ( جو بیع اول میں شمن تھا) اور اس کے دسویں حصہ کے عوض فروخت کیا اور گھوڑے کے دسویں حصہ کا عام قیمت کے ذریعہ ہوگا اور قیمت مجہول ہے پس جب گھوڑے کی قیمت مجہول ہے تو قیمت کا اندازہ کرنے میں خیانت اگر متحقق نہ ہو تو شبہ خیانت ضرور متحقق ہوگا اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ بیچ مرابحہ اور تولیہ میں خیانت اور شبہ خیانت دونوں سے احتراز ضروری ہے اس لیے اس صورت میں شبہ خیانت کی وجہ سے بیع مرابحہ نا جائز ہے۔
Because the profit is one-tenth of the price, and one-tenth of a thing is of its own genus. Here, the price (thaman), i.e., the horse, is not from things of similar type (dhawat al-amthal) but from things of value (dhawat al-qiam). So it is as if Khalid sold this slave to Hamid for that horse (which was the price in the first sale) and for one-tenth of it. One-tenth of the horse will be assessed by the general market value, and the price is unknown. When the horse's price is unknown, in estimating the price, if deception (khiyanah) is not certain, suspicion of deception (shubh khiyanah) is certainly present. It has passed earlier that in murabahah and tawliyah sales, both deception and suspicion of deception must be avoided. Therefore, in this case, due to suspicion of deception, the murabahah sale is impermissible.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a demonstration of a ruling applied to a specific scenario. It explains why a murabahah sale is invalid when there is suspicion of deception. The scenario involves a horse being used as part of the price (thaman) for a slave in a previous sale, and then the seller wants to resell the slave on a murabahah basis. Since the horse is a unique valuable (dhawat al-qiam) and not a fungible (dhawat al-amthal), its one-tenth share cannot be precisely valued in kind, leading to uncertainty in the cost price (ras al-mal). This uncertainty creates a suspicion of deception (shubh khiyanah) in the murabahah transaction, which is prohibited. The author refers to the established principle that both actual deception and even its suspicion must be avoided in murabahah and tawliyah sales. Therefore, the sale is ruled impermissible.

Key Terms
شبہ خیانت (shubh khiyanah): Suspicion of deception or breach of trust in the cost price (ras al-mal) of a murabahah contract.
ذوات القیم (dhawat al-qiam): Items that are not fungibles; unique valuable goods whose value varies and cannot be precisely replaced by similar items.
ذوات الامثال (dhawat al-amthal): Fungible items that can be replaced by identical goods in kind, such as grains or currency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the horse was not a valid form of price in the first sale.
B) Because there is suspicion of deception due to the unknown market value of the horse.
C) Because the slave was sold for more than its market value.
D) Because the seller did not specify the profit percentage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi muamalat, even the mere suspicion of deception (shubh khiyanah) renders a murabahah sale impermissible due to the requirement of absolute clarity in the cost price.

Adding Service Wages to Capital in Murabahah: The Role of Custom and Value
Ruling with proof listing permissible expenses for murabahah capital.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which service wages may be added to ras al-mal in murabahah and explain the Hanafi proofs based on custom and the principle of value increase.

Core Idea
Custom and value increase determine which expenses attach to capital in murabahah.

When selling goods on a cost-plus-profit basis (murabahah) or at cost (tawliyah), the seller must clearly state the capital (ras al-mal). But what expenses can legitimately be added to that base? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that wages for specific services—laundering, embroidery, dyeing, rope-twisting, and grain porterage—may be included. The justification rests on two pillars: the established custom of merchants (urf al-tujjar) and the general principle that any expense increasing the item's substance or market value is attached to its capital.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Determine the act under discussion (adding wages to ras al-mal for murabahah/tawliyah) and the hukm level (jā'iz/permissible).
The text lists five specific wages; others are not included by analogy unless they meet the same criteria.
2
Locate the primary proof – custom (urf)
The author cites ongoing custom among merchants as the core evidence. In Hanafi usul, irf (custom) is a legitimate source when no clear text contradicts it.
The Arabic phrase: 'لان العرف جار بالحاق هذه الاشياء براس المال في عادة التجار'.
3
Trace the secondary proof – value increase principle
The text states a general rule: anything that increases the sold item (ayn) or its value (qīmah) is attached to capital. This is a qiyās-like reasoning.
Dyeing increases the substance; transport increases value due to location change.
4
Apply the proofs to the enumerated examples
Match each listed wage to the principle: laundering, embroidery, dyeing, rope-twisting affect the physical item; porterage affects market value.
The commentary provides concrete examples (e.g., cloth bought for 100, laundered for 5, sold at 105 base).
5
Consider the exception and hierarchy
The commentator notes that transport may not always increase value (destination has lower price). Yet custom remains the preferred basis.
This shows that custom (urf) takes precedence over the value-increase principle when they conflict.

راس المال میں دھوبی نقش نگار کرنے والے، رنگ کرنے والے، رسی بٹنے والے اور اناج اگانے والے کی اجرت لگائی جائے گی
ويجوز ان يضيف الى راس المال اجر القصار والطراز و الصبغ والفتل واجرة حمل الطعام لان العرف جار بالحاق هذه الاشياء براس المال في عادة التجار ولان كل ما يزيد في المبيع أو في قيمته يلحق به هذا هو الاصل وما عددناه بهذه الصفة لان الصبغ واخواته يزيد في العين والحمل يزيد في القيمة لان القيمة تختلف باختلاف المكان
ترجمہ اور راس المال میں دھوبی کی اجرت اور نقش و نگار بنانے والے کی اجرت اور رنگ کی اجرت اور رسی باٹنے کی اجرت اور اناج ڈھونے کی اجرت کا ملانا جائز ہے کیونکہ تاجروں کی عادت میں ان چیزوں کو راس المال کے ساتھ ملانے کا عرف جاری ہے اور اس لیے کہ جو چیز بیع میں یا اس کی قیمت میں زیادتی کرے اس کو راس المال کے ساتھ لاحق کیا جائے گا یہی اصل ہے اور جن چیزوں کو ہم نے شمار کیا ہے وہ اسی صفت کی ہیں کیونکہ رنگ اور اس کے مانند چیزیں عین شئی میں اضافہ کرتی ہیں اور بار برداری قیمت میں اضافہ کرتی ہے کیونکہ جگہ بدلنے سے قیمت بدل جاتی ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ بیع مرابحہ اور بیع تولیہ کرتے وقت رأس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ دھوبی کی اجرت ملانا جائز ہے مثلاً ایک تھان ایک سو روپیہ میں خریدا اپھر دھوبی کو پانچ روپیہ اجرت دے کر اس کو دھلایا گیا تو اب مشترکی اس تھان کو ایک سو پانچ روپیہ پر نفع لے کر مرابحہ یا بغیر نفع لئے ایک سو پانچ روپیہ کے عوض تولیہ فروخت کر سکتا ہے اسی طرح اگر کپڑے میں پھول بوٹے بنوائے تو اس نقش و نگار کرنے والے کی اجرت کو راس المال کے ساتھ ملانے کی اجازت ہے اسی طرح رنگ کی اجرت ملانا جائز ہے اور اسی طرح پچھلولے باٹنے کی اجرت ملانا جائز ہے مثلاً ایک آدمی نے ایک سو روپیہ میں کمبل یا چادر خریدی پھر کسی کو دس رو پیدا جرت دے کر اس کے دونوں جانب پھلوے بوائے تو اب اگر یہ شخص مرابحہ یا تولیہ کے طور پر بیچنا چاہے تو مرابحہ کی صورت میں ایک سو دس روپیہ پر نفع لے گا اور تولیہ کی صورت میں ایک سو دس روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کرے گا اور اسی طرح ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ اناج ڈھونے کی اجرت کا راس المال کے ساتھ ملانا جائز ہے، مثلاً ایک آدمی نے دیوبند میں دس من گندم دو سو روپیہ کے عوض خریدا پھر میں روپیہ بار برداری کی اجرت دیکر اس کو سہارنپور میں منتقل کرایا تو اب اگر مشترکی سہارنپور میں اس گندم کو مرابحہ یا تولیہ فروخت کرنا چاہے تو بار برداری کی اجرت یعنی ہیں رو پیدراس المال کے ساتھ ملا سکتا ہے چنانچہ مرابحہ کی صورت میں دوسو میں روپیہ پر نفع لے گا اور تولیہ کی صورت میں دو سو میں رو پہیہ
كے عوض فروخت کرے گا۔ بہر حال بیع مرابحہ اور تولیہ میں رأس المال کے ساتھ دھوبی اور کشیدہ کاری اور رنگ اور پچھلوے ہائے اور اناج دھونے کی اجرت کا ملانا جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ تاجروں کے عرف میں ان چیزوں کی اجرت راس المال کے ساتھ ملانا جائز ہے۔ اور عرف ایک شرعی حجت ہے اس لئے مذکورہ چیزوں کی اجرت کا راس المال کے ساتھ ملنا جائز ہے۔ دوسری دلیل ... جو فقہاء کے یہاں ضابطہ بھی ہے یہ ہے کہ بنو چیز خود بیچ میں یا اس کی قیمت میں زیادتی کرتی ہو اس کو راس المال کے ساتھ ملانا جائز ہے۔ اور جو چیزیں متن میں مذکور ہیں وہ سب اسی صفت کی ہیں کیونکہ رنگ نقش و نگار، پھلوے باشا اور کپڑے کی دھلائی سے عین مبیع میں زیادتی ہوتی ہے اور بار برداری سے قیمت بڑھتی ہے کیونکہ جگہ بدلنے سے قیمت بدل جاتی ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ ایک چیز کی قیمت ایک جگہ کم ہوتی اور دوسری جگہ زیادہ ہوتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کا بیان کردہ ضابطہ اگر چہ درست ہے لیکن کبھی کبھی اس کے خلاف بھی ہو جاتا ہے۔ یعنی ایسا ہوتا ہے کہ جس جگہ سے اناج منتقل کیا گیا ہے وہاں قیمت زیادہ ہوتی ہے اور جس جگہ کی طرف منتقل کیا گیا وہاں قیمت کم ہوتی ہے۔ اب ایسی صورت میں بار برداری کی وجہ سے قیمت کم ہوگی نہ کہ بڑھے گی ۔ پس تاجروں کے عرف کو مبنی قرار دینا انسب اور اولی ہے۔
And it is permissible to add to the capital (ras al-mal) the wage of the launderer, the embroiderer, the dyer, the rope-twister, and the porter of food, because custom (urf) is current in attaching these things to the capital in the practice of merchants, and because everything that increases the sold item or its value is attached to it. This is the principle. What we have enumerated are of this description because dye and its like increase the 'ayn (substance), and carrying increases the value because value varies by location.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning which expenses can be added to the capital (ras al-mal) in murabahah and tawliyah sales. The author lists five specific wages: launderer (dhobi), embroiderer (naqsh o nigar), dyer (rang), rope-twister (pachluwe), and grain porter (anj dhone wala). The proof is based on two principles: first, ongoing custom (urf) among traders allows this addition; second, any expense that increases the very substance (ayn) of the commodity or its market value can be legitimately added. The commentary elaborates with examples: a cloth bought for 100 rupees, then laundered for 5 rupees, can be sold as murabahah on a base of 105 rupees plus profit. Similarly, embroidery, dyeing, and rope-twisting add to the physical item, while transport adds to its value because prices differ by location. The commentator notes that the principle of value increase from transport may sometimes not hold (if the destination has lower prices), but the reliance on custom (urf) is the preferred basis.

Key Terms
راس المال (ras al-mal): The cost price or capital of an item, which serves as the basis for calculating profit in murabahah and tawliyah sales.
عرف (urf): Customary practice, particularly of merchants, which is recognized as a legal basis for adding expenses to the capital in trade transactions.
اجر القصار (ajr al-qassar): The wage paid to a launderer (dhobi) for washing cloth, which can be added to ras al-mal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following expenses can be added to the capital (ras al-mal) in a murabahah sale?
A) The wage of a shepherd for herding livestock.
B) The rental of a storage house for safekeeping the item.
C) The wage of a dyer (sabbagh) for dyeing cloth.
D) The fee for teaching a slave a skill.

Key Takeaway
Only customary wages that increase the item's substance or market value may be added to the capital in murabahah and tawliyah, with custom as the final arbiter.

Proper Wording in Murabahah and Tawliyah: Using 'Qama 'Alay'
Instructing the seller to use truthful phrase 'qama 'alay' not 'ishtaraytu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a seller in murabahah or tawliyah must use the truthful phrase 'qaama 'alay' (it cost me) rather than 'ishtaraytu' (I bought it) to avoid lying, and distinguish between expenses that can and cannot be included in the capital basis.

Core Idea
In murabahah, truth demands: say 'it cost me', not 'I bought it', because the cost includes expenses not part of the purchase.

Honesty is the foundation of Islamic commerce. When selling on murabahah or tawliyah, the seller must disclose the cost basis truthfully. This lesson clarifies the precise wording required by the Hanafi school to avoid falsehood, and explains which additional expenses may be legitimately included in the capital. Understanding this rule protects the transaction from sin and preserves trust between buyer and seller.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling goods on murabahah or tawliyah after adding permissible expenses. The ruling is that the seller must use a truthful phrase that reflects the total cost basis.
2
Distinguish permissible and non-permissible expenses
Expenses that increase the substance or value of the item (like driving sheep, comparable to carrying grain) can be included. Expenses that do not enhance the item's substance or value (shepherd wage, storage rent) cannot. Teaching fee is an exception because it imparts inherent skill (dakawat) that increases value.
3
Apply to a scenario with a written price
If the seller writes a higher price on the goods (e.g., 125 rupees on a 100-rupee purchase) and then sells on that written price with profit, he should not say the goods cost him 125 rupees; instead, he should say 'the goods are written as 125 rupees, I sell with X profit.' This avoids lying about the actual cost.
4
Derive the underlying principle
The principle is that the seller must avoid lying (haram) and must use wording that truthfully reflects the reality. The phrase 'qaama 'alay' encompasses all permissible additions, while 'ishtaraytu' is restricted to the original purchase price.

بائع کن الفاظ کو استعمال کرے
ويقول قام على بكذا ولا يقول اشتريته بكذا كيلا يكون كاذبا وسوق الغنم بمنزلة الحمل بخلاف اجرة الراعى وكراء بيت الحفظ لانه لايزيد فى العين والمعنى وبخلاف اجرة التعليم لان ثبوت الزيادة لمعنى فيه وهو حذاقته
ترجمہ اور یوں کہے ( یہ چیز ) مجھے اتنے میں پڑی ہے اور یہ نہ کہے کہ میں نے اس کو اتنے میں خریدا ہے تا کہ جھوٹا نہ ہو ۔ اور بکریوں کا ہانکنا اناج لادنے کے مرتبہ میں ہے برخلاف چرواہے کی اُجرت اور حفاظت خانہ کے کرایہ کے۔ کیونکہ یہ نہ عین مبیع میں زیادتی کرتا ہے اور نہ قیمت میں زیادتی کرتا ہے اور برخلاف تعلیم کی اجرت کے کیونکہ زیادتی کا ثبوت ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے ہے جو خود مبیع میں ہے اور وہ اس کی ذکاوت ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ جس جگہ راس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ اوپر کا خرچہ ملانے کی اجازت ہے اُس جگہ مرابحہ یا تولیہ فروخت کرتے وقت یہ کہے کہ یہ چیز مجھ کو اتنے روپیوں میں پڑی ہے کیونکہ یہ کہنا صداقت اور سچائی ہے لیکن یہ نہ کہے کہ میں نے یہ چیز اتنے روپیوں میں خریدی ہے کیونکہ جھوٹ ہوگا اور جھوٹ بولنا حرام ہے۔ ہاں اگر کسی نے کوئی سامان ایک سو روپیہ میں خریدا پھر اس سامان پرشمن سے زیادہ مثلاً ایک سو پچیس روپے لکھ دیا پھر اس نے لکھے ہوئے پر مرابحہ کیا مثلا مشتری نے یہ کہا کہ جور قم سامان پر تحریری ہے دس روپیہ نفع کے ساتھ اس کے عوض فروخت کرتا ہوں یعنی ایک سو پینتیس روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کرتا ہوں تو یہ جائز ہے اس صورت میں نہ تو یہ کہے کہ یہ سامان مجھے کو ایک سو پچیس روپیہ میں پڑا ہے اور نہ یہ کہے کہ میں نے ایک سو پچیس روپے کے عوض خربارا ہے کیونکہ یہ دونوں باتیں جھوٹ ہیں ہاں یہ کہے کہ سامان پر ایک سو پچیس روپیہ تحریر میں میں اس پر دس روپیہ نفع لیکر بیچتا ہوں ۔ یہ کہنے میں جھوٹ کا
And he should say, 'It cost me such-and-such,' and should not say, 'I bought it for such-and-such,' so that he is not a liar. Driving sheep is like carrying grain, unlike the wage of a shepherd and the rent of a storage house, because these do not increase the substance or value. And unlike the wage of teaching, because the increase is due to a meaning in the thing itself, which is its sharpness/handicraft.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the proper wording a seller should use when selling as murabahah or tawliyah after adding permissible expenses to the capital. The seller should say 'This item cost me X' (qaama 'alay bi-kadha) rather than 'I bought it for X' (ishtaraytu bi-kadha). This is because the actual purchase price might be lower, and including extra expenses in the capital would make 'ishtaraytu' a lie. The phrase 'qaama 'alay' truthfully reflects the total cost including those added expenses. The text also distinguishes between expenses that can be added (like driving sheep, which is similar to carrying grain) and those that cannot (like shepherd's wage, storage rent, and teaching fee). Teaching fee is an exception because it increases the item's value through a skill (dakawat) inherent in the item itself (e.g., teaching a parrot to speak increases its value). The commentary clarifies a further scenario: if the seller writes a higher price on the item (e.g., 125 rupees on a 100-rupee item) and then sells on that written price with profit, he should say 'I am selling this item written as 125 rupees with 10 rupees profit' rather than claiming the cost was 125.

Key Terms
قام على بكذا (qama 'alay bi-kadha): A truthful phrase meaning 'It cost me such-and-such,' used by the seller in murabahah/tawliyah to indicate the total cost including permissible additions.
اشتريته بكذا (ishtaraytu bi-kadha): The phrase 'I bought it for such-and-such,' which may be false if extra expenses are included in the capital.
ذکاوت (dakawat): Inherent skill or sharpness (e.g., of a trained animal) that increases an item's value, making the teaching fee an exception for inclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a seller say when selling a cloth on murabahah after having it cleaned for an additional cost?
A) I bought this cloth for $100 (the cloth price only).
B) This cloth cost me $105 (including cleaning fee).
C) I bought this cloth for $105 (including cleaning fee).
D) The market value of this cloth is $105.

Key Takeaway
In murabahah/tawliyah, the seller must use a phrase that truthfully reflects the total capital (including permissible additions) and avoid phrases that could be false, to obey the prohibition of lying.

Expenses Includable in Ra's al-Mal: Custom and Increase
Ruling with proof: which expenses can be included in ra's al-mal?

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that expenses increasing the commodity or its price (based on custom) may be included in ra's al-mal for murabahah/tawliyah, and distinguish includable from non-includable expenses.

Core Idea
Custom determines which expenses enter ra's al-mal; only those enhancing commodity or price are includable.

In trust-based sales like murabahah and tawliyah, the seller must truthfully disclose the capital cost. But what qualifies as 'capital'? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on which ancillary expenses may legitimately be added to the original purchase price, drawing on the custom of merchants and a key legal principle that anything increasing the commodity or its value may be included.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is including expenses in ra's al-mal for a murabahah or tawliyah sale. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) for certain expenses.
The ruling applies only when selling as murabahah or tawliyah, not for ordinary sales.
2
Locate the primary proof: custom ('urf)
The text first cites the custom of merchants as a proof. In Hanafi fiqh, established custom ('urf) is a recognized source of law (mujtahad fih).
Custom must be consistent and not contradict a clear text.
3
Identify the secondary proof: the increase principle
The second proof is a principle (qāʿida): any expense that either increases the commodity itself (e.g., dyeing, stitching) or increases its price (e.g., transportation) may be included.
The principle derives from the effect: enhancement of physical or market value.
4
Evaluate the nuance and the role of custom
The commentator notes that the principle may fail (e.g., transportation to a cheaper market reduces price). Hence, relying on custom is more appropriate and preferable (ansab wa awla).
Custom acts as a corrective to the principle when its application yields contradictory results.

بہر حال بیع مرابحہ اور تولیہ میں رأس المال کے ساتھ دھوبی اور کشیدہ کاری اور رنگ اور پچھلوے ہائے اور اناج دھونے کی اجرت کا ملانا جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ تاجروں کے عرف میں ان چیزوں کی اجرت راس المال کے ساتھ ملانا جائز ہے۔ اور عرف ایک شرعی حجت ہے اس لئے مذکورہ چیزوں کی اجرت کا راس المال کے ساتھ ملنا جائز ہے۔ دوسری دلیل ... جو فقہاء کے یہاں ضابطہ بھی ہے یہ ہے کہ بنو چیز خود بیچ میں یا اس کی قیمت میں زیادتی کرتی ہو اس کو راس المال کے ساتھ ملانا جائز ہے۔ اور جو چیزیں متن میں مذکور ہیں وہ سب اسی صفت کی ہیں کیونکہ رنگ نقش و نگار، پھلوے باشا اور کپڑے کی دھلائی سے عین مبیع میں زیادتی ہوتی ہے اور بار برداری سے قیمت بڑھتی ہے کیونکہ جگہ بدلنے سے قیمت بدل جاتی ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ ایک چیز کی قیمت ایک جگہ کم ہوتی اور دوسری جگہ زیادہ ہوتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کا بیان کردہ ضابطہ اگر چہ درست ہے لیکن کبھی کبھی اس کے خلاف بھی ہو جاتا ہے۔ یعنی ایسا ہوتا ہے کہ جس جگہ سے اناج منتقل کیا گیا ہے وہاں قیمت زیادہ ہوتی ہے اور جس جگہ کی طرف منتقل کیا گیا وہاں قیمت کم ہوتی ہے۔ اب ایسی صورت میں بار برداری کی وجہ سے قیمت کم ہوگی نہ کہ بڑھے گی ۔ پس تاجروں کے عرف کو مبنی قرار دینا انسب اور اولی ہے۔

بائع کن الفاظ کو استعمال کرے
ويقول قام على بكذا ولا يقول اشتريته بكذا كيلا يكون كاذبا وسوق الغنم بمنزلة الحمل بخلاف اجرة الراعى وكراء بيت الحفظ لانه لايزيد فى العين والمعنى وبخلاف اجرة التعليم لان ثبوت الزيادة لمعنى فيه وهو حذا قته

ترجمہ اور یوں کہے ( یہ چیز ) مجھے اتنے میں پڑی ہے اور یہ نہ کہے کہ میں نے اس کو اتنے میں خریدا ہے تا کہ جھوٹا نہ ہو ۔ اور بکریوں کا ہانکنا اناج لادنے کے مرتبہ میں ہے برخلاف چرواہے کی اُجرت اور حفاظت خانہ کے کرایہ کے۔ کیونکہ یہ نہ عین مبیع میں زیادتی کرتا ہے اور نہ قیمت میں زیادتی کرتا ہے اور برخلاف تعلیم کی اجرت کے کیونکہ زیادتی کا ثبوت ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے ہے جو خود مبیع میں ہے اور وہ اس کی ذکاوت ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ جس جگہ راس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ اوپر کا خرچہ ملانے کی اجازت ہے اُس جگہ مرابحہ یا تولیہ فروخت کرتے وقت یہ کہے کہ یہ چیز مجھ کو اتنے روپیوں میں پڑی ہے کیونکہ یہ کہنا صداقت اور سچائی ہے لیکن یہ نہ کہے کہ میں نے یہ چیز اتنے روپیوں میں خریدی ہے کیونکہ جھوٹ ہوگا اور جھوٹ بولنا حرام ہے۔ ہاں اگر کسی نے کوئی سامان ایک سو روپیہ میں خریدا پھر اس سامان پرشمن سے زیادہ مثلاً ایک سو پچیس روپے لکھ دیا پھر اس نے لکھے ہوئے پر مرابحہ کیا مثلا مشتری نے یہ کہا کہ جور قم سامان پر تحریری ہے دس روپیہ نفع کے ساتھ اس کے عوض فروخت کرتا ہوں یعنی ایک سو پینتیس روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کرتا ہوں تو یہ جائز ہے اس صورت میں نہ تو یہ کہے کہ یہ سامان مجھے کو ایک سو پچیس روپیہ میں پڑا ہے اور نہ یہ کہے کہ میں نے ایک سو پچیس روپے کے عوض خربارا ہے کیونکہ یہ دونوں باتیں جھوٹ ہیں ہاں یہ کہے کہ سامان پر ایک سو پچیس روپیہ تحریر میں میں اس پر دس روپیہ نفع لیکر بیچتا ہوں ۔ یہ کہنے میں جھوٹ کا مرتکب نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اگر کسی کو کوئی چیز میراث میں ملی یا ہستہ یا صدقہ کے طور پر حاصل ہوئی پھر اس نے اس چیز کی قیمت مقرر کی اور اس قیمت پر نفع لے کر بیچ مرابحہ کی تو یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بکریوں یا دوسرے جانوروں کا ہانکنا بار برداری کے مرتبہ میں ہے یعنی جس طرح بار برداری کے خرچہ کو رأس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ ملانا جائز ہے لیکن جانوروں کو چرانے والے کی اجرت کا جانوروں کے شمن کے ساتھ ملانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح مبیع کی حفاظت کیلئے اگر مکان کرایہ پر لیا ہو تو مکان کا کرایہ بھی شمن کے ساتھ ملانا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں چیزیں نہ تو سبیع کی ذات میں کچھ اضافہ کرتی ہیں اور نہ اس کی قیمت بڑھاتی ہیں۔ حالانکہ یہ دو ہی باتیں راس المال کے ساتھ اوپر کا خرچہ ملانے کا سبب تھیں۔ پس جب یہ دونوں باتیں نہیں پائی گئیں تو چرواہے کی اجرت اور محافظ خانہ کا کرایہ بھی راس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ نہیں ملایا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر غلام فریک ٹیوشن دے کر اس کو تعلیم دلائی تو یہ خرچہ بھی راس المال یعنی غلام کے شمن کے ساتھ نہیں ملایا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں غلام کی مالیت میں زیادتی تو ثابت ہوتی ہے مگر ایسی صفت کی وجہ سے جو خود غلام کے اندر موجود ہے یعنی اس کی ذکاوت اور تعلیم وتعلم کو اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ پتھروں میں چونکہ ذکاوت نہیں ہوتی اسی لئے ان کیلئے تعلیم مفید اور کارآمد نہیں ہوتی۔ ہاں اگر تعلیم کی اجرت کو راس المال کے ساتھ لاحق کرنے پر عرف موجود ہو تو پھر اجرت تعلیم کو غلام کے راس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ لاحق کرنے اور ملانے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
Nevertheless, in a sale of murabahah and tawliyah, it is permissible to include in the capital (ra's al-mal) the wages for washing, carding, dyeing, stitching, and washing grain. The proof is that in the custom of merchants, it is permissible to include the wages for these things with the capital. And custom is a shar'i proof, so including the wages for the mentioned things with the capital is permissible. The second proof... which is also a principle among jurists, is that any thing that increases the commodity itself or its price, it is permissible to include it with the capital. And the things mentioned in the text are all of this description, because dyeing, engraving, stitching, and washing cloth increase the commodity itself, and transportation increases the price because changing place changes the price. For this reason, the price of an item may be low in one place and high in another. The principle stated by the author of al-Hidayah, though correct, sometimes contradicts, i.e., it happens that the place from which grain was transported has a higher price and the destination has a lower price. In such a case, transportation reduces the price, not increases it. So making custom the basis is more appropriate and preferable.

What words should the seller use? And he should say: 'It cost me such and such' and should not say 'I bought it for such and such' so that he is not lying. Driving goats is like loading grain, unlike the wages of a shepherd and the rent of a storage house, because they do not increase the commodity or the price. And unlike the wages of teaching, because the increase is due to a meaning in the commodity itself, which is its intelligence. Commentary: Imam al-Quduri says: Where it is permitted to include additional expenses with the capital (i.e., the price), at the time of selling as murabahah or tawliyah, he should say: 'This item cost me such and such rupees,' because this statement is truthful and honest, but he should not say: 'I bought this item for such and such rupees,' because it would be a lie and lying is haram. Yes, if someone bought goods for one hundred rupees, then wrote more than the price, e.g., one hundred twenty-five rupees, then made a murabahah on the written amount—e.g., the seller said: 'Whatever was written on the goods, I sell it for ten rupees profit, i.e., for one hundred thirty-five rupees'—then it is permissible. In this case, he should neither say 'This item cost me one hundred twenty-five rupees' nor 'I bought it for one hundred twenty-five rupees,' because both are lies. Rather, he should say: 'One hundred twenty-five rupees have been written on the goods; I am selling them with ten rupees profit.' By saying this, he will not commit a lie. And if someone received an item through inheritance or as a gift or as charity, then he set a price for it and sold it as murabahah with profit on that price, this is also permissible. The author of al-Hidayah says: Driving goats or other animals is like transportation, i.e., just as it is permissible to include the cost of transportation with the capital (i.e., the price), but it is not permissible to include the wages of the shepherd with the price of the animals. Similarly, if a place is rented for the protection of the goods, its rent cannot be included with the price, because these two things neither increase the commodity itself nor its price. Yet these two were the causes for including additional expense with the capital. So when these two are absent, the shepherd's wages and the storage rent will not be included with the capital. Similarly, if a slave is taught by giving tuition [?], this expense will not be included with the capital (i.e., the price of the slave), because in this case, the increase in the slave's value is due to a quality inherent in the slave himself, i.e., his intelligence, and teaching and learning have no role in it. For this reason, since stones do not have intelligence, teaching is not useful for them. However, if custom exists to include teaching fees with the capital, then there is no harm in including the teaching fee with the capital (price) of the slave.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah deals with two interrelated issues in murabahah and tawliyah sales: which expenses can be included in the capital cost (ra's al-mal), and what wording the seller should use. The author begins by stating the general principle: expenses that either physically increase the commodity itself (like dyeing, stitching, washing) or increase its price (like transportation) can be added to the capital. The proof is twofold: first, the custom ('urf) of merchants, which is a recognized source of law in the Hanafi school; second, a legal principle (qāʿida) that anything bringing increase to the commodity or its value may be included. However, the author notes a nuance: the principle does not always hold, as transportation might sometimes reduce price if the destination is cheaper. Hence, relying on custom is more appropriate. The second part discusses the seller's statement. To avoid lying, the seller should say 'it cost me such and such' (qāma ʿalayya), not 'I bought it for such and such' (ishtaraytuhu), because the final cost includes additional expenses beyond the purchase price. The passage then distinguishes permissible inclusions from impermissible ones: driving animals (like transport) is allowed, but shepherd's wages and warehouse rent are not, as they neither enhance the commodity nor increase its value. Teaching expenses for a slave are also generally excluded, as any increase in value comes from the slave's innate intelligence, not the teaching itself—unless custom dictates otherwise. Throughout, the commentary emphasizes the role of custom in determining what may be included, showing a practical and context-sensitive approach.

Key Terms
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital or cost price of the goods being sold in a murabahah or tawliyah transaction, including permissible additional expenses.
مرابحة (murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the capital cost and adds an agreed profit amount.
تولية (tawliyah): A sale where the seller transfers the goods to the buyer at exactly the capital cost, without profit.
عرف (urf): Custom or established practice of merchants, used as a legal basis for determining permissible inclusions in ra's al-mal.
ذكاوت (dhaka'): Innate intelligence or quick-wittedness of a slave that allows him to benefit from teaching; considered an inherent quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following expenses is generally includable in ra's al-mal for a murabahah sale?
A) Shepherd's wages for pasturing animals
B) Transportation cost for moving grain
C) Warehouse rent for storing goods
D) Teaching fees for training a slave

Key Takeaway
In murabahah and tawliyah, expenses that customarily enhance the commodity or its value are includable in ra's al-mal; custom is the preferred guide over the strict increase principle.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
7 min
Seller's Declaration in Murabahah and Tawliyah
Ruling with expansion: proper wording for the seller's declaration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct wording a seller should use when declaring the capital cost in murabahah/tawliyah and identify cases where alternative expressions are needed to avoid lying.

Core Idea
Say 'it cost me' not 'I bought it' to truthfully reflect the true cost including permissible expenses.

A critical aspect of trust-based sales is the seller's statement of cost. Using the wrong words can lead to lying, which is haram. This lesson explains the proper declaration and its exceptions based on Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on seller's declaration
The seller must use a truthful expression when stating the cost in murabahah/tawliyah sales. Lying is haram, so the wording must accurately reflect the true capital cost.
This applies only to murabahah and tawliyah, where trust is foundational.
2
Learn the default phrase
The default phrase is 'qāma ʿalayya bi-kadhā' (it cost me such and such). The seller should NOT say 'ishtaraytuhu bi-kadhā' (I bought it for such and such) because the final cost includes additional expenses beyond the purchase price.
Using 'ishtaraytuhu' would be a lie if expenses were added.
3
Recognize exceptions to the default
If the seller wrote a higher price on the goods than what he paid (e.g., added profit or expenses in the invoice), he cannot say 'it cost me' because that would be a lie. Instead, he should say: 'Such amount is written on the goods; I am selling with this profit.' Similarly, for goods received as gift/inheritance, he should set a price and declare it truthfully.
These exceptions protect against falsehood.
4
Distinguish includable expenses in declaration
When declaring, the seller must include only those expenses that are permissible to add (as per Lesson 1). He should say 'It cost me [purchase price + permissible expenses]'.
Non-includable expenses (e.g., shepherd's wages) must not be included in the declared cost.

ایک سو پچیس روپے لکھ دیا پھر اس نے لکھے ہوئے پر مرابحہ کیا مثلا مشتری نے یہ کہا کہ جور قم سامان پر تحریری ہے دس روپیہ نفع کے ساتھ اس کے عوض فروخت کرتا ہوں یعنی ایک سو پینتیس روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کرتا ہوں تو یہ جائز ہے اس صورت میں نہ تو یہ کہے کہ یہ سامان مجھے کو ایک سو پچیس روپیہ میں پڑا ہے اور نہ یہ کہے کہ میں نے ایک سو پچیس روپے کے عوض خربارا ہے کیونکہ یہ دونوں باتیں جھوٹ ہیں ہاں یہ کہے کہ سامان پر ایک سو پچیس روپیہ تحریر میں میں اس پر دس روپیہ نفع لیکر بیچتا ہوں ۔ یہ کہنے میں جھوٹ کا مرتکب نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اگر کسی کو کوئی چیز میراث میں ملی یا ہستہ یا صدقہ کے طور پر حاصل ہوئی پھر اس نے اس چیز کی قیمت مقرر کی اور اس قیمت پر نفع لے کر بیچ مرابحہ کی تو یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بکریوں یا دوسرے جانوروں کا ہانکنا بار برداری کے مرتبہ میں ہے یعنی جس طرح بار برداری کے خرچہ کو رأس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ ملانا جائز ہے لیکن جانوروں کو چرانے والے کی اجرت کا جانوروں کے شمن کے ساتھ ملانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح مبیع کی حفاظت کیلئے اگر مکان کرایہ پر لیا ہو تو مکان کا کرایہ بھی شمن کے ساتھ ملانا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں چیزیں نہ تو سبیع کی ذات میں کچھ اضافہ کرتی ہیں اور نہ اس کی قیمت بڑھاتی ہیں۔ حالانکہ یہ دو ہی باتیں راس المال کے ساتھ اوپر کا خرچہ ملانے کا سبب تھیں۔ پس جب یہ دونوں باتیں نہیں پائی گئیں تو چرواہے کی اجرت اور محافظ خانہ کا کرایہ بھی راس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ نہیں ملایا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر غلام فریک ٹیوشن دے کر اس کو تعلیم دلائی تو یہ خرچہ بھی راس المال یعنی غلام کے شمن کے ساتھ نہیں ملایا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں غلام کی مالیت میں زیادتی تو ثابت ہوتی ہے مگر ایسی صفت کی وجہ سے جو خود غلام کے اندر موجود ہے یعنی اس کی ذکاوت اور تعلیم وتعلم کو اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ پتھروں میں چونکہ ذکاوت نہیں ہوتی اسی لئے ان کیلئے تعلیم مفید اور کارآمد نہیں ہوتی۔ ہاں اگر تعلیم کی اجرت کو راس المال کے ساتھ لاحق کرنے پر عرف موجود ہو تو پھر اجرت تعلیم کو غلام کے راس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ لاحق کرنے اور ملانے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
Nevertheless, in a sale of murabahah and tawliyah, it is permissible to include in the capital (ra's al-mal) the wages for washing, carding, dyeing, stitching, and washing grain. The proof is that in the custom of merchants, it is permissible to include the wages for these things with the capital. And custom is a shar'i proof, so including the wages for the mentioned things with the capital is permissible. The second proof... which is also a principle among jurists, is that any thing that increases the commodity itself or its price, it is permissible to include it with the capital. And the things mentioned in the text are all of this description, because dyeing, engraving, stitching, and washing cloth increase the commodity itself, and transportation increases the price because changing place changes the price. For this reason, the price of an item may be low in one place and high in another. The principle stated by the author of al-Hidayah, though correct, sometimes contradicts, i.e., it happens that the place from which grain was transported has a higher price and the destination has a lower price. In such a case, transportation reduces the price, not increases it. So making custom the basis is more appropriate and preferable.

What words should the seller use? And he should say: 'It cost me such and such' and should not say 'I bought it for such and such' so that he is not lying. Driving goats is like loading grain, unlike the wages of a shepherd and the rent of a storage house, because they do not increase the commodity or the price. And unlike the wages of teaching, because the increase is due to a meaning in the commodity itself, which is its intelligence. Commentary: Imam al-Quduri says: Where it is permitted to include additional expenses with the capital (i.e., the price), at the time of selling as murabahah or tawliyah, he should say: 'This item cost me such and such rupees,' because this statement is truthful and honest, but he should not say: 'I bought this item for such and such rupees,' because it would be a lie and lying is haram. Yes, if someone bought goods for one hundred rupees, then wrote more than the price, e.g., one hundred twenty-five rupees, then made a murabahah on the written amount—e.g., the seller said: 'Whatever was written on the goods, I sell it for ten rupees profit, i.e., for one hundred thirty-five rupees'—then it is permissible. In this case, he should neither say 'This item cost me one hundred twenty-five rupees' nor 'I bought it for one hundred twenty-five rupees,' because both are lies. Rather, he should say: 'One hundred twenty-five rupees have been written on the goods; I am selling them with ten rupees profit.' By saying this, he will not commit a lie. And if someone received an item through inheritance or as a gift or as charity, then he set a price for it and sold it as murabahah with profit on that price, this is also permissible. The author of al-Hidayah says: Driving goats or other animals is like transportation, i.e., just as it is permissible to include the cost of transportation with the capital (i.e., the price), but it is not permissible to include the wages of the shepherd with the price of the animals. Similarly, if a place is rented for the protection of the goods, its rent cannot be included with the price, because these two things neither increase the commodity itself nor its price. Yet these two were the causes for including additional expense with the capital. So when these two are absent, the shepherd's wages and the storage rent will not be included with the capital. Similarly, if a slave is taught by giving tuition [?], this expense will not be included with the capital (i.e., the price of the slave), because in this case, the increase in the slave's value is due to a quality inherent in the slave himself, i.e., his intelligence, and teaching and learning have no role in it. For this reason, since stones do not have intelligence, teaching is not useful for them. However, if custom exists to include teaching fees with the capital, then there is no harm in including the teaching fee with the capital (price) of the slave.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah deals with two interrelated issues in murabahah and tawliyah sales: which expenses can be included in the capital cost (ra's al-mal), and what wording the seller should use. The author begins by stating the general principle: expenses that either physically increase the commodity itself (like dyeing, stitching, washing) or increase its price (like transportation) can be added to the capital. The proof is twofold: first, the custom ('urf) of merchants, which is a recognized source of law in the Hanafi school; second, a legal principle (qāʿida) that anything bringing increase to the commodity or its value may be included. However, the author notes a nuance: the principle does not always hold, as transportation might sometimes reduce price if the destination is cheaper. Hence, relying on custom is more appropriate. The second part discusses the seller's statement. To avoid lying, the seller should say 'it cost me such and such' (qāma ʿalayya), not 'I bought it for such and such' (ishtaraytuhu), because the final cost includes additional expenses beyond the purchase price. The passage then distinguishes permissible inclusions from impermissible ones: driving animals (like transport) is allowed, but shepherd's wages and warehouse rent are not, as they neither enhance the commodity nor increase its value. Teaching expenses for a slave are also generally excluded, as any increase in value comes from the slave's innate intelligence, not the teaching itself—unless custom dictates otherwise. Throughout, the commentary emphasizes the role of custom in determining what may be included, showing a practical and context-sensitive approach.

Key Terms
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital or cost price of the goods being sold in a murabahah or tawliyah transaction, including permissible additional expenses.
مرابحة (murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the capital cost and adds an agreed profit amount.
تولية (tawliyah): A sale where the seller transfers the goods to the buyer at exactly the capital cost, without profit.
عرف (urf): Custom or established practice of merchants, used as a legal basis for determining permissible inclusions in ra's al-mal.
ذكاوت (dhaka'): Innate intelligence or quick-wittedness of a slave that allows him to benefit from teaching; considered an inherent quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A seller received goods as a gift and wants to sell as murabahah. What should he say when declaring the cost?
A) 'I bought this for...'
B) 'It cost me...'
C) 'I value it at...' and then state the profit
D) 'This is a gift; no cost'

Key Takeaway
Truthfulness in declaring the capital cost is essential; using 'qāma ʿalayya' avoids misrepresentation, and exceptions require adapted phrasing.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Buyer's Option on Discovering Fraud in Murabahah and Tawliyah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-khiyanah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on khiyar al-khiyanah in murabahah and tawliyah, and explain the ta'lil (reasoning) behind each position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa distinguishes murabahah (option) from tawliyah (deduction); the Sahibayn differ on uniformity.

In trust-based sales like murabahah and tawliyah, the seller must disclose the true capital cost. If fraud is discovered—meaning the seller misstated the cost—what remedy does the buyer have? This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute among the three primary imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Their differing rulings reveal deep principles about how the nature of a contract determines its legal remedies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State each imam's ruling for murabahah and tawliyah separately. Abu Hanifa: option in murabahah, deduction in tawliyah. Abu Yusuf: deduction in both. Muhammad: option in both.
Note the pattern: Abu Hanifa differentiates, the Sahibayn prefer uniformity.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's ta'lil
Understand why Abu Hanifa differentiates. In tawliyah, the contract requires exact transfer at the first price; any excess changes the transaction, so deduction is mandatory. In murabahah, profit can fluctuate, so the transaction remains murabahah even without deduction; thus an option suffices.
Key concept: 'taghayyur al-tasarruf' (change in the nature of the transaction).
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's ta'lil
Abu Yusuf argues that both sales are fundamentally built on the original price (al-bina' 'ala al-awwal). The contract is concluded by mentioning the first price, so any misrepresentation must be corrected by deduction in both cases.
He sees no difference in the basis of the two contracts.
4
Analyze Muhammad's ta'lil
Muhammad focuses on the naming (al-tasmiyah). Murabahah and tawliyah are desirable descriptions (awṣaf murghab fiha) like safety (salama). When such a description is absent, the buyer has an option to rescind.
This treats the descriptions as independent grounds for khiyar.
5
Examine the practical difference and the delay rule
Note the thamarah al-khilaf: the remedies differ per imam. Also note that if the buyer delays and the goods perish, he is liable for the full price according to zahir al-riwayah, because this khiyar is a 'light option' not equivalent to khiyar al-'ayb.
This rule applies to Muhammad's option view; Abu Hanifa's option in murabahah would also follow this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذہانت مشتری مرابحہ میں خیانت پر مطلع ہو تو بیع نافذ اور نسخ کرنے کا حق ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء فان اطلع المشترى على خيانة فى المرابحه فهو بالخيار عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله ان شاء اخذه بجميع الثمن وان شاء تركه وان اطلع على خيانة في التولية اسقطها من الثمن وقال ابو يوسف يحط فيهما وقال محمد بخير فيهما لمحمد ان الاعتبار للتسمية لكونه معلوما والتولية والمرابحة ترويج وترغيب فيكون وصفا مرغوبا فيه كوصف السلامة فيتخير بفواته ولا بي يوسف ان الاصل فيه كونه تولية ومرابحة ولهذا ينعقد بقوله وليتك بالثمن الاول او بعتك مرابحه على الثمن الأول اذا كان ذالك معلوما فلا بد من البناء على الاول وذالك بالحط غيرانه يحط في التولية قدر الخيانة من راس المال وفي المرابحة منه ومن الربح ولا بى حنيفة انه لولم يحط في التولية لا تبقى تولية لانه يزيد على الثمن الأول فيتغير التصرف فتعين الحط وفى المرابحة لولم يحط تبقى مرابحة وان كان يتفاوت الربح فلا يتغير التصرف فا مكن القول بالتخيير فلو هلک قبل ان يرده او حدث فيه ما يمنع الفسخ يلزمه جميع الثمن في الروايات الظاهرة لانه مجرد خيار لإيقابله شيء من الثمن كخيار الروية والشرط بخلاف خيار العيب لأنه مطالبة بتسليم الفائت فيسقط ما يقابله عند عجزه

ترجمہ. پھر اگر مشتری مرابحہ میں کسی خیانت پر مطلع ہوا تو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک مشتری کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے تو اس کو پورے مشن کے عوض لے لے اور اگر چاہے تو اس کو چھوڑ دے۔ اور اگر تولیہ میں مشتری خیانت پر مطلع ہوا تو مقدار خیانت ثمن سے ساقط کر دے۔ اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ہے کہ مرابحہ اور تولیہ دونوں میں مقدار خیانت کم کر دے اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ دونوں میں مشتری کو اختیار ہے۔
Intelligence? When the buyer discovers fraud in murabahah, then according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) he has the option: if he wishes, he may take it for the entire price, and if he wishes, he may leave it. And if he discovers fraud in tawliyah, he deducts it from the price. Abu Yusuf said: In both cases he deducts. Muhammad said: In both cases he has the option. According to Muhammad, the consideration is the naming (of the price) because it is known, and tawliyah and murabahah are promotion and encouragement, so they are desirable descriptions like the description of safety, so he has the option due to their absence. According to Abu Yusuf, the basis is that it is tawliyah and murabahah, and therefore it is concluded by his saying 'I entrust you with it at the first price' or 'I sell it to you as murabahah on the first price' when that is known. So it must be built on the first, which is by deduction: he deducts in tawliyah the amount of fraud from the capital, and in murabahah from the capital and from the profit. According to Abu Hanifa, if one does not deduct in tawliyah, it would not remain tawliyah because it increases over the first price, thus the transaction changes, so deduction is determined. In murabahah, if one does not deduct, it remains murabahah even if the profit fluctuates; the transaction does not change, so it is possible to say he has the option. If it perishes before he returns it or something occurs that prevents rescission, he is liable for the full price according to the apparent narrations, because it is a mere option not against any part of the price, like the option of inspection and condition, unlike the option of defect because it is a claim for delivering the missing, so its equivalent is reduced when it is impossible.

Translation: Then if the buyer discovers fraud in murabahah, according to Abu Hanifa the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he may take it for the full price, and if he wishes, he may leave it. And if he discovers fraud in tawliyah, he deducts the amount of fraud from the price. Abu Yusuf said: In both murabahah and tawliyah, he deducts the amount of fraud. And Imam Muhammad said: In both, the buyer has the option.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute among the three primary imams regarding the buyer's remedy when he discovers that the seller has committed fraud (khiyanah) in a murabahah or tawliyah sale. Fraud here means the seller has misrepresented the capital cost (e.g., claimed it was higher than actual). The imams differ based on their understanding of the nature of these sales. Abu Hanifa distinguishes between murabahah and tawliyah: in murabahah, the buyer has khiyar al-khiyanah (option due to fraud) to either take the goods at the agreed price or return them; in tawliyah, the buyer must automatically deduct the fraudulent amount from the price. The reasoning is that tawliyah requires exact transfer at the first price; any excess changes the nature, so deduction is necessary to preserve the contract. In murabahah, the transaction can accommodate profit fluctuation, so the option is suitable. Abu Yusuf holds that in both cases, deduction is the proper remedy, as the contract is built on the original price. Muhammad holds that in both, the buyer has the option (takhyir), because the naming of the price is the critical element, and the description of being a murabahah/tawliyah is a desirable attribute like safety; its absence gives an option. The passage also notes that if the buyer delays and the goods perish or a bar to rescission occurs before he exercises his option, he must pay the full price according to the apparent narrations (zahir al-riwayah), because this is a pure option that does not correspond to any part of the price, unlike the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb).

Key Terms
خیانة (khiyanah): Fraud or misrepresentation by the seller regarding the capital cost (ra's al-mal) in a trust-based sale (murabahah/tawliyah).
خيار (khiyar): An option or right of choice given to a party in a contract, here specifically the buyer's option to accept or rescind upon discovering fraud.
مرابحة (murabahah): A sale with disclosure of cost and profit; the seller states the capital cost and adds a profit margin.
تولية (tawliyah): A sale where the goods are transferred at exactly the capital cost, without profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the buyer's remedy upon discovering fraud in a murabahah sale?
A) Automatic deduction of the fraud amount from the price
B) The buyer has an option to take the goods at the agreed price or return them
C) The sale becomes void automatically
D) The buyer must pay the true capital cost plus profit

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between murabahah and tawliyah based on whether the contract can accommodate the fraud without changing its nature; the Sahibayn each offer a uniform remedy based on different principles.

Expenses Not Added to Capital in Murabahah
Ruling on expenses not added to capital in murabahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between expenses that may be added to ra's al-mal in murabahah and those that may not, applying the Hanafi principle of value enhancement.

Core Idea
Only expenses that increase value or substance may be added; preservation costs and training fees (absent custom) cannot.

In a murabahah transaction, transparency requires disclosing the original cost. But which costs count? The Hanafi school distinguishes between expenses that add to the item's value or substance—like transport—and those merely preserving it—like storage. This lesson explores the Hidayah's examples and the role of custom (urf) in exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Recognize that expenses may be added to ra's al-mal only if they increase the item's substance (ayn) or value (qimah).
This is the core criterion from the passage.
2
Analyze the examples
Examine the three prohibited examples: herding wages, storage rent, and slave tuition (default). Understand why each fails the criterion.
Porterage is allowed because it brings the item to market, increasing value.
3
Understand the rationale for tuition
Tuition increases value due to the slave's inherent intelligence, not the tutor's effort; hence it is not added unless custom ('urf) treats it as part of the cost.
Custom can overrule the default when it is established.
4
Apply to new expenses
Given a novel expense (e.g., insurance, quality control), determine if it enhances value or merely preserves, and state the ruling.
This tests your grasp of the distinction.
5
Note the exception for custom
If a local custom treats a normally excluded expense as part of the cost, it may be added. Custom is recognized in Hanafi mu'amalat.
Custom must be widespread and not contradict a clear text.

مرتکب نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اگر کسی کو کوئی چیز میراث میں ملی یا ہستہ یا صدقہ کے طور پر حاصل ہوئی پھر اس نے اس چیز کی قیمت مقرر کی اور اس قیمت پر نفع لے کر بیچ مرابحہ کی تو یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بکریوں یا دوسرے جانوروں کا ہانکنا بار برداری کے مرتبہ میں ہے یعنی جس طرح بار برداری کے خرچہ کو رأس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ ملانا جائز ہے لیکن جانوروں کو چرانے والے کی اجرت کا جانوروں کے شمن کے ساتھ ملانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح مبیع کی حفاظت کیلئے اگر مکان کرایہ پر لیا ہو تو مکان کا کرایہ بھی شمن کے ساتھ ملانا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں چیزیں نہ تو سبیع کی ذات میں کچھ اضافہ کرتی ہیں اور نہ اس کی قیمت بڑھاتی ہیں۔ حالانکہ یہ دو ہی باتیں راس المال کے ساتھ اوپر کا خرچہ ملانے کا سبب تھیں۔ پس جب یہ دونوں باتیں نہیں پائی گئیں تو چرواہے کی اجرت اور محافظ خانہ کا کرایہ بھی راس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ نہیں ملایا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر غلام فریک ٹیوشن دے کر اس کو تعلیم دلائی تو یہ خرچہ بھی راس المال یعنی غلام کے شمن کے ساتھ نہیں ملایا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں غلام کی مالیت میں زیادتی تو ثابت ہوتی ہے مگر ایسی صفت کی وجہ سے جو خود غلام کے اندر موجود ہے یعنی اس کی ذکاوت اور تعلیم وتعلم کو اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ پتھروں میں چونکہ ذکاوت نہیں ہوتی اسی لئے ان کیلئے تعلیم مفید اور کارآمد نہیں ہوتی۔ ہاں اگر تعلیم کی اجرت کو راس المال کے ساتھ لاحق کرنے پر عرف موجود ہو تو پھر اجرت تعلیم کو غلام کے راس المال یعنی شمن کے ساتھ لاحق کرنے اور ملانے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
He will not commit sin. And if someone inherits something, or obtains it as a gift or charity, then sets its price and sells it via murabahah with profit on that price, that too is permissible. The author of al-Hidayah says: Driving goats or other animals is like the category of porterage, i.e., just as adding porterage expense to the capital (price) is permissible, but adding the wage of a herdsman to the price of the animals is not permissible. Similarly, if a house is rented for the protection of the sold item, the rent of the house cannot be added to the price. Because these two things neither add to the substance of the sold item nor increase its value, whereas these two matters were the reason for adding additional expense to the capital. So when these two matters are not found, the wage of the herdsman and the rent of the protective house will not be added to the capital (price). Similarly, if a slave is given private tuition, this expense will also not be added to the capital (price of the slave), because in this case the slave's value does increase, but due to a quality inherent in the slave himself (his intelligence); the teaching/learning has no role. This is why stones, since they do not have intelligence, teaching is not useful and effective for them. However, if there is a custom (urf) of adding the tuition fee to the capital, then there is no objection to adding the tuition fee to the slave's capital (price).
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement clarifying which expenses can legitimately be added to the capital sum (ra's al-mal) when reselling an item via murabahah. The ruling: expenses that increase the item's value or add to its substance (like porterage) may be incorporated; those that merely preserve or maintain the item (like herding fees, rent for storage) cannot. Similarly, tuition for a slave does not warrant addition because the value increase arises from the slave's innate intelligence, not from the tutor's effort. However, an exception exists: if local custom ('urf) treats such tuition fees as part of the cost, then inclusion is permitted. This demonstrates the Hanafi reliance on 'urf as a secondary source of law.

Key Terms
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The original cost or price of the item being sold in a murabahah transaction; the base upon which profit is calculated.
مرابحة (murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the original cost and adds a specified profit margin.
عرف ('urf): Custom or prevailing practice that can legitimize adding certain expenses to the capital in murabahah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can the tuition fee for a slave not be added to the capital in a murabahah sale?
A) Because tuition does not increase the slave's value at all.
B) Because the value increase is due to the slave's inherent intelligence, not the tutor's effort.
C) Because tuition is not a recognized expense in Hanafi law.
D) Because the slave must consent to the tuition.

Key Takeaway
In murabahah, only expenses that enhance the item's value or substance may be added to ra's al-mal; preservation costs and training fees (absent custom) are excluded.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Buyer's Option Upon Discovering Dishonesty in Murabahah and Tawliyah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on buyer's khiyar upon discovering dishonesty in murabahah and tawliyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the buyer's khiyar when fraud is discovered in murabahah and tawliyah, evaluate their proofs, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
In fraud cases, Abu Hanifa distinguishes between murabahah (option) and tawliyah (deduction); the Sahibayn differ.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the buyer's remedy when the seller cheats by misstating the original cost in a trust-based sale. The debate hinges on the nature of the contract: does fraud affect the essence of the transaction or only the description? Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply khiyar rules in commercial contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract types
Recognize the two trust-based sales: murabahah (profit disclosed) and tawliyah (cost without profit). The passage deals with khiyanah (dishonesty) in both. The buyer discovers the seller understated the actual cost.
In murabahah, the seller declares cost + profit; in tawliyah, only cost.
2
State the three imams' positions
For each, identify whether the remedy is an option (khiyar) or mandatory deduction (hittah). Abu Hanifa: option in murabahah, deduction in tawliyah. Abu Yusuf: deduction in both. Muhammad: option in both.
This forms the core ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the proofs for each position
Examine the reasoning given in the text. Abu Hanifa argues that in tawliyah, not deducting would change the transaction's nature (price exceeds cost), while murabahah remains even with uneven profit. Abu Yusuf says the contract is built on the first price, so deduction restores it. Muhammad says the stated price is the binding element, and murabahah/tawliyah are mere descriptions like a warranty.
Each imam's dalil focuses on a different aspect: contractual nature, reliance on original cost, or primacy of stated price.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Compare the outcomes for a buyer in each scenario. Under Abu Hanifa's view, a murabahah buyer can walk away; a tawliyah buyer can only claim reduction. Under Abu Yusuf, both buyers get reduction. Under Muhammad, both buyers have the full option.
The difference matters for the buyer's negotiating power.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Identify which view is relied upon in the school. The text presents Abu Hanifa's view first and Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah supports it. Later Hanafi fatwa adopts Abu Hanifa's distinction.
This is the operative position for fatwa.
