اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہشتم

اور اگر خالد نے کپڑے کا تھان دس روپیہ میں خرید کر اس پر قبضہ کرنے کے بعد حامد کو بیس روپیہ کے عوض بیع مرابحہ کے طور پر فروخت کیا اور حامد نے مبیع یعنی تھان اور خالد نے ثمن یعنی بیس روپیہ پر قبضہ کر لیا پھر خالد نے حامد سے وہی تھان دس روپیہ کے عوض خرید کر قبضہ کر لیا اب اگر خالد اس تھان کو مرابحہ بیچنا چاہے تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس تھان کو مرابحہ بیچنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے کیونکہ بیع سابق میں خالد نے دس روپیہ کا جو نفع حاصل کیا ہے اس کو کم کرنے کے بعد ثمن باقی نہیں رہتا اور جب ثمن باقی نہیں رہا تو مرابحہ کس چیز پر کرے گا۔ ہاں اگر خالد یہ تفصیل بیان کر دے کہ میں اس تھان کو ایک بار بیچ کر دس روپیہ کا نفع حاصل کر چکا ہوں۔ اب دوبارہ دس روپیہ پر اس قدر نفع لے کر فروخت کرتا ہوں تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نفع ثمن کو گھیرے یا نہ گھیرے دونوں صورتوں میں بغیر تفصیل بیان کئے دس روپیہ پر بیع مرابحہ کر سکتا ہے یعنی دس روپیہ پر نفع متعین کر کے بیچ سکتا ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دوسری بیع یعنی خالد کا حامد سے دس روپیہ کے عوض خریدنا ایک نیا عقد ہے جس کے احکام عقد اول سے بالکل جدا ہیں اور جب عقد ثانی یعنی شراء ثانی کے احکام عقد اول سے جدا ہیں تو عقد ثانی پر مرابحہ کو مبنی کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے یعنی عقد ثانی پر مرابحہ کیا جا سکتا ہے یعنی خالد دس روپیہ پر نفع لے کر تھان فروخت کر سکتا ہے جیسا کہ جب تیسرا آدمی درمیان میں آ گیا ہو۔ مثلاً خالد نے ایک تھان دس روپیہ کا خرید کر بیع مرابحہ کے طور پر پندرہ روپیہ کے عوض حامد کو بیچ دیا پھر حامد نے پچیس روپیہ کے عوض شاہد کے ہاتھ بیچ دیا پھر خالد نے شاہد سے دس روپیہ کے عوض خرید لیا تو اب اگر خالد دس روپیہ پر مرابحہ کر کے بیچنا چاہے تو بالاتفاق جائز ہے۔ پس اسی طرح اگر خالد حامد سے دس روپیہ کا خرید کر دس روپیہ پر مرابحہ کرنا چاہے تو جائز ہے یعنی دس روپیہ پر نفع لے کر بیچ سکتا ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو نفع عقد اول کی وجہ سے حاصل ہوا ہے یعنی جب خالد نے دس روپیہ کا تھان خرید کر پندرہ روپیہ میں حامد کو بیچا تو اس عقد کی وجہ سے خالد کو پانچ روپیہ کا نفع ہوا اور اس نفع کے حصول کا شبہ عقد ثانی سے بھی ثابت ہے یعنی جب خالد نے اس تھان کو اپنے مشتری یعنی حامد سے دس روپیہ میں خرید لیا تو وہ پانچ روپیہ جو خالد کو نفع میں ملا ہے گویا عقد ثانی سے ثابت ہوا۔ کیونکہ عقد ثانی سے پہلے اس کے ساقط ہونے کا امکان ہے اس طور پر کہ حامد اگر بیع یعنی تھان کے کسی عیب پر مطلع ہو جائے اور خیار عیب کی وجہ سے تھان خالد کو واپس کر دے اور اپنے پندرہ روپیہ لے لے تو خالد کو جو پانچ روپیہ کا نفع حاصل ہو رہا تھا وہ ساقط ہو جائے گا لیکن جب خالد نے مذکورہ تھان حامد سے دس روپیہ کے عوض خرید لیا ہے تو پانچ روپیہ کا نفع خالد کے لیے مستحکم اور مؤکد ہو گیا۔ پس پانچ روپیہ کا نفع حقیقۃ تو عقد اول سے حاصل ہوا ہے مگر چونکہ عقد ثانی سے اس کا استحکام ہوا ہے اس لئے شبہ عقد ثانی سے بھی ثبوت ہوگا۔ اور جب عقد ثانی سے شبہ اس نفع یعنی پانچ روپیہ کا حصول ہوا ہے تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا کہ خالد نے حامد سے دس روپیہ کے عوض کپڑے کا ایک تھان اور پانچ روپیہ خریدے میں۔ پس پانچ روپیہ کے مقابلہ میں تو پانچ روپیہ ہو گئے اور کپڑے کا تھان پانچ روپیہ کے عوض رہا۔ اور جب کپڑے کا تھان پانچ روپیہ کے عوض رہا تو خالد پانچ روپیہ پر مرابحہ کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ دس روپیہ پر مرابحہ کرنے کی صورت میں خیانت کا شبہ ہوگا۔ حالانکہ بیع مرابحہ میں احتیاطاً شبہ خیانت حقیقت خیانت کے مانند ہوتا ہے۔ پس بیع مرابحہ میں جس طرح حقیقت خیانت سے احتراز ضروری ہے اسی طرح شبہ خیانت سے بھی احتراز ضروری ہے۔ اسی احتیاط کی وجہ سے اگر کوئی چیز صلح کر کے لی گئی ہو تو اس کو مرابحہ بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے مثلاً شاکر کے قاسم پر دس روپیہ قرضہ ہیں پس قاسم نے ایک کپڑے پر صلح کر لی یعنی بجائے دس روپیہ کے ایک کپڑا شاکر کو دے دیا اب اگر شاکر اس کپڑے کو دس روپیہ پر نفع لے کر بیچنا چاہے تو جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ صلح بالعموم دام گھٹا کر کی جاتی ہے پس اس میں یہ شبہ ہو گیا کہ کپڑا دس روپیہ کا نہ ہو بلکہ دس روپیہ سے کم کا ہو تو اس شبہ سے بچنے کے لئے اس کپڑے کو مرابحہ بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف جب درمیان میں تیسرا آدمی پڑ گیا ہو یعنی خالد نے حامد کو بیچا اور حامد نے کسی اور کو بیچا اور اس سے خالد نے خریدا تو اس صورت میں خالد کو جو پانچ روپیہ کا نفع ہوا ہے اس کا استحکام تیسرے آدمی کے خریدنے سے ہوا ہے خالد کو یہ نفع شراء ثانی سے حاصل نہیں ہوا۔ پس جب اس نفع کا ثبوت شراء ثانی سے نہیں ہوا تو خیانت کا شبہ بھی منفی ہو گیا۔ اور جب خیانت کا شبہ منفی ہو گیا تو خالد کپڑے کا تھان دس روپیہ پر مرابحہ کر کے فروخت کر سکتا ہے۔
Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 8. And if Khalid bought a bolt of cloth for ten rupees, and after taking possession, sold it to Hamid as a murabahah sale for twenty rupees, and Hamid took possession of the sold item (the bolt) and Khalid took possession of the price (twenty rupees), then Khalid bought that same bolt from Hamid for ten rupees and took possession. Now if Khalid wants to sell that bolt as murabahah: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he is not permitted to sell it as murabahah, because the profit of ten rupees that Khalid obtained from the previous sale, after deducting it, no price (thaman) remains; and when no price remains, on what basis will he do murabahah? Yes, if Khalid explains that he already earned ten rupees profit from selling it once, and now he is selling it again with that much profit on ten rupees, then it is permissible. According to the Sahibayn, regardless of whether the profit encircles the price or not, in both cases he can do murabahah on ten rupees without explaining the details, i.e., he can fix a profit on ten rupees and sell. The proof of the Sahibayn is that the second sale (Khalid's purchase from Hamid for ten rupees) is a new contract whose rulings are completely separate from the first contract. And when the rulings of the second contract (the second purchase) are separate from the first contract, then there is no harm in basing murabahah on the second contract, i.e., murabahah can be done on the second contract. So Khalid can sell the cloth with profit on ten rupees, just like when a third person intervened. For example: Khalid bought a bolt for ten rupees and sold it as murabahah to Hamid for fifteen rupees, then Hamid sold it to Shahid for twenty-five rupees, then Khalid bought it from Shahid for ten rupees. Now if Khalid wants to sell it as murabahah on ten rupees, it is unanimously permissible. Similarly, if Khalid bought it from Hamid for ten rupees and wants to do murabahah on ten rupees, it is permissible, i.e., he can sell with profit on ten rupees. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the profit obtained from the first contract (when Khalid bought the bolt for ten and sold to Hamid for fifteen, he made five rupees profit) and the suspicion of that profit's acquisition is also established from the second contract. Because before the second contract, it was possible for that profit to be nullified if Hamid had discovered a defect and returned the cloth taking back his fifteen rupees, but when Khalid bought the cloth from Hamid for ten rupees, the five rupees profit became firmly established and confirmed for Khalid. So the five rupees profit, in reality, was obtained from the first contract, but since its confirmation came from the second contract, there is a suspicion (shubha) of establishment from the second contract as well. And when the profit is obtained from the second contract by suspicion, it becomes as if Khalid bought from Hamid a bolt of cloth and five rupees for ten rupees. So in exchange for five rupees, there are five rupees, and the cloth remains for five rupees. And when the cloth remains for five rupees, Khalid can do murabahah on five rupees. Because if he does murabahah on ten rupees, there will be suspicion of dishonesty (khiyanah). Whereas in a murabahah sale, precautionarily, the suspicion of dishonesty is like actual dishonesty. Therefore, just as actual dishonesty must be avoided in murabahah, so too must the suspicion of dishonesty be avoided. For the same precautionary reason, if something is acquired through sulh (compromise), selling it as murabahah is not permissible. For example, Shakir has a debt of ten rupees on Qasim. Qasim made sulh with a cloth, i.e., he gave Shakir a cloth instead of ten rupees. Now if Shakir wants to sell that cloth with profit on ten rupees, it is not permissible because sulh is generally made by reducing the price. So there arises a suspicion that the cloth is not worth ten rupees but less. To avoid this suspicion, selling that cloth as murabahah is not permissible. On the contrary, when a third person intervened, i.e., Khalid sold to Hamid, and Hamid sold to someone else, and Khalid bought from that someone, then the five rupees profit that Khalid obtained became confirmed through the purchase by the third person; Khalid did not obtain this profit from the second purchase. So when the profit is not established from the second purchase, the suspicion of dishonesty is negated. And when the suspicion of dishonesty is negated, Khalid can sell the bolt as murabahah on ten rupees.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical ruling in the Hanafi madhhab regarding murabahah sales. It presents an intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) on whether a seller can resell an item via murabahah at the original cost after repurchasing it from the same buyer at a lower price. The scenario: Khalid buys cloth for 10, sells to Hamid via murabahah for 20 (cost + profit), then repurchases it from Hamid for 10. Now Khalid wants to sell it again as murabahah. Abu Hanifa says no, because the initial profit (10) must be deducted, leaving no basis for the cost; but if Khalid discloses the previous profit, it's permissible. The Sahibayn say yes, because the second purchase is a new contract, independent of the first. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is subtle: the profit from the first sale is potentially revocable (e.g., due to defect) until the second purchase confirms it. Thus, the second purchase creates a suspicion that the profit is part of the new price, making the effective cost only 5 (10 paid minus 5 profit returned). Selling on 10 would imply dishonesty. The Sahibayn analogize to a third party intervening, where repurchase from a stranger removes the suspicion. The passage also illustrates the principle that in murabahah, even suspicion of dishonesty is prohibited, similar to actual dishonesty. This is supported by the analogy with sulh, where a compromise settlement may involve a hidden reduction, making murabahah impermissible without disclosure.

Key Terms
مرابحہ (murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the original cost and adds a specified profit; the buyer pays cost plus profit.
شبہ خیانت (shubhah khiyanah): Suspicion of dishonesty; in murabahah, even a reasonable suspicion that the seller is not truthful about the cost or profit is treated like actual dishonesty.
شراء ثانی (shira' thani): Second purchase; the act of buying back an item from the same person to whom it was previously sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why can Khalid not sell the cloth as murabahah on ten rupees after repurchasing it from Hamid for ten rupees?
A) Because the second purchase is invalid due to lack of possession.
B) Because the profit from the first sale is confirmed by the second purchase, reducing the effective cost and creating suspicion of dishonesty.
C) Because the cloth is no longer in the same condition.
D) Because the price fluctuated between the two transactions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's ikhtilaf on murabahah after repurchase from the same buyer hinges on whether the second contract is truly independent or whether it reinforces a prior profit, with the mufta bihi ruling following the Sahibayn but caution favouring disclosure.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Murabahah with a Ma'dhun Slave: The Effect of Overwhelming Debt
Ruling on murabahah with a ma'dhun slave in debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on murabahah when a ma'dhun slave with overwhelming debt sells to or buys from his master, and explain the rationale of shubhat al-'adam.

Core Idea
For murabahah, a sale tainted by legal suspicion is treated as non-existent; only the original cost counts.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in murabahah involving a ma'dhun slave who is heavily in debt. According to the Hanafi school, such a slave is effectively owned by creditors, not his master. Consequently, any trade between master and slave, though valid in reality, is disregarded for murabahah purposes due to the concept of shubhat al-'adam (suspicion of non-existence). The murabahah must be based on the original acquisition price from a third party, not the price exchanged between master and slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the transaction
Note that the slave is ma'dhun (permitted to trade) and carries debt that encompasses his entire value. The transaction is a sale between the master and the slave (in either direction).
The slave's overwhelming debt is the key factor.
2
Determine the legal status of the slave's person
Because the debt covers the slave's full value, the slave becomes the right of the creditors, not the master. Thus the master does not truly own the slave or his actions.
This is a rational (aqli) proof based on the effect of the debt.
3
Apply the concept of shubhat al-'adam
Although the sale between master and slave is valid in reality (haqiqatan jaa'iz), the existence of a contradictory element (the slave's transfer to creditors) creates a suspicion of non-existence. For murabahah – which requires transparency – this sale is considered non-existent.
This is a ruling specific to murabahah, not to the contract itself.
4
Derive the murabahah basis
Since the later sale is disregarded, the murabahah must be based on the original cost at which the slave or master acquired the item from a third party. In both scenarios (slave to master or master to slave), the basis is the first price (10 dirhams).
The practical result: the seller cannot claim a higher cost than the original acquisition price.

عبد مأذون فی التجارة نے کپڑا دس درہم میں خریدا اور اس پر اتنا دین ہے کہ اس کی رقبہ کو محیط ہے مولیٰ کو پندرہ درہم کا بیچ دیا تو مولیٰ کتنے پر مرابحہ بیچ سکتا ہے
قال واذا اشترى العبد الماذون له فى التجارة ثوبا بعشرة وعليه دين يحيط برقبته فباعه من المولى بخمسة عشر فانه يبيعه مرابحة على عشرة وكذلك ان كان المولى اشتراه فباعه من العبد لان في هذا العقد شبهة العدم لجوازه مع المنافى فاعتبر عدما في حكم المرابحة وبقى الاعتبار للاول فيصير كان العبد اشتراه للمولى بعشرة في الفصل الاول وكانه يبيعه للمولى فى الفصل الثاني فيعتبر الثمن الاول
ترجمہ: اور اگر غلام مأذون لہ فی التجارة نے ایک تھان دس درہم کے عوض خریدا حالانکہ اس غلام پر اس قدر قرضہ ہے کہ اس کی ذات کو محیط ہے پھر اس غلام نے یہ تھان اپنے مولیٰ کے ہاتھ پندرہ درہم کے عوض فروخت کیا تو مولیٰ اس تھان کو دس درہم پر مرابحہ کر کے بیچ سکتا ہے اور اسی طرح اگر مولیٰ نے اس تھان کو خریدا ہو پھر اپنے غلام مأذون لہ فی التجارة کے ہاتھ پندرہ درہم کے عوض فروخت کیا ہو کیونکہ اس عقد میں (جو مولیٰ اور اس کے غلام مأذون میں ہوا ہے) نہ ہونے کا شبہ ہے کیونکہ یہ عقد منافی کے ساتھ جائز ہے پس مرابحہ کے حکم میں اس بیع کو معدوم شمار کیا گیا اور بیع اول کا اعتبار باقی رہ گیا پس پہلی صورت میں ایسا ہو گیا گویا غلام نے اس تھان کو دس درہم کے عوض مولیٰ کے واسطے خریدا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں گویا غلام مأذون اس تھان کو مولیٰ کے واسطے فروخت کرتا ہے پس پہلا ثمن معتبر ہوگا۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر غلام مأذون لہ فی التجارة نے ایک تھان دس روپیہ کے عوض خریدا اور غلام مأذون پر لوگوں کا اس قدر قرضہ ہے کہ وہ اس کے رقبہ کی پوری مالیت کا احاطہ کر لیتا ہے پھر اس غلام مأذون نے یہ تھان اپنے مولیٰ کے ہاتھ پندرہ روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کیا تو مولیٰ اس تھان کو دس روپیہ پر مرابحہ کر کے فروخت کر سکتا ہے، پندرہ روپیہ پر بیع مرابحہ کرنے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی۔ اسی طرح اگر مولیٰ نے ایک تھان دس روپیہ کے عوض خرید کر اپنے غلام مأذون لہ فی التجارة کے ہاتھ پندرہ روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کیا تو غلام مأذون اس تھان کو دس روپیہ پر مرابحہ کر کے فروخت کر سکتا ہے، پندرہ روپیہ پر مرابحہ کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس عقد میں غلام کے مولیٰ کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنے میں اور مولیٰ کے غلام کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنے میں بیع جائز نہ ہونے کا شبہ ہے حقیقتاً جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ حقیقتاً بیع جائز ہے۔ اور حقیقتاً اس لئے جائز ہے کہ جب غلام دین محیط کے ساتھ مدیون ہے تو غلام قرض خواہوں کا حق ہوا اور جب غلام قرض خواہوں کا حق ہوا تو گویا یہ غلام اپنے مولیٰ کی ملک نہ رہا بلکہ قرض خواہوں کی ملک ہو گیا۔
A ma'dhun slave in trade bought a cloth for ten dirhams and he has a debt that encompasses his person (value). He sold it to the master for fifteen dirhams. Then the master can sell it as murabahah on ten (dirhams). Similarly, if the master bought it and sold it to the slave, because in this contract there is a suspicion of non-existence (shubhat al-'adam) due to its permissibility despite a contradictory element. So it is considered non-existent in the ruling of murabahah, and the consideration remains for the first. So it becomes as if the slave bought it for the master for ten in the first case, and as if he sells it for the master in the second case. Thus the first price is considered.

Translation: And if a ma'dhun slave in trade bought a bolt for ten dirhams, while he has a debt that encompasses his entire person, then he sold that bolt to his master for fifteen dirhams, then the master can sell that bolt as murabahah on ten dirhams. Similarly, if the master bought the bolt and then sold it to his ma'dhun slave for fifteen dirhams. Because in this contract (between master and his ma'dhun slave) there is a suspicion of non-existence, since this contract is permissible with a contradictory element. So in the ruling of murabahah, this sale is considered non-existent, and the first sale remains considered. So in the first case, it becomes as if the slave bought the bolt for the master for ten dirhams, and in the second case, as if the ma'dhun slave sells the bolt for the master. So the first price is considered.

Explanation of the case: If a ma'dhun slave in trade bought a bolt for ten rupees and the ma'dhun slave has a debt of people that covers the entire value of his person, then that ma'dhun slave sold this bolt to his master for fifteen rupees, then the master can sell this bolt as murabahah on ten rupees; he is not permitted to sell as murabahah on fifteen rupees. Similarly, if the master bought a bolt for ten rupees and sold it to his ma'dhun slave for fifteen rupees, then the ma'dhun slave can sell this bolt as murabahah on ten rupees; he is not permitted to do murabahah on fifteen rupees. The proof is that in this contract, whether the slave sells to the master or the master sells to the slave, there is a suspicion that the sale is not valid, but in reality it is valid. And it is valid in reality because when the slave is indebted with a debt encompassing his person, the slave becomes the right of the creditors. And when the slave becomes the right of the creditors, it is as if this slave is no longer the property of his master but has become the property of the creditors.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific ruling regarding murabahah sales involving a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted to trade) and his master. The key fact is that the slave is heavily in debt (debt encompassing his entire value as a slave). In such a case, the slave is effectively owned by his creditors, not by the master. Therefore, any sale between the master and the slave is considered legally valid but tainted with a 'suspicion of non-existence' (shubhat al-'adam) because the slave is not truly the master's property. For the purpose of murabahah, this transaction is disregarded, and the original cost (the price at which the slave originally bought the item) is used as the basis for murabahah. The reasoning: the slave's debt makes him belong to the creditors, so the master does not truly own the slave's actions. The sale is valid because the slave's permission to trade is still effective, but the connection between master and slave (ownership) is severed by the debt. Therefore, when the master sells the item he bought from the slave, he must base the murabahah on the original cost (10 dirhams), not on the price he paid (15). Similarly, when the slave sells an item bought from the master, he also bases murabahah on the original cost (10). This ensures that the murabahah reflects the true economic reality, avoiding any suspicion of dishonesty. The passage illustrates a key Hanafi principle: transactions that are valid but subject to a legal suspicion (shubhah) are treated as non-existent for certain rulings, particularly where transparency is required (as in murabahah).

Key Terms
عبد مأذون له في التجارة (abd ma'dhun lahu fi al-tijarah): A slave who has been granted permission by his master to engage in trade; his transactions are valid but the slave's person is security for debts.
شبهة العدم (shubhat al-'adam): Suspicion of non-existence; a legal doubt about the validity of a transaction due to a contradictory element (manafi), causing it to be disregarded for certain purposes.
دين محيط برقبته (dayn muhit bi-raqabati-hi): A debt that encompasses the slave's entire value (his person as a commodity); the slave becomes effectively owned by creditors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A ma'dhun slave buys a cloth for 10 dirhams, then sells it to his master for 15 dirhams. The master wants to sell it as murabahah. On what price should he base the murabahah according to the Hanafi school?
A) 15 dirhams, because that is what he paid.
B) 10 dirhams, because the slave's debt makes the sale between them suspicious and disregarded for murabahah.
C) 12.5 dirhams, the average of the two prices.
D) The master cannot sell it as murabahah at all.

Key Takeaway
In murabahah, when a ma'dhun slave with overwhelming debt trades with his master, the transaction is disregarded for cost calculation; the original acquisition price must be used.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Murabahah Sale of a Debt-Laden Slave (Abd Ma'dhun)
Explaining Murabahah price for a slave with debts selling to his master

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for the Murabahah price when a debt-laden slave sells to his master and identify the key concept of shubhat al-`adam.

Core Idea
For Murabahah of a debt-laden slave, the master must use the original price, as the second sale is treated as non-existent.

This passage tackles a nuanced scenario in trust-based sales: a slave permitted to trade buys goods on credit, is deeply in debt, and then sells to his master at a profit. The Hanafi school here demonstrates a careful balancing act—the sale is valid in reality, but for Murabahah purposes, the second transaction is disregarded to avoid any suspicion of deception. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the concept of 'shubhat al-`adam' (suspicion of non-existence) and how the author prioritizes transparency in Murabahah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key elements of the scenario
What are the parties, the original price, the debt situation, and the sale price to the master? Pinpoint the facts: slave buys cloth for 10 dirhams, has debts covering his entire value, sells to master for 15 dirhams.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The master can resell the cloth on Murabahah only at the original price of 10 dirhams, not the 15 dirhams he paid to the slave.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Follow the reasoning using shubhat al-`adam
The sale between slave and master is valid because the slave's debts make him effectively owned by creditors, removing the master's ownership. However, there remains a suspicion of invalidity because the master still has a residual ownership claim. In Murabahah, which requires full transparency, this doubtful second sale is treated as non-existent, and the first sale’s price governs.
The term 'شبهة العدم' is key.
4
Apply the same principle to the reverse scenario
If the master originally bought the cloth and sold it to the slave, the same rule applies: the slave (or master in a subsequent Murabahah) uses the first price (10 dirhams), not the second.
5
Confirm the practical result
The Murabahah is based on the original price, ensuring no hidden profit or deception. The second sale is ignored for the purpose of cost disclosure.
This protects the buyer in a trust sale.

Source Text

عبد ماذون فی التجارة نے کپڑا دس درہم میں خریدا اور اس پر اتنا دین ہے کہ اس کے رقبہ کو محیط ہے مولیٰ کو پندرہ درہم کا بیچ دیا تو مولیٰ کتنے پر مرابحہ بیچ سکتا ہے

قال واذا اشترى العبد الماذون له فى التجارة ثوبا بعشرة وعليه دين يحيط برقبته فباعه من المولى بخمسة عشر فانه يبيعه مرابحة على عشرة وكذالك ان كان المولى اشتراه فباعه من العبد لان في هذ العقد شبهة العدم لجوازه مع المنافى فاعتبر عد ما في حكم المرابحة وبقى الاعتبار للاول فيصير كان العبد اشتراه للمولى بعشرة في الفصل الاول وكانه يبيعه للمولى فى الفصل الثاني فيعتبر الثمن الاول

ترجمہ اور اگر غلام ماذون لہ فی التجارة نے ایک تھان دس روپیہ کے عوض خریدا حالانکہ اس غلام پر اس قدر قرضہ ہے کہ اُسکی ذات کو محیط ہے پھر اس غلام نے یہ تھان اپنے مولیٰ کے ہاتھ پندرہ روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کیا تو مولیٰ اس تھان کو دس درہم پر مرابحہ کر کے بیچ سکتا ہے اور اسی طرح اگر مولیٰ نے اس تھان کو خریدا ہو پھر اپنے غلام ماذون لہ فی التجارة کے ہاتھ پندرہ روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کیا ہو کیونکہ اس عقد میں ( جو مولی اور اس کے غلام ماذون میں ہوا ہے ) نہ ہونے کا شبہ ہے کیونکہ یہ عقد منافی کے ساتھ جائز ہے پس مرابحہ کے حکم میں اس پیج کو معدوم شمار کیا گیا اور بیج اول کا اعتبار باقی رہ گیا پس پہلی صورت میں ایسا ہو گیا گویا غلام نے اس تھان کو دس درہم کے عوض مولی کے واسطے خریدا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں گویا غلام ماذون اس تھان کو مولی کے واسطے فروخت کرتا ہے پس پہلا شمن معتبر ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر غلام ماذون لہ فی التجارة نے ایک تھان دس روپیہ کے عوض خریدا اور غلام ماذون پر لوگوں کا اس قدر قرضہ ہے کہ وہ اس کے رقبہ کی پوری مالیت کا احاطہ کر لیتا ہے پھر اس غلام مازون نے یہ تھان اپنے مولی کے ہاتھ پندرہ روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کیا تو مولی اس تھان کو دس روپیہ پر مرابحہ کر کے فروخت کر سکتا ہے، پندرہ روپیہ پر بیع مرابحہ کرنے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی۔ اسی طرح اگر مولیٰ نے ایک تھان دس روپیہ کے عوض خرید کر اپنے غلام ماذون لہ فی التجارة کے ہاتھ پندرہ روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کیا تو غلام مازون اس تھان کو دس روپیہ پر مرابحہ کر کے فروخت کر سکتا ہے، پندرہ روپیہ پر مرابحہ کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس عقد میں غلام کے مولی کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنے میں اور مولیٰ کے غلام کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنے میں بیع جائز نہ ہونے کا شبہ ہے حقیقت انا جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ حقیقتا بیع جائز ہے۔ اور حقیقتا اس لئے جائز ہے کہ جب غلام دین محیط کے ساتھ مدیون ہے تو غلام قرض خواہوں کا حق ہوا اور جب غلام قرض خواہوں کا حق ہوا تو گویا یہ غلام اپنے مولیٰ کی ملک نہ رہا بلکہ قرض خواہوں کی ملک ہو گیا اور جب قرض خواہوں کی ملک ہو گیا تو مولی اور اس غلام کے درمیان مالک اور مملوک کی نسبت نہ رہی بلکہ اجنبیت ہوگئی اور دو اجنبیوں کے در میان بیع جائز ہوتی ہے، اس لئے مولی اور اس کے غلام مدیون کے درمیان بیع جائز ہو جائے گی۔ اور بیع جائز نہ ہونے کا شبہ اس لئے ہے کہ یہ بیچ منافی کے باوجود جائز کی گئی ہے اور منافی غلام کا اپنے مولیٰ کی ملک ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ جب تک قرض خواہ اس غلام کو نہ لے لیں اس وقت تک یہ اپنے مولیٰ کی ملک ہی رہے گا یا اگر مولیٰ اس کا قرضہ ادا کر دے تو بھی یہ اپنے مولیٰ کی ملک رہے گا۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا گویا مولی نے اپنی ملک کو خود خریدا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں گویا مولیٰ نے اپنی ملک کو خود اپنے ہاتھ بیچا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ درست نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال غلام اور مولی کے درمیان یہ بیج اگر چہ دین محیط کی وجہ سے حقیقتاً جائز ہے لیکن شبہ عدم جواز کا بھی ہے اور بیع مرابحہ کے اندر چونکہ شبہ سے بچنا بھی ضروری ہے اس لئے بیج مرابحہ میں غلام اور مولی کے درمیان واقع ہو نیوالی اس بیج کو معدوم شمار کیا گیا ہے اور بیج اول کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے اور ایسا ہو گیا گویا پہلی صورت میں غلام نے کپڑے کا تھان دس روپیہ کے عوض اپنے مولیٰ کے واسطے خریدا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں گو یا غلام اُس تھان کو اپنے مولیٰ کیلئے فروخت کرتا ہے، پس جب بیع ثانی معدوم ہے اور بیع اول ہی معتبر ہے تو مرا بجہ اس ثمن پر کرنا جائز ہوگا جو بیع اول میں مذکور ہے اور جوشن بیع ثانی میں مذکور ہے اس پر مرابحہ کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا او ربع اول میں چونکہ یمن دس درہم میں اس لئے دس درہم پر مرابحہ کرنے کی اجازت ہوگی۔
A slave permitted to trade bought a cloth for ten dirhams and owes a debt that covers his entire value. He then sold it to his master for fifteen dirhams. On what price can the master sell it as Murabahah? He said: If a slave permitted to trade buys a cloth for ten and has debt covering his value, then sells it to his master for fifteen, he (the master) sells it as Murabahah at ten. Similarly, if the master bought it and sold it to the slave. Because in this contract there is suspicion of non-existence, since it is valid despite a contradiction. Thus, in the ruling of Murabahah, this (second sale) is considered non-existent, and the first sale remains valid. So in the first case, it becomes as if the slave bought it for the master for ten, and in the second case, as if he sells it for the master. So the first price is considered. Translation: If a slave permitted to trade bought a cloth for ten rupees, and he has such debt that covers his entire being, then he sold this cloth to his master for fifteen rupees, then the master can sell this cloth as Murabahah at ten dirhams. Similarly, if the master bought the cloth and sold it to his slave... [continued explanation].
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding Murabahah sale when a debt-laden slave (Abd Ma'dhun) sells to his master. The ruling states that the master (or slave in the reverse case) can only resell the cloth on a Murabahah basis using the original purchase price (10 dirhams), not the inflated price (15 dirhams). The reasoning is based on 'shubhat al-`adam' (suspicion of non-existence) of the second sale in the context of Murabahah. Although the sale between master and slave is valid in reality (because the slave's debt makes him effectively owned by creditors, creating a quasi-stranger relationship), there remains a suspicion of invalidity because of the underlying ownership contradiction. Since Murabahah requires transparency and avoidance of suspicion, the second sale is treated as non-existent, and the first sale's price is used. The author carefully explains that the sale is valid in itself but is disregarded for Murabahah purposes to prevent any potential deception (khianah). This is a distinctive Hanafi application of istihsan (juristic preference) to uphold the integrity of trust-based sales.

Key Terms
عبد ماذون فی التجارة (Abd Ma'dhun fi al-Tijarah): A slave who has been granted permission by his master to engage in trade.
دین محیط (Dayn Muhit): A debt that covers the entire value of the slave's estate (his purchase price or net worth), effectively making the slave's entire asset subject to creditors.
شبهة العدم (Shubhat al-'Adam): A suspicion of non-existence, meaning that while the contract is valid in reality, it is treated as if it did not exist for certain legal purposes due to a potential conflict or doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a debt-laden slave (Abd Ma'dhun) sells a cloth to his master for 15 dirhams, on what price can the master resell it on a Murabahah basis?
A) 10 dirhams
B) 15 dirhams
C) 12.5 dirhams
D) The market price

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a debt-laden slave sells to his master, the master's Murabahah cost is the slave's original price, as the second sale is considered non-existent to avoid suspicion of deception.

Murabahah Price When Mudarib Sells to Rab al-Mal
Explaining Murabahah price when a Mudarib sells to the capital owner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the correct Murabahah price when a Mudarib sells the purchased asset to the capital owner, applying the principle of shubhat al-`adam.

Core Idea
In Murabahah, when Mudarib sells to Rab al-Mal, only Rab al-Mal's share of profit is added to the cost.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in Mudarabah: the Mudarib buys an asset with partnership capital and then sells it to the capital owner (Rab al-Mal) at a profit. The question is: at what price can Rab al-Mal resell that asset as Murabahah? The Hanafi ruling uses a unique reasoning based on agency and disregard of the Mudarib's profit share. You will learn the correct calculation and the underlying legal principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the resale of an asset by Rab al-Mal on a Murabahah basis after the Mudarib sold it to him. The ruling: it is permissible only at a price of 12.5 dirhams in the given scenario.
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides a proof based on the purpose of Mudarabah: obtaining authority to transact (wilayat al-tasarruf). The contract follows the benefit, and the Mudarib is an agent from one perspective, so half the profit is disregarded.
This is a talil (rationale) argument, not a textual proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning: because the Mudarib acts as an agent (wakil) for Rab al-Mal in the first purchase (from a certain viewpoint), the second sale between them is considered non-existent with respect to the Mudarib's share of profit. Therefore, the profit attributable to the Mudarib is not counted for Murabahah purposes.
This is the principle of shubhat al-`adam (suspicion of non-existence).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar holds that the initial sale from Mudarib to Rab al-Mal is invalid when there is no profit (since Rab al-Mal buys his own property). The majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) upholds its validity based on istihsan.
This ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The text uses 'at our school' (عندنا) to indicate the relied-upon position. The majority view is mufta bihi: the sale is valid and Rab al-Mal can resell at 12.5 dirhams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مضارب نے دس درہم میں کپڑ ا خرید کر رب المال کو پندرہ درہم کا بیچ دیا تو رب المال کتنے پر مرابحہ بیچ سکتا ہے؟

قال و اذا كان مع المضارب عشرة دراهم بالنصف فاشترى ثوبا بعشرة وباعه من رب المال بخمسة عشر فانه يبيعه مرابحة باثني عشر ونصف لان هذا البيع وان قضى بجوازه عندنا عند عدم الربح خلافا لزقر مع انه اشترى ماله بماله لما فيه من استفاده ولاية التصرف وهو مقصود والانعقاد يتبع الفائدة ففيه شبهة العدم الاترى انه وكيل عنه فى البيع الاول من وجه فاعتبر البيع الثاني عد مافي حق نصف الربح

ترجمہ اور اگر مضارب کے پاس آدھے نفع کی شرط پر دس درہم ہوں پھر مضارب نے ایک تھان دس درہم کے عوض خرید کر رہے المال کے ہاتھ پندرہ درہم کے عوض فروخت کر دیا تو رب المال اُس تھان کو ساڑھے بارہ درہم پر مرابحہ کر کے فروخت کر سکتا ہے اس لئے کہ یہ بیج اگر چہ ہمارے نزدیک عدم نفع کے وقت اس کے جواز کا حکم ہوا ہے خلاف ہے امام زفر کا باوجود یکہ رب المال نے اپنا مال اپنے مال کے عوض خریدا ہے کیونکہ اس میں ولایت تصرف کا حصول ہے اور یہی مقصود ہے اور انعقاد عقد سے فائدہ بھی لگا ہوا ہے لیکن اس میں نہ ہونے کا شبہ ہے، کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ مضارب بیج اول میں من وجہ رب المال کا وکیل ہے، پس آدھے نفع کے حق میں بیج ثانی کو معدوم شمار کیا جائے گا۔

تشرت صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک آدمی نے دوسرے کو بیچ مضاربت کرنے کیلئے دس روپیہ دیئے اور آدھے نفع کی شرط کی یعنی جس قدر نفع ہوگا وہ رب المال اور مضارب کے درمیان مشترک ہو گا ، نصف رب المال کا ہوگا اور نصف مضارب کا ہوگا ۔ پس مضارب نے ان دس روپیوں کا کپڑا خرید کر رب المال کے ہاتھ پندرہ روپے میں فروخت کر دیا ، اب رب المال اگر اس کپڑے کو بیع مرابحہ کے طور
If a Mudarib has ten dirhams on condition of half (profit), then he buys a cloth for ten and sells it to the capital owner (Rab al-Mal) for fifteen, then he (Rab al-Mal) sells it as Murabahah at twelve and a half. Because this sale, although we rule it valid in our school when there is no profit, contrary to Zufar, even though he (Rab al-Mal) bought his own property with his own property, because it contains obtaining the authority to transact, and that is the purpose, and the contract follows the benefit. So there is suspicion of non-existence. Do you not see that he (Mudarib) is an agent from one perspective in the first sale? So the second sale is considered non-existent in respect of half the profit. Translation: If a Mudarib has ten dirhams on half-profit condition, then buys a cloth for ten, and sells it to Rab al-Mal for fifteen, then Rab al-Mal can sell that cloth as Murabahah at twelve and a half dirhams. Because this sale, although ruled valid in our school when there is no profit, contrary to Imam Zufar, even though Rab al-Mal bought his own property with his own property, because it contains obtaining the authority to transact, and that is the purpose, and the contract follows the benefit. But there is suspicion of non-existence. Don't you see that the Mudarib is in a way an agent for Rab al-Mal in the first sale? So the second sale is considered non-existent in respect of half the profit. Explanation of the case: If a person gave another ten rupees for Mudarabah on half-profit, i.e., whatever profit is made will be shared, half for Rab al-Mal and half for Mudarib. Then the Mudarib bought a cloth with those ten rupees and sold it to Rab al-Mal for fifteen rupees. Now if Rab al-Mal wants to sell this cloth as Murabahah... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof concerning Murabahah when a Mudarib (agent-manager) sells the purchased asset to the Rab al-Mal (capital owner). The ruling states that Rab al-Mal cannot resell on Murabahah at the inflated price of 15 dirhams; rather, he can only sell at the original cost plus the share of profit belonging to Rab al-Mal, which is 12.5 dirhams (cost 10 + half of the 5 profit = 2.5). The reasoning is based on the principle of 'shubhat al-`adam' applied to half the profit, because the Mudarib is effectively an agent for Rab al-Mal in the first purchase (on one view), so the second sale is considered void in respect of that half. The author notes that Imam Zufar disagrees with the validity of the sale itself when there is no profit (since it's like buying one's own property), but the Hanafi school holds it valid due to the benefit of enabling transactions. This is a classic application of istihsan to reconcile the apparent conflict.

Key Terms
مضارب (Mudarib): The person who manages capital in a Mudarabah partnership, entitled to a share of profit.
رب المال (Rab al-Mal): The capital provider in a Mudarabah contract.
ولایت تصرف (Wilayat al-Tasarruf): The legal authority to conduct transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Mudarabah with half-profits, a Mudarib buys cloth for 10 dirhams and sells it to Rab al-Mal for 15. On what price can Rab al-Mal resell on Murabahah?
A) 10 dirhams
B) 15 dirhams
C) 12.5 dirhams
D) 17.5 dirhams

Key Takeaway
When Mudarib sells to Rab al-Mal, the Murabahah resale price is cost plus Rab al-Mal's share of profit only, because the Mudarib's profit share is considered nonexistent due to the Mudarib's agency.

Murābaḥa Sale Between Master and Indebted Slave
Ruling on murābaḥa when master buys from his indebted slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that in a murābaḥa sale involving an indebted slave, only the original purchase price from the first sale is valid for disclosure, and explain the qiyas reasoning that disregards the sale with shubhah.

Core Idea
In murābaḥa, a sale with shubhah is disregarded; the price from the original cost is used.

This passage tackles a nuanced scenario: a master sells a cloth that his indebted slave had previously purchased from a third party. While the sale between master and slave is valid due to the slave's debt, murābaḥa requires absolute transparency, free from any semblance (shubhah) of dishonesty. The author of Ashraf al-Hidāyah demonstrates how the Hanafi school resolves this tension by treating the second sale as non-existent for murābaḥa purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is a murābaḥa sale by the master of a cloth originally purchased by his indebted slave. The ruling: the murābaḥa is valid only if based on the price of the first sale (what the slave paid to the third party), not the price of the subsequent sale between master and slave.
The overall sale between master and slave is valid, but the murābaḥa contract has special requirements.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas: the sale between master and indebted slave is valid due to necessity (the debt creates a separation of ownership). However, murābaḥa requires avoiding shubhah, so the second sale is treated as non-existent.
The reasoning is talīl—the underlying cause is the need to avoid ambiguity in murābaḥa.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The legal link: the shubhah arises from the fact that the slave is still technically owned by the master until creditors take possession. In murābaḥa, such ambiguity invalidates the contract. Therefore, the second sale is disregarded, and only the first sale's price is reliable.
The principle is that murābaḥa requires full disclosure; any doubt about the cost price undermines the contract.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While the passage does not discuss intra-Hanafi dispute, some scholars (e.g., Imam Zufar) may differ on whether the initial sale between master and slave is valid without profit. However, here the focus is on the murābaḥa ruling.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fīh, but the Hanafi position is clear.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position: the murābaḥa must be based on the first sale's price. The authority is the author of Ashraf al-Hidāyah, representing later Hanafi fatawa.
This is consistent with the Hanafi emphasis on avoiding shubhah in financial transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جب قرض خواہوں کی ملک ہو گیا تو مولی اور اس غلام کے درمیان مالک اور مملوک کی نسبت نہ رہی بلکہ اجنبیت ہوگئی اور دو اجنبیوں کے در میان بیع جائز ہوتی ہے، اس لئے مولی اور اس کے غلام مدیون کے درمیان بیع جائز ہو جائے گی۔ اور بیع جائز نہ ہونے کا شبہ اس لئے ہے کہ یہ بیع منافی کے باوجود جائز کی گئی ہے اور منافی غلام کا اپنے مولیٰ کی ملک ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ جب تک قرض خواہ اس غلام کو نہ لے لیں اس وقت تک یہ اپنے مولیٰ کی ملک ہی رہے گا یا اگر مولیٰ اس کا قرضہ ادا کر دے تو بھی یہ اپنے مولیٰ کی ملک رہے گا۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا گویا مولی نے اپنی ملک کو خود خریدا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں گویا مولیٰ نے اپنی ملک کو خود اپنے ہاتھ بیچا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ درست نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال غلام اور مولی کے درمیان یہ بیع اگر چہ دین محیط کی وجہ سے حقیقتاً جائز ہے لیکن شبہ عدم جواز کا بھی ہے اور بیع مرابحہ کے اندر چونکہ شبہ سے بچنا بھی ضروری ہے اس لئے بیع مرابحہ میں غلام اور مولی کے درمیان واقع ہونے والی اس بیع کو معدوم شمار کیا گیا ہے اور بیع اول کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے اور ایسا ہو گیا گویا پہلی صورت میں غلام نے کپڑے کا تھان دس روپیہ کے عوض اپنے مولیٰ کے واسطے خریدا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں گویا غلام اُس تھان کو اپنے مولیٰ کیلئے فروخت کرتا ہے، پس جب بیع ثانی معدوم ہے اور بیع اول ہی معتبر ہے تو مرابحہ اس ثمن پر کرنا جائز ہوگا جو بیع اول میں مذکور ہے اور جو ثمن بیع ثانی میں مذکور ہے اس پر مرابحہ کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا اور بیع اول میں چونکہ ثمن دس درہم ہے اس لئے دس درہم پر مرابحہ کرنے کی اجازت ہوگی۔
When the creditors have taken ownership (of the slave), then between the master and that slave the relationship of owner and owned ceases; rather, they become strangers, and a sale between two strangers is valid. Therefore, the sale between the master and his indebted slave is valid. And the semblance of invalidity is because this sale is made valid despite the impediment (that the slave is still the master's property), and the impediment is that the slave is owned by his master. Because as long as the creditors do not take the slave, he remains the master's property; or if the master pays his debt, he also remains the master's property. Thus it becomes as if the master purchased his own property, and in the second scenario, as if the master sold his own property to himself, and it is clear that this is not correct. Nevertheless, this sale between the slave and the master is actually valid due to the encompassing debt, but there is also a semblance of invalidity. And since in a murābaḥa sale it is necessary to avoid semblance, therefore in the murābaḥa sale, this sale that occurred between the slave and the master is considered non-existent, and the first sale is considered. It becomes as if in the first scenario the slave purchased the cloth for ten rupees on behalf of his master, and in the second scenario the slave sells that cloth for his master. Thus when the second sale is non-existent and only the first sale is considered, then murābaḥa is permissible on the price mentioned in the first sale, and it is not permissible to do murābaḥa on the price mentioned in the second sale. And since in the first sale the price is ten dirhams, therefore permission is given to do murābaḥa at ten dirhams.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talīl). The author of Ashraf al-Hidāyah explains the ruling on a murābaḥa sale involving an indebted slave. The situation: a master sells a cloth to his own slave who is indebted to creditors. The sale is valid in itself because the debt has effectively transferred ownership of the slave to the creditors, removing the impediment of the slave being the master's property. However, there remains a semblance (shubhah) of invalidity because the slave is still technically owned by the master until the creditors actually take possession. In murābaḥa sales, where the seller must disclose the cost price and profit, any semblance of dishonesty must be avoided. Therefore, the second sale (between master and slave) is disregarded in the murābaḥa calculation. Only the first sale—where the slave originally purchased the cloth from a third party for ten dirhams—is considered. Thus the master may sell the cloth as murābaḥa based on that original cost of ten dirhams, not the price of the subsequent sale between them. This follows the Hanafi principle that murābaḥa requires complete transparency, and any ambiguity due to the relationship is resolved by disregarding the sale that creates the ambiguity.

Key Terms
غلام مدیون (ghulām madīūn): A slave who is in debt, such that his value is owed to creditors, effectively transferring ownership.
بیع مرابحہ (bay' murābaḥa): A sale where the seller discloses the cost price and adds a known profit margin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a master buys cloth from his indebted slave and then wants to sell it as murābaḥa, which price should he disclose?
A) The price paid to the slave (the second sale).
B) The original cost paid by the slave to the third party (the first sale).
C) The market value of the cloth.
D) Any price agreed upon between master and slave.

Key Takeaway
In murābaḥa, any sale with shubhah is disregarded; only the original cost from the first sale is valid for disclosure.

Murābaḥa Price Adjustment After Mudārib Sells to Capital Owner
Ruling on murābaḥa after mudārib sells to capital owner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the correct murābaḥa price when a mudārib sells to the capital owner, and explain the Hanafi rationale based on shubhah and wilāyat al-taṣarruf.

Core Idea
When a mudārib sells to the capital owner, the capital owner's share of profit is tainted by shubhah and must be excluded from the murābaḥa cost.

In a mudāraba partnership, the mudārib (manager) may sometimes sell the purchased goods to the capital owner (rabb al-māl). If the capital owner then wishes to resell the goods as murābaḥa (cost-plus sale), what price should he disclose as his cost? This passage from al-Hidāyah tackles precisely that question, revealing a subtle interplay between restoring authority to transact and avoiding dishonesty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Transaction Details
Lay out the facts: Mudārib receives 10 dirhams on half-profit share, buys a cloth for 10, sells it to the capital owner for 15. The capital owner now wants to sell it as murābaḥa.
The profit of 5 dirhams is split equally: 2.5 for mudārib, 2.5 for capital owner.
2
Recognise the Dispute Over the Initial Sale
Imam Zufar argues the initial sale (mudārib to capital owner) is invalid because it is an exchange of the capital owner's property with his own property. The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa) holds it valid due to the benefit of restoring wilāyat al-taṣarruf.
This ikhtilaf is the foundation for the murābaḥa adjustment.
3
Understand the Hanafi Position on Murābaḥa
Even though the sale is valid, there is a shubhah (semblance of invalidity) because the mudārib is an agent (wakīl) of the capital owner in some respect. To avoid dishonesty in murābaḥa, the capital owner's own share of profit (2.5 dirhams) is considered tainted and must be deducted from the disclosed cost.
The disclosed cost becomes: original price (10) + mudārib's share (2.5) = 12.5 dirhams.
4
Apply the Rule to Compute the Murābaḥa Price
The capital owner may offer the cloth as murābaḥa at a cost of 12.5 dirhams, plus any additional profit he wishes to state. He cannot claim the full 15 dirhams as cost.
This ensures no semblance of dishonesty (shubhah al-khiyānah).

Source Text

زفر کا باوجود یکہ رب المال نے اپنا مال اپنے مال کے عوض خریدا ہے کیونکہ اس میں ولایت تصرف کا حصول ہے اور یہی مقصود ہے اور انعقاد عقد سے فائدہ بھی لگا ہوا ہے لیکن اس میں نہ ہونے کا شبہ ہے، کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ مضارب بیع اول میں من وجہ رب المال کا وکیل ہے، پس آدھے نفع کے حق میں بیع ثانی کو معدوم شمار کیا جائے گا۔ تشرت صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک آدمی نے دوسرے کو بیچ مضاربت کرنے کیلئے دس روپیہ دیئے اور آدھے نفع کی شرط کی یعنی جس قدر نفع ہوگا وہ رب المال اور مضارب کے درمیان مشترک ہو گا ، نصف رب المال کا ہوگا اور نصف مضارب کا ہوگا ۔ پس مضارب نے ان دس روپیوں کا کپڑا خرید کر رب المال کے ہاتھ پندرہ روپے میں فروخت کر دیا ، اب رب المال اگر اس کپڑے کو بیع مرابحہ کے طور پر فروخت کرنا چاہے تو ساڑھے بارہ روپیہ پر مرابحہ کر سکتا ہے۔ پندرہ روپیہ پر مرابحہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ یعنی رب المال یہ کہے کہ یہ کپڑا مجھ کو ساڑھے بارہ روپیہ میں پڑا ہے اور میں اس پر اس قدر نفع لوں گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع مرابحہ کا مبنی خیانت اور شبہ خیانت سے بچنے پر ہے، اور رب المال کے اس کپڑے کو پندرہ روپیہ پر مرابحہ کر کے فروخت کرنے میں شبہ خیانت موجود ہے کیونکہ مال مضاربت میں اگر کچھ نفع حاصل ہو گیا ہو تو مضارب کا رب المال کے ہاتھ اور رب المال کا مضارب کے ہاتھ بیچنا بالاتفاق جائز ہے اور اگر کچھ نفع حاصل نہ ہوا ہو تو مضارب کا رب المال کے ہاتھ اور رب المسان کا مضارب کے ہاتھ بیچنا امام زفر کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے لیکن ہمارے نزدیک یعنی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے بیع مبادلۃ المال بالمال کا نام ہے اور یہ اس وقت متفق ہو گا جب کہ آدمی اپنے مال کا تبادلہ دوسرے کے مال سے کرے اور اگر اپنے مال سے اپنے ہی مال کا مبادلہ کیا تو بیع تحقیق نہ ہوگی اور یہاں یہی صورت ہے کیونکہ جب مضارب نے دس روپیہ کا تھان خرید کر رب المال کے ہاتھ بیچا تو گو یا رب المال نے اپنا مال اپنے مال کے عوض خریدا اس لئے کہ تھان بھی رب المال کا مال ہے اور پندرہ روپیہ جس کے عوض خریدا ہے وہ بھی رب المال کا مال ہے، پس مضارب اور رب المال کے درمیان یہ بیع موجود نہ ہوگی اور ہمارے نزدیک جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ بیع ایک فائدہ پر مشتمل ہے اور وہ فائدہ یہ ہے کہ جب رب المال نے دس روپیہ مضارب کو دیدیئے تو ان دس روپیوں سے رب المال کی ولایت تصرف منقطع ہو گئی تھی یعنی دس روپیہ مضارب کو سپرد کرنے کے بعد رب المال کو ان میں تصرف کرنے کا کوئی حق باقی نہیں رہا تھا مگر جب رب المال نے ان دس روپیوں میں خریدا ہوا کپڑے کا تھان پندرہ روپیہ کے عوض خرید لیا تو اب رب المال کو ولایت تصرف حاصل ہوگئی اور بیع سے تصرف ہی مقصود ہوتا ہے، پس جب یہ بیع فائدہ پر مشتمل ہے تو منعقد ہو جائے گی کیونکہ انعقاد بیع سے فائدہ حاصل کرنا ہی مطلوب ہوتا ہے لیکن اس کے باجود امام زفر کی بیان کردہ دلیل کی وجہ سے عدم جواز کا شبہ ہے، اور عدم جواز کا شبہ اس لئے بھی ہے کہ بیع مضاربت میں مضارب من وجہ رب المال کا وکیل ہوتا ہے یعنی مضارب اپنے لئے بھی عمل کرتا ہے اور رب المال کیلئے بھی عمل کرتا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ نفع مضارب اور رب المال دونوں کیلئے ہوتا ہے برخلاف وکیل کے کہ وہ فقط موکل کیلئے عمل کرتا ہے اور نفع بھی خالص مؤکل کیلئے ہوتا ہے پس چونکہ مضارب من وجہ رب المال کا وکیل ہوتا ہے اس لئے مضارب اور رب المال کے در میان بیع جائز نہ ہوگی جیسا کہ وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان بیع جائز نہیں ہوتی ، پس جب مضارب اور رب المال کے درمیان بیع میں عدم جواز کا شبہ ہے تو بیع ثانی یعنی رب المال کا پندرہ روپیہ کے عوض مضارب سے تھان خریدنا آدھے نفع یعنی ڈھائی روپیہ کے حق میں معدوم شمار ہوگی کیونکہ ڈھائی روپیہ رب المال کا حق ہے، پس خیانت کے شبہ سے بچنے کیلئے ڈھائی روپیہ ثمن سے کم کر دئیے جائیں گے اور چونکہ اصل ثمن یعنی دس روپیہ میں اور مضارب کے حصہ یعنی ڈھائی روپیہ میں کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے اس لئے رب المال ساڑھے بارہ روپیہ پر بیع مرابحہ کر سکتا ہے، یعنی یہ کہہ سکتا ہے کہ یہ کپڑا مجھے کو ساڑھے بارہ میں پڑا ہے اور اس پر اس قدر نفع لیکر فروخت کرتا ہوں ۔
A mudārib bought a cloth for ten dirhams and sold it to the capital owner for fifteen dirhams. On what price can the capital owner sell it as murābaḥa? He (the author) said: If a mudārib has ten dirhams on the condition of half profit, then he bought a cloth for ten and sold it to the capital owner for fifteen, then he sells it as murābaḥa at twelve and a half. Because this sale, even if it is ruled permissible in our view when there is no profit, contrary to Zufar, despite the fact that he bought his own property with his own property, because it involves the acquisition of the authority to transact (wilāyat al-taṣarruf), which is the purpose, and the contract follows the benefit, so there is a semblance of non-existence. Do you not see that he is an agent for him in the first sale in some respect, so the second sale is considered non-existent in respect of half the profit. Translation: And if a mudārib has ten dirhams on the condition of half profit, then the mudārib bought a cloth for ten dirhams and sold it to the capital owner for fifteen dirhams, then the capital owner can sell that cloth as murābaḥa at twelve and a half dirhams. Because this sale, although in our view it is ruled permissible when there is no profit, contrary to Imam Zufar, despite the fact that the capital owner bought his own property with his own property, because in it there is the acquisition of the authority to transact, and that is the purpose, and the contract follows the benefit, but there is a semblance of non-existence. Do you not see that the mudārib is an agent for the capital owner in the first sale in some respect? So the second sale will be considered non-existent in respect of half the profit. Explanation: The case is that if a man gave another ten rupees for a mudāraba partnership and stipulated half profit—i.e., whatever profit occurs, it will be shared between the capital owner and the mudārib, half for the capital owner and half for the mudārib. Then the mudārib bought a cloth with those ten rupees and sold it to the capital owner for fifteen rupees. Now if the capital owner wants to sell that cloth as a murābaḥa sale, he can do murābaḥa at twelve and a half rupees. It is not permissible to do murābaḥa at fifteen rupees. That is, the capital owner should say: 'This cloth cost me twelve and a half rupees, and I will take such and such profit on it.' The proof is that murābaḥa is based on avoiding dishonesty and the semblance of dishonesty, and in the capital owner selling this cloth as murābaḥa at fifteen rupees, there is a semblance of dishonesty. Because in mudāraba property, if some profit has been obtained, the mudārib selling to the capital owner and the capital owner selling to the mudārib is unanimously permissible. And if no profit has been obtained, then the mudārib selling to the capital owner and the capital owner selling to the mudārib is impermissible according to Imam Zufar, but in our view (Imam Abu Hanifa's) it is permissible. Imam Zufar's proof is that a sale is an exchange of property for property, and it will be realized when a person exchanges his property with another's property. But if he exchanges his own property with his own property, then the sale will not be actualized. And here that is the case, because when the mudārib bought the cloth for ten rupees and sold it to the capital owner, it is as if the capital owner bought his own property with his own property, because the cloth is also the capital owner's property, and the fifteen rupees with which he bought it are also the capital owner's property. Therefore, this sale between the mudārib and the capital owner would not exist. And in our view, the reason for permissibility is that this sale contains a benefit, and that benefit is that when the capital owner gave ten rupees to the mudārib, the capital owner's authority to transact (wilāyat al-taṣarruf) in those ten rupees was cut off—i.e., after entrusting the ten rupees, the capital owner had no right to transact in them. But when the capital owner bought the cloth (purchased with those ten rupees) for fifteen rupees, he regained the authority to transact. And the purpose of a sale is transaction. So when this sale contains a benefit, it will be concluded, because concluding a sale is done to obtain benefit. Nevertheless, due to Imam Zufar's argument, there is a semblance of invalidity. And the semblance of invalidity is also because in a mudāraba sale, the mudārib is an agent for the capital owner in some respect—he acts for himself and for the capital owner. This is why profit is for both, unlike a wakīl who acts only for the principal. So since the mudārib is an agent in some respect, the sale between mudārib and capital owner would not be permissible, just as a sale between a wakīl and his principal is not permissible. So when there is a semblance of invalidity in the sale between mudārib and capital owner, the second sale—i.e., the capital owner's purchase of the cloth from the mudārib for fifteen rupees—will be considered non-existent in respect of half the profit, i.e., two and a half rupees, because that two and a half is the capital owner's own right. So to avoid the semblance of dishonesty, two and a half rupees will be deducted from the price. And since the original price (ten rupees) and the mudārib's share (two and a half) have no semblance, the capital owner can do murābaḥa at twelve and a half rupees—i.e., he can say: 'This cloth cost me twelve and a half, and I sell it taking such and such profit.'
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talīl) concerning a murābaḥa sale after a mudārabah transaction. The situation: a mudārib (investment manager) receives ten dirhams from the capital owner (rabb al-māl) on the condition of half profit. He buys a cloth for ten dirhams and then sells it to the capital owner for fifteen dirhams. The capital owner now wants to sell the cloth as murābaḥa (cost-plus sale). The author rules that the capital owner may sell it as murābaḥa at twelve and a half dirhams, not fifteen. The reason involves a dispute: Imam Zufar considers the initial sale (mudārib to rabb al-māl) invalid because it amounts to exchanging one's own property with one's own property. In the Hanafi view (Imam Abu Hanifa), the sale is valid because it provides a benefit—it restores the capital owner's authority to transact (wilāyat al-taṣarruf) which was suspended. However, since the mudārib is considered an agent (wakīl) of the capital owner in some respect, there is a semblance (shubhah) of invalidity akin to a sale between a principal and his agent. Therefore, for the purpose of murābaḥa, this shubhah must be removed. The profit of five dirhams is split equally between the mudārib and capital owner. The capital owner's share of the profit (2.5 dirhams) is considered tainted by shubhah because it comes from a transaction with his own agent. So that amount is deducted from the disclosed cost price, leaving the original cost (10 dirhams) plus the mudārib's share (2.5 dirhams which is not tainted) totaling 12.5 dirhams. Thus the capital owner may disclose a cost of 12.5 dirhams and add his profit. This avoids any semblance of dishonesty in the murābaḥa.

Key Terms
مضارب (muḍārib): The manager of the mudāraba partnership who invests the capital and shares in the profit.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The capital owner who provides funds in a mudāraba partnership.
ولایت تصرف (wilāyat al-taṣarruf): The legal authority to conduct transactions with property.
شبہ (shubhah): Semblance or doubt; here it refers to a semblance of dishonesty (khiyānah) that must be avoided in murābaḥa.
مرابحہ (murābaḥa): A sale where the seller discloses the cost and adds a stated profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, why is the capital owner allowed to sell the cloth as murābaḥa at 12.5 dirhams instead of 15 dirhams?
A) Because he wants to give a discount to the buyer.
B) Because the mudārib's share of profit (2.5 dirhams) is tainted by shubhah due to the agency relationship.
C) Because Imam Zufar ruled that the sale is invalid.
D) Because the cloth actually cost only 12.5 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
When a mudārib sells to the capital owner, the capital owner's own profit share is tainted by shubhah and must be excluded from the disclosed cost in a subsequent murābaḥa sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Murabahah Pricing on Mudarabah Goods: Avoiding Suspicion of Cheating
Ruling on murabahah price for mudarabah goods with ikhtilaf of Imam Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on murabahah pricing when a rabb al-mal buys back mudarabah goods and explain why the price is adjusted to avoid shubhah khiyanah.

Core Idea
Murabahah requires avoiding even the shadow of cheating; the price must be reduced by the profit share that raises suspicion.

Murabahah is a trust-based sale that requires full transparency. When a mudarib purchases goods and later sells them back to the capital provider (rabb al-mal), a suspicion of cheating may arise because the mudarib also acts as an agent. This lesson examines how Imam Abu Hanifa resolves this suspicion by adjusting the murabahah price, and contrasts his view with that of Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Understand the facts: a mudarib buys a cloth for 10 rupees using capital from the rabb al-mal. No profit is made. Then the rabb al-mal wants to buy the cloth for 15 rupees and later sell it on murabahah.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the sale between mudarib and rabb al-mal is valid, but the subsequent murabahah must be at 12.5 rupees (cost + mudarib's share), not 15 rupees.
3
Understand the Reasoning for Permissibility
Imam Abu Hanifa's argument: when the rabb al-mal gave capital to the mudarib, his legal authority (wilayat tasarruf) over that property ceased. The sale restores this authority, which is a benefit (maslahah) that justifies the sale's validity.
4
Analyze the Suspicion and Its Resolution
Imam Zufar objects that no real sale occurs because both the cloth and the price belong to the rabb al-mal. Although Abu Hanifa rejects this, he acknowledges a remaining suspicion due to the mudarib's partial agency. To avoid even the appearance of cheating, the profit that belongs to the rabb al-mal (half of the 5 rupee profit, i.e., 2.5 rupees) is subtracted from the sale price, leading to a murabahah cost of 12.5 rupees.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar deems the initial sale invalid; Abu Hanifa deems it valid but with a price adjustment. The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's.

المال کے درمیان بیچ میں عدم جواز کا شبہ ہے تو بیع ثانی یعنی رب المال کا پندرہ روپیہ کے عوض مضارب سے تھان خریدنا آدھے نفع یعنی ڈھائی روپیہ کے حق میں معدوم شمار ہوگی کیونکہ ڈھائی روپیہ رب المال کا حق ہے، پس خیانت کے شبہ سے بچنے کیلئے ڈھائی روپیہ یمن سے کم کر دئیے جائیں گے اور چونکہ اصل ثمن یعنی دس روپیہ میں اور مضارب کے حصہ یعنی ڈھائی روپیہ میں کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے اس لئے رب المال ساڑھے بارہ روپیہ پر بیج مرابحہ کر سکتا ہے، یعنی یہ کہہ سکتا ہے کہ یہ کپڑا مجھے کو ساڑھے بارہ میں پڑا ہے اور اس پر اس قدر نفع لیکر فروخت کرتا ہوں ۔
If he wants to sell (the cloth) on murabahah, he can do murabahah at twelve and a half rupees. Doing murabahah at fifteen rupees is not permissible. That is, the owner of capital (rabb al-mal) says: 'This cloth cost me twelve and a half rupees, and I will take this much profit on it.' The proof is that the basis of murabahah is to avoid cheating and suspicion of cheating, and in the rabb al-mal selling this cloth on murabahah at fifteen rupees, there exists a suspicion of cheating. Because in mudarabah, if some profit has been made, the sale by the mudarib to the rabb al-mal and by the rabb al-mal to the mudarib is unanimously permissible. And if no profit has been made, the sale by the mudarib to the rabb al-mal and by the rabb al-mal to the mudarib is impermissible according to Imam Zufar, but according to us, i.e., Imam Abu Hanifa, it is permissible.

Imam Zufar's evidence: A sale is named an exchange of property for property, and it will occur only when a person exchanges his property for another's property. If he exchanges his own property for his own property, it is not a valid sale. That is the case here because when the mudarib bought a cloth (thān) for ten rupees and sold it to the rabb al-mal, it is as if the rabb al-mal bought his own property for his own property, because the cloth is also the property of the rabb al-mal, and the fifteen rupees with which he buys are also the property of the rabb al-mal. Therefore, this sale does not exist between the mudarib and the rabb al-mal.

According to us, the reason for permissibility is that this sale involves a benefit, and that benefit is that when the rabb al-mal gave ten rupees to the mudarib, the rabb al-mal's authority of disposition (wilayat tasarruf) over those ten rupees was severed. That is, after giving the ten rupees to the mudarib, the rabb al-mal had no right to dispose of them. But when the rabb al-mal bought the cloth (which was purchased with those ten rupees) in exchange for fifteen rupees, he (re)gained the authority of disposition. And from a sale, the intended thing is disposition. So when this sale involves a benefit, it becomes valid, because obtaining benefit through concluding a sale is what is sought.

Nevertheless, due to the evidence presented by Imam Zufar, there is a suspicion of impermissibility, and there is also a suspicion of impermissibility because in mudarabah, the mudarib is partially (min wajh) an agent of the rabb al-mal. That is, the mudarib acts both for himself and for the rabb al-mal. This is why profit goes to both the mudarib and the rabb al-mal, unlike an agent (wakil) who acts only for the principal (muwakkil) and profit is purely for the principal. So since the mudarib is partially an agent of the rabb al-mal, the sale between the mudarib and the rabb al-mal is not permissible, just as a sale between an agent and his principal is not permissible. Therefore, when there is a suspicion of impermissibility in the sale between mudarib and rabb al-mal, the second sale, i.e., the rabb al-mal's purchase of the cloth from the mudarib for fifteen rupees, is considered non-existent with respect to half the profit, i.e., two and a half rupees, because two and a half rupees is the right of the rabb al-mal. So to avoid the suspicion of cheating, two and a half rupees will be reduced from the price. And since there is no suspicion in the original price, i.e., ten rupees, and in the mudarib's share, i.e., two and a half rupees, the rabb al-mal can do murabahah at twelve and a half rupees. That is, he can say: 'This cloth cost me twelve and a half, and I am selling it with this much profit.'
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of murabahah sale in the context of mudarabah. It begins by stating that if a person wants to sell a cloth (which was purchased in a mudarabah) on murabahah, he can do so at a price of twelve and a half rupees, but not at fifteen rupees. This is because murabahah is based on transparency and avoiding even the suspicion of cheating (shubhah khiyanah). In the scenario, the cloth originally cost ten rupees, and the mudarib made a profit of five rupees? Actually the text says: if the cloth cost the rabb al-mal twelve and a half, he can do murabahah on that. But later explanation says: the rabb al-mal wants to sell it at fifteen, but because of suspicion, he reduces the profit. The reasoning proceeds: In mudarabah, if some profit has been made, selling between the mudarib and rabb al-mal is unanimously allowed. If no profit, Imam Zufar deems it invalid while Imam Abu Hanifa allows it. Imam Zufar's evidence: A sale requires exchange of property between two distinct parties. Here, since the cloth and the price both belong to the rabb al-mal in essence, no real sale occurs. Imam Abu Hanifa's counter-argument: When the rabb al-mal gave the capital to the mudarib, his authority (wilayat tasarruf) over that capital ceased. The sale to him restores that authority, so the sale achieves its purpose of transferring authority. However, due to Imam Zufar's reasoning, a shadow of suspicion remains. Therefore, to preserve the integrity of murabahah, the rabb al-mal cannot claim the full profit; instead, he reduces the price by the amount of profit that corresponds to his own share (two and a half rupees). The mufta bihi position is that the sale between mudarib and rabb al-mal is valid, and the murabahah price should be adjusted to avoid suspicion. Hence the ruling: the rabb al-mal can sell on murabahah at twelve and a half, stating the cost to be twelve and a half, but cannot claim the full fifteen.

Key Terms
مرابحہ (murabahah): A sale in which the seller discloses the cost and profit margin to the buyer.
مضاربت (mudarabah): A partnership in which one party provides capital (rabb al-mal) and the other provides labor (mudarib) and profit is shared according to agreement.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The capital provider in a mudarabah contract.
مضارب (mudarib): The working partner in mudarabah who manages the capital.
خیانت (khiyanah): Cheating or breach of trust.
شبہ خیانت (shubhah khiyanah): Suspicion of cheating that must be avoided in murabahah sales.
ولایت تصرف (wilayat tasarruf): Legal authority to dispose of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, on what price can the rabb al-mal sell the cloth on murabahah after buying it back from the mudarib?
A) 15 rupees
B) 12.5 rupees
C) 10 rupees
D) 7.5 rupees

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, even when a sale is valid, the murabahah price must be adjusted to eliminate any suspicion of cheating arising from the seller's own interest in the transaction.

Disclosure of Defects in Murabahah: The Hanafi Distinction Between Attributes and Essence
Ruling on disclosure when selling a defective slave-girl on murabahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a seller must disclose a defect acquired after purchase when selling on murabahah, and apply the distinction between attributes (awsaf) and essence (dhat) to determine disclosure requirements.

Core Idea
Price is paid for the essence, not attributes; thus, loss of an attribute does not require disclosure in murabahah.

This passage explores when a buyer who acquired a sound slave-girl and later discovered she became defective (e.g., lost an eye or was no longer virgin) can resell her on murabahah without disclosing the defect. The Hanafi school, led by Imam Abu Hanifa, makes a crucial distinction: defects that affect only attributes do not require disclosure, while loss of a part (juz') does. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is selling a slave-girl on murabahah after she became defective (one-eyed or thayyib after intercourse). The ruling is that the seller may sell without disclosing these defects.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is that attributes (awsaf) are subordinate to the essence (dhat); price is paid for the essence, not for attributes. Evidence: if the slave-girl dies before delivery, no price is refunded; similarly, the benefits of intercourse (manafi' al-bud') are not compensable by price.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The legal link: since the defect is merely an attribute, the seller has not retained any part of the price in his possession, so he may sell at the full original cost without disclosure.
4
Note the exception: loss of virginity
If the slave-girl was a virgin and the buyer had intercourse, disclosure is required because the hymen is considered a part (juz') of her, and the buyer has retained that part. Therefore, the price must be reduced accordingly.
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf (in one narration) and Imam Shafi'i hold that even attribute defects must be disclosed. The Hanafi response distinguishes between parts (which reduce price) and attributes (which do not). The mufta bihi position is Imam Abu Hanifa's view that no disclosure is needed for attribute defects.

باندی خریدی ہو کانی ہوگئی یا ولی کی اور وہ شیبہ ہوگئی تو کتنے پر مرابحہ بیچ سکتا ہے؟
قال ومن اشترى جارية فاعورت او وطيها وهى ثيب يبيعها مرابحة ولا يبين لانه لم يحتبس عنده شئى يقابله الثمن لان الاوصاف تابعة لايقابلها الثمن ولهذ الوفتات قبل التسليم لا يسقط شئى من الثمن وكذا منافع البضع لا يقبلها الثمن والمسالة فيما اذالم ينقصها الوطى وعن ابى يوسف فى الفصل الاول انه لا يبيع من
